Report on the results of parallel checks on value added tax management between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The material submitted informs the progress and results of parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's Supervisory Authority, which focused on the field of value added tax management and the use of the VIES information system (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) on value added tax).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so the revenue from value added tax affects not only the national budgets of both countries, but also the European Union budget as a whole.
Parallel control actions focused mainly on the control of the tax administrators procedure when checking the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions between Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system enabled an electronic exchange of information on the registration of value added tax payers in individual Member States of the European Union and on commercial transactions carried out by these payers.
The inconsistency between VIES data and the data in the value added tax return submitted by the payer should draw the attention of the tax manager to suspicious cases and allow tax evasion to be detected or. scams.
The contribution of parallel checks carried out consisted not only in exchange of information on the financial or financial procedure. the tax authorities in the management of value added tax, but especially in the verification of the use of VIES in checking the application of value added tax exemption in intracommunitary transactions.
The knowledge gained during the implementation of parallel checks is a benefit for the development of cooperation between them and will be used in carrying out further parallel checks in cooperation with the control institutions of Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel Value Added Tax Administration checks for the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of inspection: (CZ) Value added tax management, (SK) Control of the tax authority's procedure for the management, control and enforcement of value added tax and performance of tasks within the VIES system to exchange information between EU Member States
The Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ, the Czech Republic ′′) and the Slovak Republic's Najvyšší SR (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ SR ′′) concluded a cooperation agreement in the control activity on 12. August 2005
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the parallel control events ′′ Value added tax management ′′ included in the plan of control activity NKÚ, Czech Republic for 2005 under no. 05/19 and ′′ Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the management, control and enforcement of tax on added value and full of tasks within the VIES system on the exchange of information mediated by the Member Landscapes. ", included in the control plan of the NKÚ SR under No. 22/2005.
The parallel control actions performed were the character of coordinated checks.
The result of the joint coordinated inspection was processed within the meaning of the European Implementing Regulation No. 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information within the scope of the contract concluded and drawing up a joint final report on the result of parallel checks.
The purpose of a coordinated inspection was to verify selected delivery and acquisition cases in suspicious commercial transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the ′′ SR ′′).
Both parties contractually committed to each other to provide information from public sources, VIES electronic system (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on accepted and sent requests to verify commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and SR.
The checks were carried out parallel between June and December 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by the department of the state budget and territorial unions of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The Ministry of Finance and 12 financial authorities were controlled by the Ministry of Finance and 12 financial authorities: the IRS in Mladá Boleslav, the Finance Office in Kolín, the Finance Office in Teplice, the Finance Office in Karlovy Vary, the Finance Office in Tábor, the Finance Office in Brno III, the Financial Office in Znojmo, the Financial Office in Znojmo Office in Zlín, Finance office in Šumperku, Ostrava I, Finance office for Prague 7 and the Financial Office for Prague 9.
The inspection in the territory of the SR was carried out by the financial and tax section of the NKÚ SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 9 selected tax offices: Bratislava I tax office, Komárno tax office, Trenčín tax office, Prievidza tax office, Tax office Elected, Dolný Kubín tax office, Košice II tax office, Košice V tax office and Michalovka tax office.
Objective of checks:
The aim of parallel control actions was to examine the progress of financial and / or financial. tax authorities in the management of value added tax (VAT) after the inclusion of the Czech Republic and the SR into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as the EU) and verify the use of the VIES electronic information system, especially when checking the application of the VAT exemption claim I'm sorry.
The controlled period of coordinated inspection was the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions In EU Member States, an electronic VIES system is in place, allowing tax administrators to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and in the country of destination it allows the customer to check whether the acquired goods have been properly admitted and taxed.
VIES system is not centralized within the EU, each Member State is developing its own system.
The inspection revealed different variations of national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and SR in the following areas:
Summary reports indicate the values of delivery of goods to other EU Member States, the values of services provided are not included in the summary reports.
Data from summary reports submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the financial authorities where they compare with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States given in VAT tax returns.
The financial authorities transmit data from summary reports to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In SR, data from summary reports submitted by Slovak tax payers are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the SR Tax Directorate (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers show the value of supplying goods and the value of providing services to other EU Member States on separate lines of tax returns for VAT, which allows comparing the values given in the summary reports with the value of the supply of goods according to VAT tax returns and identifying their differences.
In the SR, the values of the goods supplied and services provided to other EU Member States are reported summarily on the common line of VAT return.
As a result, the SR system does not automatically identify the differences between the value of the supply of goods according to VAT returns and summary reports.
Separate reporting of the value of supplies of goods in VAT tax returns allows you to use the results of comparison of data when checking the exemption of goods to the EU from VAT.
The data delivered from summary reports submitted by payers in other EU Member States are processed into CLO and compared with the value of acquisition of goods given by the payer from the Czech Republic or. SR in VAT tax returns.
In SR, these data are sent to tax authorities and tax administrators will decide which cases of differences will check.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) will determine which quantified differences between the value of delivery and acquisition of goods must be checked by the tax administrators and transmit a list of such cases to the local authorities.
This ensures that the most significant variations will be verified whether VAT has been granted to the right amount of the goods.
The inspection further highlighted some problems in the VAT management system complications caused by different reporting of intracommunitary transactions (i.e. delivery and acquisition of goods made by payers from different EU Member States):
Summary reports are submitted in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
A shortening of the period for which summary reports are submitted to one month, together with a shortening of the deadline for processing them, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
Tax administrators could thus verify more effectively whether VAT was awarded to the correct amount of intracommunitary acquisitions.
At the same time, filing tax returns and summary reports for the same tax period (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer reported the same value of the delivery of goods to the EU in the summary report and VAT return.
Differences between the values of supply of goods declared by EU payers and the values of acquisition of goods declared by the payers from the Czech Republic or. SR was caused by MJ. different reporting of intracommunitary supply and acquisition data in individual EU Member States.
For example, it was the introduction of advances received into summary reports, or the reporting of intracommunitary deliveries in a summary report of the supplier in a different quarter than intracommunitary acquisitions in the tax return to the customer's VAT.
Unification of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlined monitoring activity of the Member State s' tax administrations.
The cooperation of NKU, Czech Republic and NKU SR was also focused on the examination of selected intracommunitary transactions between the two states.
A total of 40 cases of commercial transactions between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined together, where there were doubts about their effectiveness or. suspicion of tax evasion on VAT.
NKÚ, Czech Republic and NKÚ SR found out, among others. the following facts:
tax entities have reported in their VAT tax returns for the purpose of unauthorized tax deduction of excessive VAT transactions, which were not actually implemented;
tax operators showed intracommunitary delivery within the carousel shops, which caused a deliberate reduction in the value of deliveries to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their tax returns for VAT and summary reports intracommunitary supply of VAT exempt goods to buyers who were so-called. ' lost company s' and tax on goods acquired;
suppliers carried out an intracommunitary supply of goods exempted from VAT for tax entities not registered in another Member State.
In these cases the VAT supply should not have been exempted and should have been taxed in the country of the supplier;
suppliers reported intracommunitary delivery at higher value in their VAT tax returns than the intracommunitary acquisition, in some cases VAT was incorrect.
The knowledge gained in the control action showed that VIES provides tax administrators with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracommunitary transactions.
Tax administrators should pay increased attention especially to the thorough examination of the differences between VAT payers and VIES data and the use of all information in tax proceedings.
The issue of value added tax after the Czech Republic and SR accession to the EU
Value added tax
On June 1., 2004, Czech Republic and SR became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on movement of goods within the EU were abolished.
The VAT manager was the relevant financial or financial or financial administrator until 30. June 4. tax office, except for goods importation and occasional bus transport in the country where the tax manager was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new law No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No., 235/2004 Coll."), resp. Act No. 222/2004 Z. z., on value added tax (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No., 222/2004 Z. from.") VAT administration has passed on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU Member States from customs offices to financial and responses. tax authorities.
Delivery of goods in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as the owner.
Delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the supply of goods actually shipped or transported to another EU Member State.
According to the provisions of Section 64 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. this is an exempted taxable operation with the right to deduct VAT when the goods are delivered to a VAT registered person in another EU Member State.
For the supply of goods, the SR is under the provisions of Section 8 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. considers the supply of material property, where the property rights change.
The transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the country to another Member State shall be considered to be the supply of goods, where such goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on their behalf to another Member State for the purposes of their business.
According to the provisions of Section 43 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. is the delivery of goods from the country to another Member State exempted from VAT if the customer is a VAT person in another Member State.
The acquisition of goods from another EU Member State is in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 16 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose of goods dispatched or transported by the customer by a VAT registered person in another EU Member State.
Czech payer purchases goods at a price without VAT and its duty is to award VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 25 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., if the conditions set out in Section 73 of this Act are fulfilled, he is entitled to VAT deduction.
By purchasing goods in the country from another EU Member State, the SR is in accordance with Section 11 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. means the acquisition of the right to dispose of movable material property dispatched or transported by the purchaser by the supplier or by the customer or on their account to the domestic country from another Member State.
Tax liability in SR arises when acquiring goods in the country from another Member State under Section 20 of Law No. 222/2004 Z.z.
The payer may, according to the provisions of Section 49 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. deduct VAT if the tax is applied by it on the acquisition of goods in the country from another Member State according to the provisions of §§ 11 and 11 a of this law.
Trilateral trade is understood according to the provisions of Section 17 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., resp. Section 45 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. trade between three VAT registered persons in three different EU Member States, where the subject of trade is the supply of the same goods between these three persons.
Intracommunitary transactions means the supply and acquisition of goods between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volume of intracommunitary transactions between the Czech Republic and SR are shown in the following table.
VIES system
In order to control the application of the VAT exemption claim on intra-communitarian goods supply, a VAT information exchange system has been established within the EU.
This includes the VIES electronic system, which allows tax administrators of EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and, on the contrary, whether the acquaintant admitted and taxed the goods acquired.
VIES information system is not centralized within the EU.
Each Member State is developing its own VIES system.
National systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU common communication network called. CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was linked to an automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as ′′ ADIS ′′), in SR with application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as ′′ APV DIS ′′).
These systems are used by financial and resp. tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in tax and fees management.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU member country receives information on tax entities that without this cooperation it would not be able to obtain on its own.
The main goal of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
According to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 Each Member State shall establish a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the management of VAT, within the internal organisational structure, called: CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance - Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in VAT Management (hereinafter referred to as ′′ MF CLO ′′ was established).
The CLO function in SR is performed by the SR Tax Directorate, the department of international administrative cooperation (DR CLO).
These departments, including. communicate with EU foreign administrations especially in the area of information exchange within the VIES system, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax checks, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as 'VAT') persons registered in VAT other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to verify a certain intracommunitary transaction or obtain further information related to a particular tax entity, they send financial or responsive information. tax authorities via MF CLO or DR CLO to the EU for information request.
Through these applications, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use for the correct determination of VAT.
Requests for information are sent among the CLO of EU Member States mostly in electronic form using the standardized SCAC form.

The operator of this free zone was listed on the invoices as the recipient of the goods.

The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the free zone space on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator launched tax checks on individual taxation periods 2004 and 2005. with the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel shops.
Verification of the transactions carried out was requested by Czech local tax administrators via several SCAC forms.
Individual replies gradually created a picture of shops and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from SR and Czech Republic in carousel shops.
NKÚ, Czech Republic, in cooperation with the NKÚ SR, found that in these business relationships, there was a gradual decrease in the value of goods.
The SR tax directorate concluded on the basis of the information obtained that in this case of carousel trade it is free price creation (i.e. imports of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between importer and exporter) which is not a violation of the VAT law in SR.
The current legislation cannot prevent excessive VAT deduction to export companies since they meet all the conditions of the VAT exemption law.

The course of the inspection action
As part of the preparation of parallel control events, a coordination meeting of representatives of NKU, Czech Republic with representatives of NKU SR took place in the first half of July 2005
Participants of this meeting acquainted with VAT legislation in both states and the integration of the VIES electronic system into national databases.
The outcome of the negotiations was a specification of the scope of cooperation and the conditions for the selection of control samples.
The two parties agreed that cooperation will focus on the following areas: (a) validation and correctness of VAT registered persons in the Czech Republic or. SR during intracommunitary delivery; (b) verification of data on intracommunitary acquisitions specified in DAP payer in Czech Republic using information from summary reports (SH) of SR payers contained in VIES system and vice versa; (c) exchange of information between tax administrations in Czech Republic and in SR about business transactions.
It was also agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out following the volume of intracommunitary supplies between the Czech Republic and SR and according to the number of applications for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the SR via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intracommunitary transactions
The procedure for processing information by tax administrations of the Czech Republic and SR during intra-communitarian delivery and acquisition of goods shows the following scheme.
5.1.1 Intracommunitary delivery
If a VAT payer makes an intracommunitary delivery, he / she is obliged to submit SH by the 25. th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic presents in SH summary information about supplies of goods to another EU Member State exempted from VAT for previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to state the value of goods exempted and delivered from the country to other EU Member States during the calendar quarter period.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always available in Czech or Czech. in Slovak currency broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their tax ID, under which they were registered in their country.
Service data are not included in SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds out that he has reported false data in SH, he is obliged to submit subsequent SH.
If the SR payer finds that the data provided in SH were incomplete or incorrect, he will submit a correct SH before the expiry of the deadline for submission of SH, after expiry of this period he is obliged to submit additional SH.
VIES system allows exchange of VAT registration data for VAT registered in EU Member States.
Payers from Czech Republic or. The SR can verify whether the customer's VAT is registered in a given EU Member State.
The data from the SH submitted are on MF CLO or. DR CLO by VIES system grouped according to individual customer's tax.
A cumulative value of all deliveries for each customer's tax and a code of the way they are filling from all their Czech or Czechs. Slovak suppliers, so-called. L1QD files.
Data from L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intracommunitary fulfilments between Czech Republic and SR (from L1QD files) is shown in the following table.
If the VIES system in another Member State detects erroneous customer's tax ID in the sent L1QD files, it will generate the so-called. O _ MCTL report containing all erroneous VAT with error type.
This message is then sent to MF CLO or. DR CLO.
The O _ MCTL report can contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect VAT ID, VAT is not registered in a given state or has never been assigned, the customer with a certain VAT number was not a VAT payer in a given quarter, the VAT registration of the customer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, MF CLO transmits data from received reports O _ MCTL to the financial authorities.
If an EU payer's malfunctioning tax ID is used in one of the sh or subsequent SH lines, the ADIS system is generated by the ADIS system. ′′ Notice of doubt to VAT ID ".
The IRS will verify whether the delivery of the payer registered for VAT in another EU Member State has actually occurred and will record the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, the DR CLO in VIES processes all O _ MCTL reports and sends them electronically to the local tax authorities together with identification of tax payers who have reported the wrong ID in their SH.
The tax authorities subsequently invite the payer to submit additional SH and to provide valid VATs or VATs. The tax office will check the delivery of goods with the relevant payer when reporting an invalid VAT in the SH filed.

When reporting intracommunitary transactions between the Czech Republic and the SR, Czech VAT payers reported on average less bad tax than SR payers.
When checking the activities of financial or financials tax authorities found that VIES did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of tax payer s' VAT registrations in all cases.
For example.:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax body in the 4. th quarter of 2004, the report O _ MCTL was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer registration in this quarter.
The investigation established that the registration ended until 1. August 2005;
- NKÚ SR further found that 6 tax entities filed a SH, which reported the wrong ID, but the O _ MCTL reports did not contain this ID.
In SR the filed SH will be converted into an electronic form at the tax authorities and the data from them to DR CLO.
Following subsequent processing of this data in VIES system, DR CLO will send the so-called tax authorities to the relevant tax authorities. breakdowns of errors in SH filed by tax entities for the respective quarter.

In the Czech Republic, the value of intracommunitary deliveries given by the payer in the relevant DAP lines is compared with the value of intracommunitary delivery specified by this payer in quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should check the differences, eliminate any inconclusiveness and use the data obtained when determining the tax liability.
NKU, Czech Republic found that controlled financial authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values shown in SH and DAP was 537 thousand in these cases...
Since the 3. th quarter of 2004, the ADIS system enabled the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values given in SH and DAP of up to 0,5 % of the total value of intracommunitary delivery according to SH as a conformity and set it in ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intracommunitary delivery in one quarter, 0,5 % of the value is an insignificant amount, therefore tax administrators should not set SH and DAP conformity without clarifying the causes of differences.
For example: the tax administrator set a match without verification in case of difference in values of 1 thousand...
Verification of differences in the Czech Republic and SR was complicated by the fact that SH was served by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
Tax administrators could not compare the intracommunitary supply values given in these DAP with the monthly taxation period at the time of DAP for the first two months of the calendar quarter.
In these cases, tax administrators learned about any non-compliance of data in DAP and SH only when tax liability or excessive deduction of VAT was collected, or. Returned.
5.1.2 Intracommunitary acquisition
The VIES system provides inter alia information on the values of intracommunitary transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Buy goods in Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, data from SH submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered by L2QD) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing the data are converted by the minimum and maximum daily currency rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the value of the acquisition given by the Czech payers in DAP for the respective quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods declared by the payer in DAP should be within the minimum and maximum conversion values L1QD (L1min and L1max values).
If the value reported in DAP is lower than the L1min value, the so-called is generated for the payer with the most significant irregularities. verification order.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax entities and are transmitted to local competent financial authorities, which must be investigated by the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders for controlled financial authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the following table.
NKÚ, Czech Republic found that the inspected financial authorities did not verify irregularities in the values of intracommunitary acquisitions, which were highlighted by delivered verification orders.
The total difference between the values shown in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers was at least 148 thousand in these cases...
NKÚ, Czech Republic selected 533 tax entities files for which controlled financial authorities received a verification order from MF CLO.
The following common causes of differences between the values given in the DAP of the customer and the supplier's SH: on the side of the customer (Czech payer) in 263 cases, the customer did not indicate the acquisition of goods in proper DAP, in 93 cases the payer admitted the acquisition of goods in another taxation the period before he was entitled to tax, in 6 cases the customer stated the value of the goods acquired in the wrong DAP line, on the part of the supplier (EU payer) in 88 cases, EU payers included the values of the services provided to Czech in their SH payers, of which in 54 cases it was a payer from SR, in 39 cases the suppliers included the delivery of goods in a different tax period from the Czech Republic to their DAP, in 22 cases the suppliers reported incorrect ID in SH Czech payer, in 16 cases, suppliers reported incorrect values of delivery of goods in SH, in 12 cases suppliers included the value of goods delivered to the Czech Republic before 1. 5. 2004, in 5 cases suppliers included in the Czech Republic SH value of advances received.
The most commonly misconception of the value of the services provided in SH was on the side of the SR payers.
54 such cases were identified in the inspected financial authorities.
For example: when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference of 10 thousand. Kč was created by introducing the Slovak payer to SH for the 1. th quarter of 2005 services (construction work and delivery of goods including assembly in the Czech Republic).
Another reason for differences was to include the values of advances received in SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers announced advances received from Czech payers in SH, resulting in a generated order to verify the difference of 3 thousand...
Orders for verification of goods purchased are generated only once in one quarter.
In cases where the SH data changes in EU Member States such as: change of customer of goods in the Czech Republic or increased value of delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since the VIES system does not automatically alert these changes, the local competent tax manager of the goods purchaser without any other impulse about facts applicable to the correct determination of the tax liability of the goods acquired and there is a strong probability of tax evasion on VAT.
By checking NKU, the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
Slovak payer stated in SH for the 2. th quarter of 2004 the value of delivery of goods for a Czech payer of 1 thousand. Sk.
On June 1., 2005, the tax office sent a request for information to the Czech payer to SR, because the Czech payer admitted the acquisition of goods only 425 thousand...
Based on the tax procedure, the Slovak payer filed an additional SH on 3. 1., in which he corrected data on the supply of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the supply for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand. Sk and by increasing the value of the supplied goods for another Czech payer from 194 thousand. Sk to 160 1 thousand. Sk.
Four Slovak payers announced intracommunitary delivery to the Czech Republic for the 2. th quarter of 2004 240 thousand. Sk (i.e. 8 183 thousand..).
However, Czech buyers did not show intracommunitary acquisition in DAP.
Based on international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer, which was not listed in SH by Slovak payers.
During the 1. th quarter of 2005 Slovak payers increased the value of intracommunitary delivery for this Czech payer by 10 thousand in additional SH regarding the 2. th quarter of 2004 Sk.
Due to the above facts, the local tax manager in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in the DAP for the 2. th quarter of 2004, although the real customer failed to fulfil the obligation to admit intracommunitary acquisition for this quarter.
NKÚ Czech Republic found that based on international exchange of information between tax administrations, VAT was additional for the tax period 5 and 6/2004 of 3 thousand. Kč and for the 3. th quarter 2004 of 3 305 thousand. Kč from goods purchased during these periods.
From the above, it is evident that tax administrators had to check not only the differences caused by the errors of the DAP by the purchaser, but also the differences caused by different reporting of intracommunitary supply and acquisition data in individual EU Member States.
Unification of the conditions for reporting such data would lead to a streamline of the control activities of tax administrators.
Buy goods in SR
In the SR, the APV DIS system allows comparison of the value of goods acquired through the VIES system from other EU Member States with the data contained in the DAP by Slovak customers.
The method by which data are compared is called the ′′ MIN-MAX Method ".
Using this method, a conversion of the value of delivery of goods specified in SH payers from other EU Member States at the minimum and maximum exchange rate for the relevant quarter.
There will be an interval of MIN-MAX, which is used for comparing with the values of acquisition of goods specified in DAP by Slovak payers.
DR CLO will send tax administrators information on intracommunitary acquisitions values listed in DAP and EU delivery values in VIES.
The tax administrator will decide for which VAT registered persons will be tested, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
Based on data provided by the DR CLO, the NKÚ SR selected 57 writings of Slovak goods from the inspected tax authorities, of which 25 payers acquired goods from the Czech Republic, where the highest differences between acquisitions obtained from VIES and values were found declared in DAP.
The controlled NKÚ SR inspection confirmed that the tax administrators did not thoroughly check the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the accuracy of the data contained in the DAP of Slovak customers.
NKÚ SR asked tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations with specific tax entities as part of the inspection.
During the NKÚ SR inspection at tax authorities, 31 local investigation was terminated.

5.2 International exchange of information level L3
The exchange of information at úrovni level is initiated by local tax administrators who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as ′′ ŽOI ′′) or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as ′′ SPI ′′) related to a tax entity or transaction via MF CLO or via MF.
DR CLO to another EU member country. The goal of ŽOI is for example demonstration of the implementation of the transaction within intracommunitary transactions, certain ID, etc.
In the case of SPI, it is a communication of information relevant to tax administrators in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum deadline for the response to the ŽOI has been set in Article () of the 8 of this regulation for 3 months.
The conditions for admissibility of applications are regulated by the Commission Decision of the European Communities of 15. 11. 2004 stipulating that unless the participating States agree otherwise, the ŽOI must relate to commercial transactions worth at least EUR 1 500 without VAT.
If the JOI concerns a commercial transaction of less than EUR 15 000 without VAT, the requested authority may refuse to respond with regard to its load.
The procedure for handling of the ŽOI received by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the indoor time limits set for processing at individual organizational levels, shows the following scheme.
In the SR, the deadline for the handling of the ŽOI by the tax authorities was internally set for 2 months so that the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 2 can be observed. 1798/2003.
The MF CLO received ŽOI and SPI from SR from 1. 5. 5. to 30. 30. 2005 2005 ŽOI and 3
Out of 29 accepted ŽOI were 26 (i.e. 89,7 %) finished within the specified time limit of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10,3 % were done after this deadline.
During the same period, DR CLO received a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI from the Czech Republic.
Out of the 71 adopted ŽOI were 64 (i.e. 90,1 %) finished within the specified deadline of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7,0 %) was finished after this period (in the other 2 cases, it was not possible to determine the deadline of the materials transmitted).

Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No has been examined. 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and further use of VIES system to exchange information between EU Member States, especially in checking the application of the VAT exemption claim.
International cooperation enabled the selected intracommunitary transactions between VAT payers from Czech Republic and SR.
The examination of the selected transactions found that, based on international exchange of information, tax administrations of both countries revealed cases of companies carrying out fictional intracommunitary commercial transactions to obtain excessive VAT deductions and also cases where the buyers did not pay VAT on the goods received at the correct amount.
The inspection further identified differences in the processing and use of VIES data by tax administrations of both countries.
The inspection also highlighted problems caused by different reporting of data on intracommunitary supply and acquisition of goods in individual EU Member States.
Unification of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlined monitoring activity of the Member State s' tax administrations.
By checking the financial or financial procedure tax authorities in the management of VAT and the use of VIES system have been found to be financial or. the tax authorities did not use sufficiently all VIES options and relevant legal permissions.
It was also found that VIES did not provide up-to-date information on goods supply and validity of VAT registration in all cases.
NKÚ SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with data processed after the completion of the inspection.
From the comparison of these data it was apparent that the check of the NKÚ SR had an impact not only on the reduction in the number of SH with the wrongly mentioned ID, but also on the reduction of the number of unmixed errors in SH.
In case of irregularities in reported NKÚ SR data, the tax authorities asked for local investigations or tax checks to be carried out.
NKU, Czech Republic did not have such an option within the valid legislation in the Czech Republic.
The knowledge gained by the control actions showed that VIES provided tax administrators with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-communitarian transactions.
Since there is still room for tax evasion in this area, increased attention should be given to intracommunitary transactions when managing VAT.
Communicating
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the chairman of the Slovak Supervisory Authority.
Parallel control of the value added tax and excise duty management between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material provides an overview of the progress and results of parallel control actions carried out by the High Supervisory Authority and the Slovak Republic's Supervisory Authority, which focused on the field of administration given from added value and excise duties.
Cooperation between the top supervisory authorities of both countries was carried out under a cooperation agreement in control activity concluded in February 2004.
The topic of parallel control actions has been selected considering the fact that indirect taxes are significantly involved in the revenue of the state budget of both countries.
The design of value added tax, allowing refund of excessive deduction, provides room for tax fraud or tax fraud. Escape.
High excise duty rates, especially for tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, make a high profit for those who escape taxation by the illegal sale of these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue in a comprehensive way across the European Union, the VAT Working Group has been created by the highest inspection institutions of the Member States of the European Union, which also includes the highest control offices of both countries.
The greatest contribution of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in exchange of experience, but especially in a common effort to identify the problem areas of indirect tax management in order to reduce space for tax evasion.
Experience gained and knowledge will be used in the planned checks of indirect taxes, mainly focused on the involvement of tax administrators of both states in the VIES system, allowing the movement of goods between Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of value added tax and excise duty control for the years 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duty
(SK) Control of the procedure of the tax administrator in the management, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On June 11.2., 2004, a cooperation agreement in the control activity between the Supreme Supervisory Authority (hereinafter referred to as ' NKÚ ') and the Slovak Republic's Supervisory Authority (hereinafter referred to as ' NKÚ SR ') was concluded. The subject of the agreement was cooperation in the parallel control actions carried out ' Value added tax and excise duty ", included in the NKÚ control activity plan for 2004 under no. 04/07 and ′′ Control of the procedure of the administrator dan when managing, checking and enforcement of tax on added value and consumption taxes ", included in the inspection plan NKÚ SR under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted of exchange of information within the scope established by the contract concluded and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
Both parties committed in the contract to provide information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from the files of tax entities led by the Czech Republic and tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the Contracting Parties could not obtain when checking the application of the value added tax and excise taxes on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the competent State.
The checks were carried out parallel between January and August 2004.
In the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) the inspection was carried out by the state budget and territorial unions of South Bohemia, northeast Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The inspected persons were the Directorate-General of Customs and 12 selected financial authorities: The Finance Office for Prague 1, the Finance Office for Prague 3, the Financial Office in Českých Budějovicích, the Financial Office in Frýdku-Místek, the Finance Office in Hodonin, the Finance Office in Hodonín in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Kroměříži, the Financial Office in Písek, the Financial Office in Rožnově pod Radhostem, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Velkém Meziříčí.
The inspection in the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as ′′ SR ′′) was carried out by the Section of the Tax and Customs Administration of the NKÚ SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 10 tax offices:
Bratislava tax office for selected tax entities, Bratislava III tax office, Trnava tax office, Pooh-breeding tax office, Banská Bystrica I tax office, Liptovský Nicholas tax office, Žilina I tax office, Žilina II tax office, Košice I tax office and Tax office Košice IV office.
Objective of inspection
The aim of the control actions was to examine the fulfilment of financial and / or financial duties. tax offices and customs offices in the management of value added tax and excise duties with a focus on collecting these taxes on import and export of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the SR Customs database and their subsequent verification in tax returns on the relevant financial or financial returns. tax authorities.
The controlled period was 2002 and 2003.
2. Recap of inspection results
2.1. General evaluation of the control activity
As part of the international cooperation of the NKÚ SR from the Czech Customs database, the NKÚ SR handed over 22 items of uniform customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as ′′ JCD ′′) on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and SR and on the contrary, the NKÚ SR handed over to NKÚ from the Customs database SR 30 221 JCD items.
A comparison of the listed JCD items from the Czech Customs database and the SR Customs database was made.
Out of 5 selected JCD items from the Czech Customs database, a total of 43 % of the related JCD items were assigned.
Out of 12 selected JCD items from the SR Customs database, a total of 26 % of JCD related items were assigned.
Based on the unassigned JCD items, he was on financial or. the tax offices selected the tax agency files for which imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and SR.
Based on the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and SR and financial or. tax authorities have been verified in the territory of the second state that reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and SR were reported.
NKÚ and NKÚ SR performed a joint pilot inspection at the border customs crossing of Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, where both interested parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and SR.
The inspection did not detect deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods made in 2002.
International cooperation enabled the examination of commercial transactions between trading partners from both States and highlighted the shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of the results of the inspection
In the field of international cooperation, the NKÚ and NKÚ SR control focused on imports and exports of spirits and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, or other types of goods.
Based on the inspection of tax entities files on selected financial and / or the NKÚ tax authorities asked for verification of exports of goods declared at 40 JCD total statistical value of CZK 15 and NKÚ SR for export verification in statistical value of 56 989 Sk.
NKÚ and NKÚ SR found out the following facts among other things:
- commercial transactions were not declared on both sides in the same way, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the Czech Republic customs database and the customs database of the SR,
- error in entering data into customs databases prevented certain imports from identifying or identifying. exports,
- some exports from the Czech Republic have not been demonstrated by adequate imports into SR.
In these cases, there is reason to suspect fictional exports of goods for the purpose of unauthorized application of value added tax deductions,
- tax agencies did not comply with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- in the activities of financial or financials tax offices were identified in the management of value added tax and excise duty and in their synergy with customs authorities.
In the field of value added tax and excise duty, attention will continue to be needed to be paid to international trade in order to minimize tax evasion effectively.
The improvement of tax administrators's activity in the performance of value added tax administration is important.
The basis of effective control of excise duties is the control of documents circulation, systematic physical inspection of goods and exchange of information with each other when goods are imported and exported.
3. Description of value added tax and excise duty status
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as 'VAT') was collected by financial and / or financial. tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out in the country and customs offices on importation of goods.
The tax revenue was for financial or financial income the tax authorities are given the difference between chosen own tax liability and excessive VAT deductions refunded.
VAT revenue at customs offices was given the amount of tax collected by them.
The tax collected by the customs authorities, in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, reflected in the tax deductions applied to financial and / or financial tax. tax authorities.
Most financial or financial ones tax authorities exceeded excessive VAT deductions above the tax liability.
VAT is one of the key taxes in terms of state budget revenue, since it participated in the tax revenue of the Czech Republic's budget in 2003 and about 42 % in the tax revenue of the state budget of the Czech Republic.
Total VAT collection in the Czech Republic reached 162,9 billion in 2003..
In 2003, the financial and customs authorities collected a total of 394,3 billion for VAT. Kč and excessive VAT refunds were totaled 231,4 billion...
Total VAT recovery in SR amounted to 83,8 billion in 2003 Sk.
In 2003 tax and customs authorities collected 187,0 billion for VAT. Sk and excessive VAT refunds amounted to a total of 103,2 billion. Sk.
Excise taxes
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as ′′ SpD ′′) was carried out by the relevant financial and / or financial respectively tax authorities and imports of products subject to SpD by customs authorities.
The share of SpD in the tax revenue of the state budget in the Czech Republic was around 16 % in 2003 and in SR about 19 %.
The total SpD collection selected in the Czech Republic by the financial and customs offices in 2003 was 85,6 billion. Kč and in SR it reached 38,0 billion. Sk.
4. The course of the inspection action
Cooperation between NKÚ and NKÚ SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR, in the second stage the results of this comparison were used in mutual verification of the realization of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the SR and during checks carried out in the territory of both states.
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel VAT and SpD checks was presented at a working meeting of representatives of NKÚ and NKÚ SR in April 2003.
In November 2003 there was a coordination meeting, including him. selection of commodities agreed - types of goods that posed a significant risk in compliance with customs and tax rules: - alcohol and spirit drinks, customs tariff items No 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, customs tariff items No. 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff items and subheadings No. 8471 and 30 8473, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff subheadings No. 8525 91 20, 8525 99 20, 8529 90 40.
The two parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out: (a) from unassigned items found by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the SR, (b) from entities making imports and exports regularly or on a single basis in large volume, (c) based on findings from checks carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR
In the first stage, a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities tested for the month of October 2002 tested the mechanism for the mutual allocation of JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR.
Subsequently, part of the exports from the Czech Republic was compared with imports into SR for 2002 and on the contrary, for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:

JCD items from customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR were mutually assigned based on the agreement of individual paragraphs of JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration plate of car transporting cargo, date of crossing state border, customs tariff item, etc.).
The results of the comparison are shown in the following tables and charts.
Mutual attribution of individual imports and exports made it difficult, among others. the fact that commercial transactions were not declared on both sides in the same way.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic, declared on one export JCD, were declared on multiple import JCD in the territory of SR, or export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that affected the success rate of attribution were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of the corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples on controlled financial or. tax authorities.
Some tax entities that made imports or imports were selected prioritized. exports between the Czech Republic and the SR, which have failed to identify in both databases.
In addition, some tax entities with import data were selected to verify the commercial operations reported in VAT tax returns. exports between Czech Republic and SR found in both databases.
4.3. Pilot inspection at border customs crossing Drietoma Hrozenkov-Drietoma
The border customs crossing for pilot control was selected based on a joint analysis of unassigned JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR.
Based on a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the SR, the use of control sheets was introduced at border customs crossings between the Czech Republic and SR from 1.6.1998
The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion as far as possible, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transporting goods of commercial character in the customs area and to create conditions for comparing customs records with each other.
Joint pilot inspection was carried out from 8. 3. to 2004 26. 3. and focused on the inspection of this customs control system.
Procedure for the use of checksheets at the border customs crossing of Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma:
1) Consideration of the vehicle, issue of the inspection certificate and handing it over to the driver.
2) Vehicle weaning in the marked sector in the parking lot.
Customs discussion in the clearance hall of the police of the Czech Republic, police of the SR, Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, Customs Administration of the SR.
Check-in was confirmed by individual components with a stamp on the check sheet.
3) Installation of the vehicle into the physical inspection area.
Presentation of the check sheet, JCD or other documents to the Customs Administration worker - check the execution of all prescribed operations and documents.
Performance of physical inspection by relevant components.
Vehicle discharge from the customs area.
Attention: When importing goods into the Czech Republic, weighted vehicles were directly carried out by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When the goods were imported into SR, the weighted vehicles were carried out by the personnel of the delegated legal person.
Vehicles were registered in computer records after consideration.

Sampling was done regardless of country of destination with a focus on risk commodities.

5.2.1. Check of selected sample at the financial authorities
NKÚ focused mainly on controlled financial authorities:
- the procedure of the financial authorities in verifying the accuracy of the VAT declared,
- cooperation of the financial authorities with customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the JCD database at the financial offices with a focus on comparing the declared value, applying the correct VAT rate following the customs classification of goods or services, or. comparison of data on JCD and attached invoices with data in the customs database,
- comparison of VAT tax return data on transactions made and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at financial offices or customs database,
- the method of verifying the right to exemption from VAT on export of goods or services abroad,
- comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services reported in VAT tax returns with data from the customs database.
The JCD database at the financial authorities only contained records of those imports and exports where tax entities were obliged to introduce imports or exports into their tax return.
The inspected financial authorities examined tax agencies files reported imports totalling 60 396 thousand in VAT tax returns in 2002 and 2003 Kč and the corresponding VAT totaling 12 644 052 thousand...
