Differences found between records in the JCD database at the financial offices and the Czech customs database were checked as follows:
- JCD items, which were missing from the customs database of the Czech Republic, were requested directly at the Directorate-General of the Czech Republic,
- JCD items that were missing from the IRS database were verified whether these were cancelled documents,
- for JCD items, where different values were found between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of the financial authorities, the relevant JCD were requested at the Directorate-General of Customs of the Czech Republic, including the attached invoices.
During the examination, it was found that the JCD database at the financial authorities did not contain, for example, records of import JCD totalling VAT 3 622 thousand. Kč and records of export JCD totalling 9 359 thousand...
5.2.1.1. Differences found
The following differences were found by comparing the JCD database at the financial authorities and accumulated tax liability for 2002 and 2003 in VAT tax returns for the selected sample of tax entities:
The differences in values were mainly caused by:
- Time shift between the implementation of imports and the claim to deduct VAT measured on importation of goods.
The tax agency could claim the tax deduction on imports of goods within 3 years of the end of the tax period in which the goods were placed under the relevant procedure or. in the case of temporary importation regime, no later than 3 years after the end of the tax period in which the scheme was terminated.
- The time shift between exports and the moment the tax body received JCD.
The tax body was obliged to provide information on exports exempted from the obligation to apply tax on the output tax return to VAT tax return first for the tax period in which the goods came out of the country, provided that it also had a tax document which was JCD.
- Failure to comply with tax entities obligations when reporting imports and exports in VAT tax returns.
In some cases tax entities did not include correct data on imports and exports in VAT tax returns.
Since tax entities did not have to attach JCD lists to VAT filed tax returns, it was difficult to check the right to deduct VAT or VAT exemption by the tax authorities.
5.2.2. Co-operation of the financial and customs authorities
During the period controlled, the customs authorities decided to repay or exemption from import or export duties and VAT.
Tax entities were lawfully imposed to reduce the previously applied right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax refunded by the customs office in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation provided for the transmission of information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT from customs offices to the tax authorities.
Some inspected financial authorities received this information, however irregularly or with significant delay and only from certain customs offices.
One controlled financial authority did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office has not received information about changes in customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the information needed to check compliance with the legal obligation of tax entities.
In 2002 the customs authorities paid VAT back more than 319 miles. Kč and in 2003 in over 398 miles...
The results of the inspection pointed out the ongoing deficiencies in the activity of tax administrators, some systemic errors in cooperation of the financial authorities with customs authorities and failure to comply with certain duties of tax payers filing tax returns and spd.
The management of VAT and SPD identified shortcomings especially in the following areas:
(a) when VAT registrations were cancelled, the payer s' obligation to pay VAT on the commercial property of the registered owner, or which should have been registered on the date of cancellation of the registration for which the payer applied the tax deduction, was verified only in a rare way,
(b) the financial authorities did not thoroughly use the opportunity to carry out a tax check or a local investigation.
This in some cases caused a lack of verification of the right to deduct VAT,
(c) the official records and oral conduct protocols did not contain all the necessary data demonstrating the legitimacy of the excess VAT deductions applied;
(d) the financial authorities did not adequately verify imports and exports declared in VAT tax returns.
5.3. Control findings in SR
5.3.1. Check of selected sample at tax authorities
For the selected sample NKÚ SR verified or the tax authority carried out a tax check for the 2002 and 2003. tax period.
After analysing the tax returns filed and tax refund applications for selected tax entities NKÚ SR, the tax authority asked to provide the relevant JCD evidence of imports and exports, invoices and documents of tax payment.
Subsequently, the NKÚ SR checked whether the JCD submitted were registered in the customs database of imports and exports and the fulfilment of the deciding facts and statutory conditions for the application of the tax deduction on entry from the importation, the refund of excess VAT, the application of the exemption from the export title and the refund SpD.
NKÚ SR verified selected cases of imports and exports of goods between SR and Czech Republic in a structure according to the tribute to JCD items and the sum of statistical values listed in the table below.
In total, imports at 856,2 mil statistical value were checked. Sk, representing 5,11 % of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic to SROV.
Exports of selected commodities were checked totalling 176 miles. Sk, from the total value of exports of selected commodities from SR to the Czech Republic represent 6,87 %.
618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white equipment, packaging and software) from EU states to SR were also checked. Sk.
5.3.2. Co-operation of tax and customs authorities
NKÚ SR by checking at tax offices found irregularities between data registered in the SR customs database and data reported in specific VAT tax returns, e.g.
- 2 tax entities (natural persons) reported imports of goods totalling 1 589 261 Sk in tax returns, which made them entitled to excess VAT deductions.
In local investigations carried out at the NKÚ SR complaint, tax agencies failed to demonstrate to the tax authority the right to apply the entry tax by relevant documents of imports and VAT payment,
- the tax body (s.r.o.) declared in tax return for the taxation period January 2003 the taxable amount of 167 77 576 Sk, export of goods worth 18 006 041 Sk and has applied excessive VAT deduction of 17 157 Sk.
The VAT tax returns filed for 2003 show that the difference between the volume of purchase and exports of 535 59 161 Sk resulting from January 2003 was not compensated throughout 2003
In the above mentioned cases, NKÚ SR asked the competent tax authorities to carry out a tax check of excessive VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax body (s.r.o.) for the tax period January to June 2002 reported exports of goods totaling 87 199 Sk in VAT tax returns.
The verification in the customs database of SR found that the tax body made exports at statistical value of 296 747 Sk during that period.
The tax office carried out multiple local inquiries at the company's headquarters, finding that the company manager (UK citizen) had traveled and the company left the leased premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of the NKÚ SR control, the tax administrator reported to the criminal proceedings authorities a notice of suspicion of non-tax failure to commit a crime.
Based on the results of the inspection at selected tax authorities, the NKÚ SR states that the biggest problems in the exercise of VAT and VAT control and SpD were mainly in the following areas:
- non-use of the possibility to carry out a tax check of VAT on problematic tax entities, especially in cases of high value of excessive VAT deductions,
- tax inspection protocols did not contain a list of checked documents
- JCD on import and export of goods,
- insufficient examination of declared imports and exports of goods in tax returns,
- the lengthy management of tax administrators when making decisions, especially in the context of the assessment procedure, as well as the result of the demise of the right to measure sanctions,
- non-compliance with legal conditions when providing tax deferrals,
- noncompensation of VAT arrears within the deadline for the refund of excessive VAT deduction,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and tax arrears.
Based on the check of the identified deficiencies of the NKÚ SR, the competent tax authorities asked for a tax inspection of VAT with a focus on the legitimacy of the excess VAT applied for 14 tax entities.
All inspected tax authorities have been taken measures to eliminate the control of the identified deficiencies, which will be monitored and controlled by the NKÚ SR.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation enabled the examination of commercial transactions between trading partners from both States and highlighted the shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
The result of the checks was also the finding of persistent deficiencies in the performance of VAT and SPD payers duties, in financial or financial activities. tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately decreased the effectiveness and effectiveness of tax checks.
The knowledge gained also revealed that the financial authorities in the Czech Republic have basic data on imports and exports from the Czech Customs database within the tax information system. There is no similar system in SR for transmitting information on imports and exports of goods between customs and tax administration.
The procedure for verifying the performance of VAT and SpD management was not the same due to different rules and conditions in both countries.
NKÚ verified the necessary data from the information obtained from the customs administration of the Czech Republic and from the documents available at the inspected financial offices. NKÚ SR verified the execution of commercial transactions from tax entities requested via tax authorities.
In case of irregularities, the tax authorities asked to carry out tax checks.
Parallel checks carried out in the VAT and SpD area evaluated the state of management of these taxes during the period before joining the European Union and pointed out the need for further cooperation in this area.
The cooperation between each other will further deepen during the monitoring of financial and financial activity. tax authorities in connection with the adoption of a new VAT law.
One of the new duties related to the supply of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of the so-called. summary report.
This report must be submitted by all VAT payers who made the delivery of goods to another Member State to a VAT registered person in another Member State.
Tax administrators are obliged to enter data from summary reports into VIES (VAT Information Exchange System), to which tax administrators of Member States of the European Union have access to.
Financial, resp. tax authorities then have the opportunity to compare these data with the data given in the VAT tax returns filed.
This system is also used to verify the validity of VAT tax persons, verification of the validity of the VAT exemption applied for delivery of goods to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel control actions showed the possibilities of cooperation between NKÚ and NKÚ SR.
Results of these control actions will be confronted with outputs of prepared inspection actions, which will, among other things, focus on vetting the VIES system to prevent tax evasion in the so-called. ′′ intracommunitary deliveries ".
Given the importance of VAT and SpD for budgetary revenue, control activity should be focused mainly on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to reduce the space for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communicating
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the Vice President of the Supreme Supervisory Authority and the chairman of Najvyšie's control office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the results of the inspection in asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State property and funds to secure the operation of the Ministry of Interior Refugee Facilities
Control action no. 04/23 ′′ State property and funds intended to secure the activities of the Ministry of Interior Refugee Facilities Administration ′′
Control action no. 15/2004 ′′ Control of economics with stack property and financial prostates intended for asylum and temporary attacking of cudzincom in SR ′′
1. Introduction
Migration of the population is one of phenomena that has a global character and have become an inseparable part of the current development phase of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Its cause is especially the escape of citizens from the country of origin or the last permanent residence from persecution, especially for reasons of racial, religious, national, political, and the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their goal is to acquire asylum and integrate into society, especially in one of Europe's developed democratic countries.
The large group is also made up of foreigners, whose reason for migration is adverse economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the Geneva agreement of 1951 and the New York Protocol 1967 on the status of refugees accepted by the governments of signatory countries to apply them in their foreign-political orientation.
The Czech and Slovak Federative Republic ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the division in 1993, the Czech Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to fulfil the international documents adopted and confirmed their commitment within national legislation by a legal act.
Both republics have enshrined asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's highest control office and the Slovak Republic related issues were focused on the asylum process and the related issues, whose results are contained in a joint final report.
Cooperation between the top supervisory authorities of the two countries was carried out on the basis of the ' Contract for Cooperation in Control Act ' (hereinafter referred to as ' the Treaty ') concluded in April 2004.
Both parties committed in the contract to provide each other with information on legislation governing asylum proceedings in the state of the other Party, selected statistical data concerning the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The effort of parallel control action was to identify identical troubled circuits and highlight the consequences of this for population migration.
The cooperation consisted of unifying the programme of control actions, exchanging information within the scope of the Treaty and drawing up a common final report on the outcome of the checks.
At the first joint action between 5.4. and 7.4.2004, the same circuits of controlled issues and control procedures were established during the preparation of control actions.
The second meeting, which took place from 28.6. to 30.6. 2004, specified common points for the programme of control action.
The third joint meeting held during the inspection event from 8.11. to 10.11.2004 was exchanged experience from ongoing inspections.
The forms of output from the checks were specified and the structure and content of the Joint Final Report, which was drawn up between 14.2. and 17.2. 2005 at the last common meeting.
The checks were carried out parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the inspectors of the Defense and Security Department and selected territorial unions carried out the inspection.
The controlled persons were the Ministry of Interior (hereinafter referred to as ′′ MV ′′) and the Ministry of Interior Refugee Facilities (hereinafter referred to as ′′ SUZ ′′).
In the Slovak Republic, the section of defence, internal and staunch offices carried out a check.
The controlled body was the Migration Office of the Ministry of Vnutra SR (hereinafter referred to as ′′ MÚ ′′).
The controlled period was 2001, 2002, 2003 (hereinafter referred to as the period controlled).
In some cases, statistical data for a longer period are used in the joint report.
2. Recap of inspection results
2.1. Assessment of control activity
The subject of parallel checks was: - asylum process, - asylum facilities, - management of funds and state property, - internal control system.
The interchange of experience gained between the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's High Supervisory Authority took place at the stage of preparation and implementation of inspection events.
This exchange enabled more thoroughly evaluated the documents submitted, analyzing the causes of the identified differences in security of the asylum process.
So it was possible to concentrate on decisive problems affecting the activity of asylum devices.
Finally, this positively impacted the quality of the inspection activity.
2.2 Summary of the results of the inspection
Harmonization of asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with European Union documents (hereinafter referred to as the EU) was the subject of European Commission evaluation reports to the preparedness of both countries for EU accession.
The adoption of legislation regulating this area continues even after both countries join the EU with the aim of further harmonization with EU law.
The number of applicants for asylum in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has a continuously growing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements.
The national budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is mainly affected by the number of applicants, the duration of asylum proceedings until the granting or granting of asylum and also the health status of applicants.
The amount of some selected benefits is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic established asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of the parties to the asylum proceedings.
Accommodation, eating, healthcare and basic material equipment and hygiene supplies are provided in asylum seekers during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organised in leisure activities and applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
Asylum facilities include admission centres and residence centres, in the Czech Republic and integration centres.
The cost of one stay day depends on the occupancy and equipment of the Centre and are comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is basically stabilized.
The Slovak Republic is projected to increase by nearly 1 000 places in the next two years.
The aim is to create conditions for applicants whose increasing numbers are expected to continue in the context of the Dublin Convention application in the years to come.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of approved budgetary expenditure was spent on service security. The decisive spending of this item was the accommodation and eating of applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, healthcare expenses provided to asylum seekers and the cost of permanent security service ensuring the protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work done and insurance were significantly involved in the overall expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of migration policy and asylum process was marked by many budgetary measures, which addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, material and services expenses and security services were crucial in drawing up current expenses.
The results of the inspection in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a fundamental impact on financial management and state property management.
These were shortcomings especially in the area of the use of state budget funds in contrast to the purpose for which the state budget law was determined when the current expenditure was covered by an action with the character of technical assessment of long-term material assets.
The accounting law in inventory and non-compliance with the account curriculum was also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were found in the handling of state property when it was left to another person without a contract.
Non-compliance with the deadline for reporting changes in the real estate cadastral data violated the Real Estate Cadastral Act and leaving waste to a person who was not a person entitled to waste management was violated.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings were also identified in the Slovak Republic when disproportionately high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, shortcomings in public procurement and management of state property, when its records were not sufficiently secured and no evidence of the disposal of unnecessary property was demonstrated.
The internal control system has been ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic within the meaning of the generally binding legislation that regulates the way financial control is carried out.
No deficiencies were found in the written documentation submitted.
The Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic Supervisory Authority, despite some deficiencies identified, evaluate positively the SUZ and MÚ procedure in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the knowledge gained during the inspection, the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's Highest Supervisory Authority find that despite the significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the relevant organisational components of both countries have managed tasks related to asylum seekers at an appropriate level I'm sorry.
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the inspection were discussed with stakeholders of the relevant state organisational components on both Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the inspection, we recommend that positive methodological experience of control be used in other joint control actions in the international cooperation of the highest control institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the Geneva Convention 1951 (Convention on the Status of Refugees and the follow-up of the New York Protocol 1967).
The first regulation was implemented by law no. 498/1990 Coll., about refugees.
In the Czech Republic there is an effective law no from 1. 1. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum and amendment of law no. 83/1991 Coll., about the police of the Czech Republic.
This law has been amended five times in total (law no. 2/2002 Coll., by law no. 217/2002 Coll., by law no. 320/2002 Coll., by law no. 519/2002 Coll. and by law no. 222/2003 Coll.).
In the legislative process there are currently two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., asylum and adoption of other amendments will be bound to European legislation.
At the time of law making no. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, the area of asylum was part of the 3. th pillar of the EU and asylum documents were in terms of commitment by political documents.
As part of the adoption of this law, efforts have been made to make it as compatible with EU law as possible.
A significant change for asylum policy within the EU was the move of asylum issues from the 3. th to the 1. th pillar, when asylum law became part of the community law from 1.5. 1999 under the Amsterdam Treaty.
This shift triggered the need to create adequate legislation, i.e. create legal instruments in the corresponding legal obligation.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents was the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key communitarian regulations in the area of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic joined the EU and their transposition period at the time of the inspection of the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic has not yet elapsed.
After their implementation into the Czech law, the Czech Republic will be obliged to inform the European Commission how it has performed the transposition.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure for the granting of refugee status proceedings and the determination of duties of foreigners who applied for refugee status or who were granted temporary refuge in the territory of the Slovak Republic was established with effect from 1.1.1996 the law of the National Council of the Slovak Republic No. 283/1995 Z. from., about refugees.
Since 2003 the Refugee Act has been replaced by Act No. 480/2002 Z. from ′′ on asylum and amending and supplementing certain laws in which the harmonization of the Slovak Republic legislation with Council of Europe 20. 2001/55 2001 on minimum standards for provision of temporary protection in case of mass influx of displaced persons and measures to support the balance of efforts between Member States in the adoption of such persons and endurance of the resulting consequences.
After two amendments to law no. 480/2002 Z z., asylum, in 2003 and 2004 a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which means further harmonization of the Slovak Republic law with EU legislation in migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the determination of the duty for asylum to attend the courses of the Slovak language during their stay in the integration center, the determination of the guardian of the courts in non-age foreigners, when they stay in the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, allowing applicants to enter into a working relationship under certain circumstances, specified in the amendment to the law.
Harmonization of the Slovak Republic law with EU law in migration and asylum process was evaluated in regular reports by the European Commission on preparedness for the entry of the Slovak Republic into the EU.
In 2002 the report highlighted the lack of staff capacity MÚ which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, matters concerning refugees have fallen within the competence of MV.
Effective from 1. August 1., the MV established an organizational component of the SUZ state. The reason was to separate the state administration's performance in the area of asylum procedure, which is performed through the MV asylum and migration policy department, from providing services to asylum seekers.
The task of SUZ is to provide accommodation, food, health and other services to participants in asylum and asylum proceedings for MV.
In the Slovak Republic they perform decisive tasks in the area of the azylového asylum process, especially in terms of financial and material-technical security of the asylum process to the extent defined by specific regulations.
Priority tasks are questions related to decisions on foreigners applications for asylum in I. degree of administrative management and complex operation of asylum facilities in the area of accommodation, meals, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, he is preparing a concept for state migration policy.
Results achieved in the area of asylum system production in the Slovak Republic in recent years have significantly influenced cooperation and support from the UN High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).
A special contribution was his financial complicity in the reconstruction of the housing fund for asylum.
UNHCR co-financed social, cultural and sports activities for applicants.
4.1 Development of asylum seekers and asylum results
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the graph.
There was a significant increase in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis and in 2003 there was an increased number of refugees from Chechnya.
Overview of the results of the asylum proceedings in the Czech Republic is given in Table No. 1.
In the controlled period, asylum was granted in total 394 cases, of which 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 cases in 2003.
Asylum was not granted in total in 22 cases in the controlled period and in 22 cases the asylum proceedings were terminated.
The number of parties to proceedings at 1.1. includes both persons who have not yet been subjected to the decision and those who have not been forwarded to the decision.
Additionally, there are persons who have been forgiven for missing the deadline for filing an appeal or who have been annulled a previous decision and have not yet been issued a new one.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers has a growing trend.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, in 2003 it was already 10 358 people.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, with 8 131 applicants registered, representing an increase of 423 % against 2000, where 556 1 people applied for asylum.
The information on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic during the controlled period is given in Table No. 2.
A total of 49 asylums were granted in the controlled period and their number did not exceed 0,22 % of the registered number of applicants in each year.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
Asylum proceedings were stopped in total in 23 cases.
Most of the applicants voluntarily left the asylum procedure before ending it, by staying outside the asylum without permission.
More than 82 % of the total registered applicants in 2002 and more than 94 % of people in 2003
The length of one applicant's stay in one of the asylum facilities, converted into an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The poznatků knowledge also shows that most applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic are looking for better living conditions, i.e. the so-called. economic migration that has no support in documents adopted by the international community, which the Slovak Republic has also signed up for.
In these cases the asylum system is purposely used by the applicant.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons such as job seeking or better living conditions is not a reason to grant asylum.
Such an application should be according to the provisions of § 12 ods. 1 (1) (a) Act No. 480/2002 Z. z., asylum, considered apparently unjustified and should be decided within 30 days.
So far, internationally recognized principles are not established to identify economic migrants that distinguish them from those persecuted in the country of origin and which would allow the asylum process to accelerate.
Given the above, it can be stated that the Slovak Republic is transit countries and migration target countries were and remain West European states in terms of international migration.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic after accession to the EU acceded to the agreement defining the state responsible for assessing asylum applications submitted in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents multiple purpose applications for asylum in multiple EU countries.
Applicants return to the country of first registration after positive identification in the EURODAC system.
The Slovak Republic is part of the outdoor border of EU countries, therefore the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to create conditions for residence in the Slovak Republic until the decision to grant or not grant asylum.
4.2 Pumping of funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements and their forthcoming national legislative arrangements.
The national budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure derived from the state budget is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of asylum proceedings until the final decision on asylum and their state of health.
The growing number of persons entering the asylum process has a direct impact on higher drawing of law-adjusted benefits for applicants, such as food, allowance, expenses on basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some benefits collected is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, during the controlled period there was a meal of CZK 58 per person per day, allowance CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child up to 15 years of age.
The cost of one asylum seeker for one stay day was on average 351 CZK in 2001, 383 CZK in 2002 and 345 CZK in 2003.
Outside of pocket money, applicants for asylum lodged in residential centres with separate cooking and applicants who are private outside asylum facilities may be given a contribution up to the minimum of life.
Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, as amended, inter alia, in § 84 municipalities, entitles to a contribution to cover costs incurred in connection with asylum facilities in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was set annually by government resolutions and in the controlled period it was CZK 7 per person and residential day.
At the same time, municipalities are entitled to a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools visited by asylum seekers.
The amount of the contribution was 120 CZK per pupil per month during the controlled period, provided that the person attended school for at least 10 days in a given month.
In the Slovak Republic, during the controlled period, 70 Sk per person per day, pocket 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk per child under 15 years of age.
The cost of one asylum seeker for one stay day was an average of 442 Sk in 2001, 447 Sk in 2002 and 445 Sk in 2003.
The municipalities in whose territory there is an asylum facility, are in accordance with Law No. 480/2002 Z. from., asylum, a contribution to partial reimbursement of the expenditure incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and activities of the asylum facility.
Meanwhile, municipalities have only partly used the opportunity to apply for a contribution set at 1 500 Sk per bed and calendar year.
National legislation in both countries for asylum decisions sets a 90-day deadline from the opening of the asylum procedure and at the same time admits an extension of this period in justified cases.
The most common reason for extending the procedure for asylum, which affects the amount of state budget spending, is the appeal against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31,54 %).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of application for asylum (17,61 %).
In total, 73 % of asylum proceedings initiated between 2001-2003 were decided within one year of their opening.
92 % of asylum applications were decided on within two years of the opening of the asylum procedure.
According to. data, up to 90 % of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic use the legal possibility of extending the deadline by appeal to the court.
In some cases, the extension was over a year and at the time of the inspection, the court proceedings were not closed.
A certain contribution in the shortening of asylum proceedings is expected from the establishment of common workplaces MÚ and the Úradu of the border and chadzinec Policy in the admission centres in Adamov-Gbeloch, Opatovskej Novej Village and in Liptovských Vlachoch, which was attended at the time of inspection from 1.10.2004.
This implies simplification of procedures and reducing the deadlines of proceedings between the two components of the asylum process.
5. Asylum devices
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic established asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for providing services to participants in asylum proceedings.
Asylum facilities provide accommodation, meals, health care, pocket and basic material equipment and hygiene supplies during the stay.
At the same time courses are organised in leisure activities and conditions for cultural and sports activities are created for applicants.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
SUZ manages and runs asylum facilities and is competent to manage state property in the premises of the reception center Vyšní Lhota, the reception and residence center Červený Újezd, Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka near Brno, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the objects of the integration asylum centres of Jaromer and Stop near Brno.
At the beginning of 2002, an admission center was established in the transit space of Prague-Ruzyně Airport.
SUZ further ensures the operation of asylum facilities in Stráži pod Ralsko, Seči, Bruntál, Zbýšově and Kashava, which are operated by a legal person based on § 80 (80). Article 3 of Law No. 325/1999 Coll, asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of the admission centres is 747 places and the total accommodation capacity of the residential centres is 1 places.
Receiving centres are closed facilities that asylum seekers must not leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic admission procedures referred to in Act No. 325/1999 Coll., asylum.
Violence of the duty to stay in the admission center is considered a misdemeanor.
Residence centres where asylum seekers from reception centres are used to accommodate applicants for asylum until the time of legal power is acquired, decisions on their application for or not granted asylum.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers are allowed to leave residence centres or. stay in private.
Asylum seekers have the right to free accommodation, food, other services and allowance in the admission and residence centres in which they are reported, where they are entitled to free accommodation, provision of food, other services and allowance, provided that they have suffered the necessary actions to identify their financial and property ratios, and these ratios are such that they cannot be fairly asked for even partial payment of the services.
Integration asylum centres serve temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are staying in the center based on a accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months with the possibility of extension until adequate housing is provided for them, or will be secured by themselves under the state integration program.
In the integration center, clients pay for all accommodation costs and eat individually.
Persons with a confessed refugee status have the same rights and duties as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Cost of asylum equipment
For comparison of asylum facilities, the best indicator of the amount of costs per physical stay day was chosen.
It is based on the factual number of persons who were actually provided daily services provided by asylum equipment.
In table no. 3 and in the graph are devices operated by SUZ designated as own and facilities operated by legal persons under Section 80 of Law No. 325/1999 Coll., asylum, as contractual.
The cost of one stay day in the own asylum facility operated by SUZ decreases with the increasing fulfillment of these facilities. The cause is that the fixed cost of operating objects is calculated on multiple asylum seekers.
The volume of total costs incurred to provide services for asylum seekers is directly increasing with their growing number.
Between 2001 and 2003, applicants in crisis capacity were lodged in their own asylum facilities.
In part of 2003, exceptional accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds) was used to solve the capacity crisis of asylum asylum seekers caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers from Poland.
This capacity was secured by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
One applicant's spending for one stay day was then lower in these years.
However, long-term maintenance of high fulfilment of these devices is not possible.
It is necessary to take into account the risks of unexpected flows of refugees and the associated requirement for higher accommodation capacity.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments with fully occupied accommodation capacity.
The form of asylum installations operated contractually allows the adoption of operational solutions in the area of asylum facilities, where necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centres and stay centres.
The MÚ has Adamov-Gbely, Rohovka, Opatovská Nová Ves and the stay center Brezová pod Bradlom in its administration.
The total capacity of the admission centres is 470 seats and a residential center of 100 seats.
The growing number of asylum seekers handled. by setting up a residential center in Gabčíkově in rented premises of the Slovak Technical University Bratislava with flexible available capacity from 250 to 940 places.
According to the contract concluded, the leaseer also ensures the provision of services related to the operation of the centre.
In this form, MÚ was dealing with lack of its own staff.
The residential center was also temporarily established in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 places.
The admission centres had an average of 57 % to 62 % during the controlled period, on average from 33 % to 50 % in the residential centres.
The occupancy changed according to the season and the highest was in the last months of the year, when he applied for asylum for a much larger number of applicants compared to other months of the year.
Another increase in accommodation capacity by about 450 places will be possible after reconstruction of resorts in Opatovskej Novej Village and Vlachoch.
After the construction of the Humennom resort in 2006, the number of places will increase by another 550 people.

In the Czech Republic, the approved budgetary expenditure of SUZ was increased by 077 103 thousand in 2001..
Of which 89 thousand. Kč (87,29 %) were purposely intended. The large part was intended to address the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (44 538 thousand. Kč) and provision of health care provided to asylum seekers (38 870 thousand..).
In 2002 SUZ spending was increased by 88 88 thousand by 362 budgetary measures...
Of which 62 thousand. Kč (70,48 %) was purposely designated means, of which mostly (53 200 thousand. Kč) was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003 SUZ spending was increased by 88 88 thousand by 078 budgetary measures...
Of which 82 thousand. Kč (93,09 %) amounted to purposely designated funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
Amount 51 thousand. Kč was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers, 24 000 thousand. Kč to solve the tide of Chechen refugees and 7 000 thousand. Kč for the program of humanitarian evacuation of disabled people of Iraqi Republic.

Expenditure on salaries, payments for work done and insurance (23,99 %-24,97 %).

In the Slovak Republic, the budget management of MÚ to ensure migration policy and asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures that addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in asylum seekers.
The draft and breakdown of the budget in the spending part was characterised in particular in 2001 and 2002 by the nerovnováha requirements, which were based on an increase in the number of applicants for asylum and the needs of financing their legal claims and resources provided mainly in the main category of ordinary spending.
Over the course of the year, the budgetary chapter manager handled multiple budgetary measures, increasing the current spending limit by 41,8 % in 2001 and by up to 71,7 % in 2002

6.2 Deficiencies detected
The results of the inspection in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a fundamental impact on the management of funds and state property.
These were shortcomings, especially in the following areas: (a) the use of state budget appropriations in violation of the purpose for which the state budget law was determined when ordinary expenses were covered by actions having the character of technical assessment of long-term material property; (b) infringement of the accounting law in the field of inventory and non-compliance with the indicative accounts curriculum.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were found in the management of the state property, when it was left to use another person without an appropriate contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes to the real estate cadastral data was violated by the law on the cadastral of real estate; leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not a person entitled waste management has been violated.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings were found in the provision of disproportionate advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, shortcomings in public procurement and management of state property, when its registration was not sufficiently secured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, an internal control system within the meaning of the law no was introduced at SUZ on 1.7. 2002 320/2001 Coll., on financial control, determining the competences of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, interim and subsequent checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system has been established and an internal auditor of SUZ has been appointed.
Every year SUZ is issued a plan of financial, socio-economic and operational technical checks aimed at comprehensive verification of the management of funds and state property in individual asylum facilities managed by SUZ.
In 2002 there were 42 management checks and in 2003 there were 54.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct exercise of control activities in the departments and organizations of the Ministry of Interior of the Slovak Republic in terms of compliance with generally binding laws and internal rules, the Office ensures the Minister's Control.
During the period controlled, no inspection of tasks on the section of asylum policy was carried out.
The internal control system MÚ is mainly focused on the implementation of preliminary and interim financial control under Law No. 502/2001 Z. from., about financial control and internal audit.
The execution of financial control is also regulated by the internal rules of the director of MÚ
The factual focus of the control activity as part of the management of individual departments was established under the annual MÚ plan.
Designated by union directors were responsible for the exercise of control in this area.
According to the documentation submitted, no shortcomings were found.
Since the Ministry of Interior regulation of the Slovak Republic No. 28 out of 23. 4. 4. 2004 is obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the complaints law.
The organizational security of this task will need to be resolved in the upcoming period.
Communicating
This report was drawn up in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the Vice President of the Supreme Supervisory Authority and the chairman of Najvyšie's control office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint report on parallel checks on spending on the construction of the Prague - Dresden highway
Introductory word
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, modern, dynamic and above all united Europe would be hard to imagine.
Quality transport networks are a necessary condition for maintaining and increasing the standard of living of Europeans.
Creating conditions for fast, safe, reliable and cheap transport of persons and costs is an important task for the government.
It is a very demanding task both organisational and technical and financial aspects.
European efforts for sustainable mobility often and hardly find compromises with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and suitable environment for humans.
Construction of transport infrastructure, thanks to the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, buildings are financially demanding.
Appropriate procedures and decision-making by the state administration in the preparation and acquisition of transport buildings can bring significant savings of public financial resources, which can be used differently for the benefit of citizens.
One of the tasks of control institutions is to actively look for shortcomings that led to lower than achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of spending on construction of transport infrastructure.
Control institutions should not only draw attention to the identified deficiencies, but recommend measures to improve the state, for the benefit of citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
The two top supervisory institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as ′′ BRH ′′) and the Supreme Supervisory Authority (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ ′′) carried out parallel checks on expenditure on 2005 and 2006 construction of the highway Prague - Dresden (highway D 8 in the Czech Republic and highway A 17 in Germany).
Highways are connected by a border bridge co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to cooperation with NKÚ, the BRH was able to carry out a thorough check on the efficiency of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
Based on close cooperation with BRH, NKÚ obtained the necessary data on the amount of German bridge and tunnel costs for comparative purposes.
The Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany closed in 2000th border bridge construction contract.
According to the construction procedure, the completion date was finally planned for the end of 2006.
However, during the award of the contract, the Directorate of Roads and Highways of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as ′′ RSD ′′) caused mistakes that led to an extension of the competition period and shortening the time for construction.
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in shorter time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, RSD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
The prices of bridges on the D 8 and A 17 highways were compared with the calculation to m2 of the bridge construction area.
Statistical price analysis allowed bridges with high costs per m2 area to be identified.
Analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges with a length of over 100 meters.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay caused by the contract procedure.
When analyzing the cost of building tunnels, the inspectors found that the prices of tunnels on the D 8 highway are significantly higher than the prices of comparable tunnels in Germany.
BRH and NKÚ now have a database of prices for bridges and tunnels, which they will be able to rely on for future checks on the effectiveness of the means used for transport infrastructure purposes.
Both control institutions recommend to build bridges: standardization of bridges and the use of coupled steel-concrete and special structures only when pre-strung iron concrete bridges are not adequate.
The main features of cooperation included her team spirit and informality.
During the parallel inspection, the inspectors participated in their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report informs about the progress and results of parallel checks on funds spent on the construction of a highway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The checks were focused on the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of the costs incurred.
Parallel checks were carried out by BRH in Germany and NKU in the Czech Republic.
Parallel checks took place in 2005 and 2006.
NKÚ controlled the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of spending of approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately přibližně 690 million) on the border section of the D 8, highway, which has number 0807.
Of this amount, 64 64 million from European funds (ISPA) was planned to be used.
In addition to a parallel inspection carried out together with NKÚ, BRH controlled the preparation and construction of the A 17 highway in 2003 and 2005.
The resources spent on the construction of all three sections of the A 17 highway amounted to about 670 670 million and of which. 277 million co-financed by European funds (EFRE).
The highway from Prague to Dresden is part of the Trans-European Transport Corridor IV. Dresden - central and southern part of Eastern Europe - Istanbul.
The D 8 highway leads from Prague through Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
Highway A 17 leads from the state border of the Czech Republic / Germany to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, border sections of both highways were under construction.
These sections were launched on December 21., 2006.
On the German side, the highway is completed all the way to Dresden, while on the Czech side of the D 8 highway is not finished, because section no. 0805 in length 16,4 km across the Czech Mountains between Řehlovicemi and Lovosice is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, section no. 0805 between Prague and Ústím nad Labem to walk through the protected landscape area of Czech Mountains.
According to the forecasts made in the Czech Republic in 2001, it should be in r. 2008 on the border section no. 0807 highway D 8 traffic intensity 22 vehicles per day.
According to German forecasts, the traffic intensity at the Czech border will amount to about 25 vehicles per day in 2010
Germany and the Czech Republic concluded in 2000 a contract between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic on the connection of the German highway A 17 and the Czech highway D 8 on a common state border by building a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, so the control of the construction of this bridge was an important aspect of parallel checks carried out by both control institutions.
Cooperation of BRH and NKÚ
Since mid-2005, the two top control institutions acted on close cooperation in the inspection of the highway building connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both parties had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1.
Germany is financially involved in building a border bridge.
Its planning and construction is based on RSD.
Therefore, BRH himself did not have the opportunity to inspect this construction project.
2.
NKÚ did not have a comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically in terms of the total cost of bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3.
NKÚ needed to be sure about the effectiveness of spending, taking into account the main technical parameters of the highway, especially the arrangement of bridges and tunnels, which should allow the same quality of driving on both sides of the border.
Following preparatory negotiations, on 4. January 2006, the Presidents of the two top control institutions were signed an agreement on coordinated inspection of the highway D 8 / A 17.
Joint work discussions between the BRH and the NKU inspectors took place throughout 2006 at an interval of approximately six to eight weeks.
The negotiations were dealing with current problems and tasks, especially the preparation of a uniform methodology for control of prices of bridges and tunnels, exchange of findings from border bridge control and preparation of joint reports.
An important sign of cooperation was the continuous exchange of information.
While the BRH has done most of the work to compare the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and procurement procedures, NKÚ has prepared for the most part a methodology for the price of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal standards for control in the state administration differ in both countries in the way control actions are closed.
For these reasons, the two top supervisory institutions have drawn their own control conclusions on their findings obtained during their checks.
This report reflects the results achieved during parallel checks.
The cooperation will be concluded with the signing of the final komuniké in the first half of 2007.
Construction of the border bridge
The Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed in the 2000 contract on the date of completion of the border bridge construction as possible in 2005.
The two parties then agreed to postpone this deadline until the end of 2006.
The RSD was an investor.
Germany financially contributes to the construction of a bridge from 42,13 %.
In the period until 1999, the RSD proposed that the border bridge should have a pre-concrete concrete structure.
In 1999, after agreement with its partners in Germany, the RSD agreed a coupled steel-concrete construction.
This decision was justified by reducing the number of double pillars from seven to five and the subsequent ecological benefit of such a solution for the valley.
In addition, comparative calculations performed by the RSD stated that coupled steel-concrete construction should be a less expensive option.
But there was a mistake in the calculations.
It stated that the new coupled steel-concrete construction will only be 397 m long.
In reality it is 5 % longer.
During the award of the border bridge contract, the RSD made serious mistakes.
It did not prepare a contract documentation to adequately describe the assessment criteria and the partial criteria for comparing tenders.
This error led to the Commission's Assessment and Assessment of Bids and the Director-General evaluating offers in a subjective and problematic way.
The failed candidate contested the results of the contract procedure.
The subsequent investigation of the Competition Authority led to the contract awarding of the construction contract being signed later than originally expected.
This meant that the summer construction season 2004 after the evaluation of offers was wasted and the construction time has been shortened.
The construction company agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time, but at the cost of a substantial increase in costs.
The procedure offered included double installation of the bridge top, change in pillar construction and installation and equipment of assembly premises.
Moreover, the construction company was not able to acquire the originally designed steel type in the necessary term.
A new type of steel - at a price higher by about zhruba 4 million, which had to be fully paid by the RSD - allowed the time to be reduced to anti-corrosion protection, which subsequently allowed to shorten the total time of construction of the border bridge.
Compared to the net price of 18,3 18,3 million offered in the tender, the total cost of building the border bridge due to accelerated progress and other financing adjustments will increase considerably.
The shortened time reserved for works led to an increase in the price of about 5,9 5,9 million.
Currently, the net cost amount is around kolem 25,9 million, without taking into account automatic price increases (as of October 2006).
Price comparison of bridges and tunnels
Both top control institutions analyzed the prices of bridges on D 8 and A 17 highways to identify bridges whose price was too high and to compare bridges on the German and Czech side.
The analysis was based on methods of mathematical statistics.
The tunnels on D 8 were also compared with similar tunnels on the highways in Germany (A 71, A 38 and A 4).
There are no similar tunnels on the A 17 highway.
When preparing this part of the inspection, it was important to identify the relevant prices accurately.
The two top supervisory institutions established the following principles to compare bridges prices: based on the actual price paid for a bridge without value added tax (VAT rates vary in the Czech Republic and SNR and are subject to changes); do not take into account prices for special foundations of the bridge; transfer prices in CZK na na according to the European Central Bank rate valid on 30. 12. 2005 (CZK 29 = = 1).
On D 8 and A 17 there are bridges of various structures (steel-concrete, pre-concrete, coupled steel-concrete and steel) and various sizes.
In order to ensure homogeneity of the structures examined, bridges were divided into groups according to the type of construction.
Within these groups the size of the bridge was also taken into account during the analysis.
By far the most common type of construction were concrete bridges (20 bridges on D 8, 36 bridges on A 17).
The analysis focused mainly on this group of bridges, as the number of the file enabled the use of mathematical and statistical methods with a high level of reliability of results.
The checks found that the prices for m 2 concrete bridges on D 8 i A 17 depend on the size of the bridge (its length, area): the larger the bridge, the lower the price per m2 of the bridge construction.
For German bridges, the price dependence on size was stronger than for Czech ones (see below charts).
Two concrete bridges on A 17 and four on D 17 have been identified, whose price is significantly higher.
To search these bridges, a method was used to enable atypical values to be detected in a set of numbers, and a regression analysis reflecting the dependency of the price of the bridge to its size (to determine atypical expensive bridges, the standard distance from the regression curve is upward).
However, information on the atypically high price of these bridges should be considered only as an indicator on which bridges need to be targeted.
In order to draw a generally applicable conclusion, the causes of high price in each identified case should be analysed.
One such cause may be an inefficient administrative measure, or also environmental requirements or other acceptable reason.
Given that Czech concrete bridges are on average longer than German (see table below), the proven negative dependency of the price of the bridge on its length could lead to the assumption that Czech bridges should be cheaper.
The hypothesis about lower prices of Czech concrete bridges is also supported by lower labor costs in the construction industry in the Czech Republic compared to Germany.
However, the results of the analysis show that concrete bridges prices on D 8 are higher than the A 17.
Two possible causes of this situation were identified during joint negotiations:
1.
In Germany most bridges are awarded as separate contracts.
Such an assignment allows small and medium-sized regional firms to participate in the contract competition.
In the Czech Republic many bridges are awarded as part of a contract for part of the highway route, which is several kilometers long.
Small and medium-sized companies do not participate in such a competition because the contract is too big for them.
2.
In the Czech Republic there is more variability in the construction of bridges than in Germany.
NKÚ found in this context that the type of bridge construction is decided long before its construction.
The decision is taken at the time when the RSD translates the application for territorial decision.
RSD is choosing types of bridges from multiple variants at this time, but economics plays a smaller role in deciding.
The general conclusion on the prices of bridges in the Czech Republic and Germany could only be expressed on the basis of a thorough analysis of the construction work market in both countries, which would go beyond this control action.
The border bridge is the most expensive steel concrete bridge on D 8 and A 17.
In the case of tunnels, it was found that the prices of tunnels on D 8 were twice the size of the tunnels in Germany.
However, comparison of main construction-technical parameters of tunnels to D 8 with tunnels in Germany showed no significant difference.
Significant price differences could be attributed to the fact that there is no real competition in the Czech Republic in the construction of tunnels.
However, a small number of tunnels did not allow for generally applicable conclusions.
The effectiveness and efficiency of the construction of the Dresden highway - Prague
The independent Czech Republic was created in 1993.
The government approved the concept of highway network development in the same year.
The D 8 highway should have been gradually extended from Prague to the state border with Germany.
Section No. 0805 through the Czech Mountains should have been purchased earlier than the border section no. 0807.
The Czech Republic acquires the D 8 highway as part of programming.
In program no. 327 220 ′′ The construction of the highway D 8 Prague - Ústí nad Labem - the state border of the Czech Republic / Germany ′′ set two goals for construction of the D 8 highway:
1.
improve the connection of Prague and Ústí nad Labem - national goal;
2.
improve the connection of Prague and Berlin within IV. trans-European transport corridor Berlin - Istanbul - international goal.
According to the program, the construction of the section of the leader across the Czech Mountains was supposed to be completed in June 2008 and the construction of the border section no. 0807 in June 2007.
It should be added here that the date of completion is not identical to the date of commissioning.
NKÚ found out that the preparation of the construction of the section of the head over the Czech Mountains is now at the stage of an official territorial decision.
Environmental activists contested this decision by lawsuits.
The lawsuits are not decided legally.
Therefore, it cannot be excluded that the section leading through the Czech Mountains will be completed several years later than stated in the program documentation.
In the summer of 2006, the Czech Ministry of Transport proposed to postpone the deadline for completion of section No. 0805 for 2010.
Due to these facts, the construction of the border section of the national goal has not achieved a better link between Prague and Ústím nad Labem.
RSD has made an estimate of capital costs for border section D 8 No. 0807 and section no. 0805 through Czech Mountains from 1999 to 2001.
The estimate of these capital costs included in the investment costs is about 639 639 million together for both sections No. 0805 and no. 0807.

The economic analysis carried out in 2001 based on the assumption that the border section and section across the Czech Mountains will be completed on time.
However, at the time of inspection, it is clear that the section across the Czech Mountains will not be open in the original term.
This will reduce the above EIRR values.
The cost of both sections without VAT, calculated at 31. 12. 2005, was 897 897 million, i.e. higher 27,4 % than the cost level with which the economic analysis worked in 27,4 2001.
However, there is a risk that section no. 0805 will be guided in a different, costly route, which would affect the abovementioned economic viability limit.
Economic analysis showed that construction of both sections of the highway is economically viable with at least 18 vehicles per day in 2010.
The forecast for 2008 amounted to 22 vehicles, but the study dealing with the issue of bypass routes for the missing section across the Czech Mountains anticipates the traffic intensity of 12 to 13 vehicles per day, which moves an investment below the economic viability limit.
With the higher load of bypass routes for the missing section across the Czech Mountains, there is a high probability of congestion and thus an increase in external costs, which were not expected during the original economic analysis.
The abovementioned reduction in revenue and cost increase means that the already low EIRR that the construction of the border section D 8. will not be achieved.
Construction of the D 8 border section is therefore inefficient.
The construction of the A 17 highway was similar cost overrun as in the case of these two sections on D 8.
As part of the overall economic assessment of the Federal Road Development Plan for Long-distance transport for 1992 The Federal Ministry of Transport of Germany counted about náklady 320 million.
The resulting cost / income ratio was then 4,6.
Meanwhile, however, costs have risen sharply to about 670 670 million and the cost-income ratio has decreased by more than half.
In addition to a parallel inspection carried out together with NKÚ BRH, he controlled the preparation and construction of the A 2005 highway in 2003 and 17.
In doing so, BRH found that the competent approval state authority requested a field tunnel for the third section A 17 that was not needed.
During the inspection event, BRH managed to convince the Federal Ministry and the German road construction administration that the tunnel is not necessary.
The result was the achievement of savings, which amounted to about 10 10 million and 0,15 million on annual operating costs alone.
Assessing the first section A 17 BRH found that the construction project was not properly prepared.
The following example shows this:
At the preparatory stage, the road construction administration did not research the conditions of the rock base in the rocks of Dölzschen because the place was difficult to access.
This was done only after the tunnel stamping machine hit the rock.
Tests showed that the rocks are more weathered inside than expected during the selection process.
Therefore, costly measures such as anchoring, injecting and protective net against stone falling, which required about 3,3 3,3 million.
Road and Highway Directorate had to bear costs not only for other emergency operations such as security measures in the Dölzschen rocks, but also measures that would not be necessary if the construction project was properly prepared first.
Expenditure of this kind includes costs associated with interruption of construction operations ((3,2 million), further training of drilling workers ((0,5 million) and increasing wages and goods costs due to overrun of the project duration (7 7 million).
The cost exceeding amounted to about zhruba 10,7 million, which was not equal to any added value.
Based on the lessons learned from this and other controlled projects, BRH asked the Federal Ministry to apply more strict leadership in its supervision of road construction work.
The Federal Ministry should give the directors of roads and highways the necessary incentive to introduce quality assurance systems.
Benefits of cooperation for BRH and NKÚ Cooperation fulfilled the intention of both control institutions.
BRH gained control knowledge about the preparation, assignment and progress of the border bridge construction.
Both top control institutions have built a database of bridges and tunnels prices, which will be able to base future checks.
NKÚ found that the main construction-technical parameters of bridges, tunnels and route of the D 8 highway are no different from parameters A 17.
Controllers of both cooperation institutions have gained new experience to use in further checks.

Coordinated control of funds for financing projects carried out under the Operational Programme of Cross-border Cooperation Czech Republic - Poland 2007-2013
INTRODUCTION
The emerging community of Europe's population is the driving force behind cross-border cooperation as an integral part of the wider territorial cooperation that has been part of our lives for the last 20 years.
So let this community provide the opening word for this joint report of the two highest control institutions of neighbouring countries:
′′ 185 million EU citizens (i.e. 37 % of the population) live in border areas.
These areas are usually underdeveloped and peripheral territories, often the remains of the darker parts of Europe's history.
The main aim of cross-border cooperation is to help to mitigate the existence of borders as administrative, legal and physical barriers and to further help develop the dormant potential of border regions.
Programmes cover various border regions: some cover seaside areas, other inland borders within the EU or borders shared with candidate countries.
Most programs are bilateral, but some include more than two neighboring countries."
The programmes last seven years and a total of 5,7 billion is earmarked from the EU budget. EUR
′′ The programmes cover the following activities: repairs and reconstruction of cross-border roads, cycling trails and bridges, investments in cross-border waste management systems, medical facilities, research centres, flood measures, etc., common management of natural sites or tourist goals, development of common services for the local population, employment advice, thematic networking and clusters for innovation.
Support from the program is provided on the condition that the organization from both sides of the border (for example regional authorities, universities or SMEs) combines to implement projects based on the needs of the border region.
Leaders of cooperating regions, relevant ministries and other local partners regularly meet and decide which projects will be supported.
This system should lead to a sustainable form of cooperation even after the program itself is finished.
Funds are provided with the condition that project partners from both sides of the border cooperate in a way that fulfils at least two of the following four characters: joint preparation, joint implementation, joint staff, joint financing."
Within the partnership, tasks and responsibilities for the preparation, implementation, financing and control of project activities are clearly defined and distributed to the relevant partners.
Among the main attributes of partnership include: Joint Leader's Choice, Joint Project Development and Application, Joint Partnership Agreement signed by all partners, taking over overall responsibility for the implementation of the project by the leading partner, total payment of support receives by the partner and executes their transfer to the relevant project partners.
Eligible projects carried out in the territory of regions and voivodeship adjacent to a common border may be supported.
OBJECTIVES AND SCOPE OF CHECK
On 11. December 2007, the European Commission (EC) approved the operation programme of cross-border cooperation Czech Republic - Poland 2007-2013 (OPPS Czech-POL).
258 187 467 €. has been earmarked for the implementation of the operational programme.
The total amount included a contribution from the European Funds (ERDF) totalling 459 219 344 (85 %) to be exhausted by the end of 2015.
Financial data on the drawing of EU funds from the Cross-border Cooperation Operational Programme Czech Republic - Poland 2007-2013 at the end of 2013 are given in the following table:
The agreement on cooperation of the highest control institutions of the Czech Republic (NKU) and the Republic of Poland (NIK) was concluded by the presidents of both offices on 27. February 2013 following previous negotiations at the meeting of the heads of the highest control institutions of the Visegrad four, Austria and Slovenia in September 2012 in Lovasberény, Hungary.
The aim of the cooperation was to check whether the implementation of the operational programme is in accordance with the legislation and with binding programming documents or agreements, whether the management and control system works reliably, whether the operational programme goals are achieved and whether the selected projects are implemented in accordance with the specified conditions of the aid granted I'm sorry.
This cooperation took a form of parallel control, whereby the inspection authorities independently examined topics whose content was discussed in advance by their legal mandate.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The inspection carried out also included elements of the performance audit.
The selected topics were tested on a sample of projects with project partners on both sides of the border.
The results of the checks carried out were the checks foundations published in the usual way by both authorities.
Based on both control conclusions set out in the Annex, this Joint Report was created.
The selected common control sample included six projects (Annex 1) that fall within the aid area 1.1-Strengthening transport availability and support area 2.2-Supporting tourism development.
Before the start of the inspection, the drawing of funds from these two areas of support accounted for more than 60 % of the funds paid to beneficiaries by the end of 2012 from ERDF for all projects implemented throughout the OPPS Czech Republic-POL.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In addition to checking a common sample of six projects, NKÚ checked 13 other projects and NIK two more (all from support area 1.1 and 2.2).
The funds paid to beneficiaries of ERDF aid, controlled by NKÚ and NIK, amounted to a total of 362 25 (NKÚ) and 174 8 (NIK).
The controlled amount of funds accounted for 41 % of all funds paid to the beneficiaries of the aid areas 1.1 and 2.2.
MAIN CONTROL CONCLUSIONS
Both checks independently carried out by NKÚ on the Czech side and NIK on the Polish side showed that the level of identified irregularities did not exceed the level of importance.
The implementation of OPPS Czech Republic-POL, involving the functioning of the management and control system and the implementation of selected projects, was successful.
Controlled persons, who were part of the management and control system, took steps to reduce the risk of misuse of funds and unused ERDF funds provided.
Proof of the effectiveness of the projects implemented under the operational programme is the high level of achievement of the set goals, which were supported by the results of the social evaluation of project implementation.
SUMMARY OF CHECK RESULTS
And. Assessment of the management and control system
A coordinated approach enabled the control and control system of the OPPS Czech Republic-POL implemented by the following institutions in both countries: managing authority (Ministry of Local Development of the Czech Republic), national coordinator (Ministry of Local Development POL) and controllers (Center for Regional Development and Voivodeship).
At the same time, the coordinated audit enabled the evaluation of tasks and functions carried out by the Joint Technical Secretariat and the Monitoring Committee.
