During the evaluation of the management system, the inspection focused on the activities carried out in connection with the set-up and performance of the function of the managing authority and the national coordinator, especially in the context of setting the programme's goals and monitoring of progress, evaluation activities and annual reports, evaluation, selection and approval project applications, drawing up program funds and fulfilling the obligation to publish correct, complete and up-to-date information on subsidies, further with the control activities of the managing authority, setting up the performance of the activities and output from the audits of the delegated audit body, and with the reporting and monitoring system of irregularities and compliance with the irregularities monitoring, at the same time it has been verified coordination of tasks and cooperation between institutions involved in the OPPS Czech Republic-POL.
The activities of the competent authorities in the field of risk analysis and the compilation of project monitoring plans were further examined and evaluation of project applications carried out by independent evaluators was assessed.
Verification of the control system included a review of administrative checks and on-the-spot checks, which allowed approval, e.g. supply of goods and co-financed services, eligibility of expenses submitted for reimbursement, while consistency of the payment of such funds and related activities (or parts thereof) with national and EU legislation.
Significant shortcomings have been identified by NKÚ control in the area of publishing correct, complete and up-to-date information on subsidies provided.
In the area of evaluation and approval of projects, the risk of non-transparentness of the process was identified.
Other shortcomings were identified in the area of monitoring indicators settings and in the settings of irregularity reporting system.
Based on these findings, the Supreme Supervisory Authority evaluated the control and management system implemented by the managing authority as partially effective.
Irregularities identified by NIK regarding the functioning of the management and control system in Poland in relation to violations of applicable laws and rules were not considered significant.
These irregularities only affected individual projects and did not have a significant impact on the implementation of the whole OPPS Czech Republic-POL.
Despite identified irregularities, NIK evaluated the functioning of the system positively.
B. Assessment of project results
The check did not show a contradiction between indicators and targets set for individual projects and those defined by the operational programme.
Expected results were achieved in all projects, funded activities were implemented and the indicators (measurable parameters) set out in the project applications of the operational programme were met.
The check conclusions are in line with the result of the survey of the social evaluation of projects described below in the text.
An important aspect that NKÚ and NIK have given attention to in their conclusions is the limited possibility of objective evaluation of the project's performance with regard to project goals and at the same time to the aims of the entire operational programme.
The Supreme Supervisory Chamber initiative took place in the summer of 2013 at the place of implementation of projects selected for the common control sample.
The survey and evaluation was carried out by the School of Higher Vocational Training in Nyse (Poland).
After agreement with the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the investigation was carried out on both sides of the border between 2 820 respondents, both with the public in Poland in relation to part of the project implemented by Polish project partners and with the Czech public in relation to the part of the project implemented in Czech Republic.
The survey mainly covered the suitability, quality, exchange of information, use of funds and social function of projects including investments made.
The number of respondents for each project is shown in Annex 2.
The survey response assessment suggested that the overall social evaluation of projects was good and reached a 4,8 point (on a scale with a maximum of 8 points), which means that the project results were positively perceived by most respondents both in terms of goals and according to other parameters specified in project applications.
According to respondents, the projects examined met the criteria expressed in the operational programme.
Respondents also noticed the positive impact of investments on improving the quality of transport and tourist infrastructure, accessibility, tourist attractiveness, business conditions, quality of life of citizens and renewal of contacts between residents of the border region.
On the other hand, the overall evaluation of the answers suggested a certain difference between the actual level of achievement of the goals / parameters (actual impact rate) and the expected respondents.
This difference applies to evaluation of the results of individual projects, where in some cases there is a significant difference.
The results of the survey were in line with the views of participants in panel discussions (target groups) conducted in the context of the NIK control on the Polish side, who highlighted the need for project implementation and confirmed their positive acceptance by the public and the expected results.
C. Assessment of the legality of controlled projects
The beneficiaries of the aid examined the consistency of the factual and time implementation of the project schedule and the content of the project application, further examination of the achievement of the set goals and purpose of the project, fulfilment of binding monitoring indicators, management of changes in projects, management of possible project revenue, fulfilment of the obligation separated project accounting records transaction, compliance with the ban on financing projects from other EU sources, implementation of project partnerships and compliance with its conditions, fulfilment of compulsory publicity regarding in particular the spread of awareness of sources of financing projects from the EU, compliance with the conditions of eligibility of project expenditure, selection of suppliers and verification of suppliers delivered on the basis of public awarded orders.
The total financial value of the shortcomings of qualified NKÚ and NIK as unfit for funding from EU funds was found at 094 85
However, this amount did not exceed the specified level of importance related to the total controlled amount of funds for sample projects.
Despite the discrepancies identified, NKÚ and NIK evaluated the implementation of selected projects positively.
In most cases, the commitments resulting from the conditions of the aid were properly fulfilled by the beneficiary.
Funds intended for the implementation of controlled projects were spent in accordance with EU regulations and national law.
Nonetheless, seven of the eight beneficiaries of the aid controlled by NIK were found to be inconsistencies in the fulfilment of factual and financial commitments.
These were individual cases of non-systemic nature and were concerned especially inconsistent preparation of project documentation and violation of public procurement rules, but did not affect the selection of contractors or supply of contracted works.
Only in one of all projects controlled by NIK can the discrepancies detected as an unfit spending of PLN 43 003 of which was financed by z 8 ERDF).
On the other hand of the border, the NKÚ identified in three of the 19 controlled projects ineligible spending of CZK 2 098 (of which 863 76 financed by the ERDF).
Irregularities included non-delivery of paid material and works or expenses for modernizing property owned by a person who had no connection to the project or as a beneficiary of the aid or as a project partner.
RECOMMENDATIONS
Joint recommendation of the NKÚ and NIK concerns the improvement of the monitoring system especially with regard to the consistent determination of proper monitoring indicators for all specific objectives of the priority axis of the operational programme.
In general, it is also necessary to aim to identify such indicators at program level and projects to enable more reliable verification of the performance of the established impacts.
Notes and recommendations resulting from checks carried out on both sides of the border are included in separate check conclusions of NKÚ and NIK on CD.
COMMUNICS
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and Polish languages and signed by presidents of the highest inspection institutions of the Czech Republic and the Polish Republic.
Procurement of public works contracts and corruption prevention
Joint report on parallel control carried out by the Czech Supreme Supervisory Authority (NKÚ) and the German Federal Court of Auditors (BRH)
Introduction and overview
Procurement of public procurement for goods and services by contracting authorities is very important for both the state and private sphere.
The role of the state is to use public resources in the most efficient and economical way possible and ensure fair and regulated free competition.
In the European Union (EU) public procurement is a key factor for the success of the single economic space.
The EU has set limits in its regulations, where the contracting authority must meet certain requirements to guarantee a wide and unlimited competitive environment across the EU.
EU Member States therefore need to transpose the European procurement right into their national rules and put it into practice.
The Czech Republic and Germany have already done so.
For public procurement that is value below EU limits, regulation of their award remains within the scope of individual countries.
Moreover, public procurement is prone to corruption with subsequent high potential of damage.
Therefore, contracting entities are obliged to take reasonable measures in their procurement procedures to prevent corruption and incorrect advantage (corruption prevention).
In January 2011, the Supreme Supervisory Authority of the Czech Republic (Czech SAI - NKÚ) and the Federal Court of Auditors of Germany (German SAI - BRH) agreed to carry out parallel checks in the field of procurement procedures and prevention of corruption in land and transport buildings.
Cooperation was also focused on the area of European procurement law as it was transposed into national legislation.
The checks included procurement below European limits to affect corruption prevention.
The control findings of the two top control institutions are summarized in a joint report, which is addressed, among other things, to international organisations such as the International Organization of Highest Supervisory Institutions (INTOSAI).
Control areas and controlled institutions
The BRH assessment is based on the area checks of the above mentioned areas, which were carried out on German construction administrations responsible for federal transport and ground buildings between 2011 and 2012.
For example, highway construction and large-scale projects of ground construction were evaluated.
BRH included findings from past checks in the evaluation.
The NKÚ evaluation is based on checks carried out between 2008 and 2012, which focused on the construction of roads, railway lines, water projects, large buildings (hospitals, cultural facilities, universities) and some other buildings in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the award of federal public procurement is mostly carried out by regional construction administrations.
In the Czech Republic, the state institution for road and rail construction is responsible for the award of public transport infrastructure contracts.
In the field of ground construction, public procurement is carried out by beneficiaries of budgetary resources.
In both countries, external experts services are also used in individual procurement stages.
The evaluation must take into account differences in legislation on public procurement and the specialities of the construction market in both countries.
The structure of the public procurement law in both countries
In Germany, the process of European procurement procedures is governed by laws and regulations.
The procurement procedure limited to Germany is governed by budgetary law and relevant administrative acts.
Internal administrative rules contain numerous additional provisions for both European and national procurement procedures.
Further details regarding the requirements of European procurement law and corruption prevention are enshrined in the so-called. federal government procurement manuals where requirements are divorced or formulated into greater detail with regard to legal precedents in the field of procurement law.
In the Czech Republic, public procurement is governed by the public procurement law and other legislation concerning contracts with value above and below European limits.
The procurement right made substantial changes in 2012
The new rules strengthened the transparency of procurement procedures, opened room for more competition and reduced corruption opportunities during the procurement procedure.
Fundamental aspects of procurement in both countries
As regards European procurement procedures, open and narrower procedures must be applied in both countries.
In Germany, contracts below the European limit are awarded in accordance with national rules (public call for competition, limited call for participation, negotiated procedure), but these are virtually identical to the abovementioned conditions for European procurement procedures.
Public procurement in Germany is characterized by the principle of preference for open proceedings (where interested in European scale are invited) and public calls for participation (only in the case of national proceedings).
In open proceedings and in the invitation to participate in the competition, any interested person can submit an offer.
Another significant sign of German procurement law is the support of small and medium-sized companies.
This is mainly achieved by dividing the total public contract into commercially specific parts and by dividing into partial contracts.
Procurement of contracts divided into these parts gives the opportunity to participate in the proceedings as many candidates as possible.
The two characteristics of German procurement law are time-proven tools to gain good value for money.
More than 330 construction companies with 1,9 million employees are registered in Germany.
In the Czech Republic it is necessary to apply the conditions of European proceedings even in cases of public procurement with value below the EU limit.
The exception is a simplified sublimit procedure, where the contracting authority can use less demanding procedures.
In accordance with European law, Czech procurement law includes conditions under which the contract must be awarded in order to ensure competition and achieve a bargain price.
Current Czech legislation allows contracting entities to choose between open procedure and narrower procedures.
85 construction companies registered in the Czech Republic, of which about 1 have 20 employees.
Total volume of contracting entities for public works and the share of different types of proceedings in both countries
In 2011 the total volume of construction works in Germany amounted to 7 675 billion.
Kč, of which 1 138 billion. Kč (15 %) was the share of public procurement, which included contracts awarded by individual spolkovými and municipalities in addition to contracts awarded by the Federal Government.
The total volume of projects of the Federal Road and Land Construction (without railway and water buildings) reached 212,5 billion...
In 2011, the composition of the Federal Procurement of Land Construction and Transport Construction was as follows: 80,7 % open proceedings and public calls; 12,7 % closer proceedings and narrower calls;
6,6 % negotiated procedure and direct procurement; 33,2 % is the share of European procurement procedures.
The volume of public construction contracts in the Czech Republic reached 118,6 billion in 2011 Kč, which was about 25 % of the total volume of all construction works.
In 2009 it reached 194,0 billion. Kč, which was 37 % of the total volume.
Structure of procurement types in 2011: 65,1 % open procedures; 14,3 % narrower procedures; 9,5 % negotiated procedures; 8,4 % simplified procedures for sublimit contracts; 2,7 % other procedures.
The data included all public supply contracts, services and works contracts awarded by contracting authorities in 2011.
The mentioned figures show that: parallel checks in both countries focused on a substantial part of public procurement procedures; prevention of corruption to be held still has a significant financial impact; open meaning. procurement procedures are crucial.
Summary of main results
NKÚ and BRH performed parallel checks on the award of European works contracts with an emphasis on corruption prevention in their countries.
The checks were aimed at comparing legislation in both countries and the EU and the implementation of public procurement in the field of land and transport buildings.
Key findings below are:
EU public procurement directive has been transposed into national rights of both countries (points 1. and 3.1).
The prevention of corruption is not only the aim of the EU directive, but the national procurement rules of both countries, which differ in part in the focus and in the details.
In both countries, the essential requirement for the contract documentation to meet is the inclusion of all information needed for the preparation of tenders.
Specifications must be neutral and must contain no requirements limiting competition.
The specification documentation in Germany meets these requirements.
In the Czech Republic, the problem is insufficient definition of the subject matter of the contract.
In Germany, division of contracts is required into parts where possible to support a competitive environment.
According to the findings of BRH, this requirement is observed in Germany.
NKÚ checks showed that in the Czech Republic large public works in the area of road buildings are awarded without being divided into parts or divided, but only on volume very significant parts. This method can distort competition and lead to restrictions on only a few large companies.
These restrictions on market potential can result in significant cost increases and incur a risk of non-serious price negotiation and inadmissible conventions.
Legislation in both countries allows contracting entities to supplement additional construction work under certain conditions if this need arises only after the contract is concluded (paragraph 4.1).
In both countries the requirements for proper designation of the type of procurement procedure are met.
In the Czech Republic, contracting entities can identify one of the open procurement procedures, open proceedings or closer procedures according to the applicable rules.
German rules in procurement and budgetary law enshrine the priority of open procedures for both European tenders and national, known as public calls for competition.
Open procurement procedures in both countries allow a larger range of candidates to submit an offer and also reduce the risk of corruption, because they make unlawful price negotiation among candidates difficult.
At the same time, the best results in value for money are achieved.
In the case of large procurement, whose expected total price exceeds or exceeds the limits laid down by the EU, controlled contracting entities have always written a European procurement procedure.
In determining the type of procurement procedure, correct determination of the expected value of the contract plays a very important role.
In Germany, databases are used to determine the price of public works, where the values are based on completed construction projects.
This is an objective enough tool.
In the Czech Republic, databases are used only in the area of road construction, but are not yet an effective tool (paragraph 4.2).
Preliminary information and notice of the opening of the procurement procedure must be published in accordance with European procurement procedures, due to strengthening competition by allowing candidates to prepare in time for submission of tenders.
As a rule, the construction authorities audited with this requirement.
In isolated cases, errors in the information released, incorrect application of provisions and / or a lack of controls may have impaired competition (item 4.3).
There is a greater risk of manipulation when selecting candidates to participate in a closer procurement procedure.
According to EU law, the number of candidates invited must be high enough to guarantee real competition.
The selection criteria must be objective, non-discriminatory and be published in advance.
Beyond the EU requirements, contracting entities in both countries should rotate as often as possible, who call for participation in the proceedings when selecting suppliers.
In Germany there are partly very detailed requirements for preventing the risks of manipulation.
In some cases, controlled contracting authorities did not follow these requirements.
In the Czech Republic, selection decisions were not always credible (paragraph 4.4).
In both countries, contracting entities must ensure that all candidates wishing to submit a tender receive the same information.
Any agreements between these candidates and between them and third parties involved in the preparation of specifications must be prevented to the extent possible from limiting competition through illegal agreements.
In Germany, the relevant measures are more thorough than in the Czech Republic.
However, the controlled German contracting authorities did not meet the said requirement in several cases (paragraph 4.5).
The principle of cross control and transparency must be applied in both countries when opening envelopes.
Labelling requirements, documentation, protection and confidentiality of offers are supposed to restrict the space for manipulation and are especially detailed in Germany.
Checks in both countries found only a few cases of irregularities (point 4.6).
Assessment and evaluation of tenders is procedurally regulated in both countries.
The relevant German measures are more complex, but have not always been respected by controlled contracting entities.
For example, contracting entities handed over their bids to third parties for consultation without properly documenting any suspicious circumstances.
The tenders were thus insufficiently protected against subsequent manipulations (paragraph 4.7).
Participants must be informed about the intended award of the contract before the latter is finalised due to legal protection of enterprises are to be informed about the intended contract award.
This legal protection rule also is designed to prevent corruption action.
The law of the Czech Republic provides for judicial review of contract award procedures also for national tenders.
Only in few cases, the notification of the enterprises was not appropriately ensured (item 4.8).
Procurement documentation was not always complete or completely credible for controlled contracting entities in both countries.
In case of several procurement procedures, the transparency requirements applied at European level were not always adequately observed in the proceedings.
In addition, some found deficiencies decreased the preventive anti-corruption function of documentation.
Contracting entities in both countries mostly fulfilled their notification duties (point 4.9).
Summary of the main principles of European procurement law and corruption prevention
European procurement law
The European Parliament and the Council of the European Union have adopted, inter alia, a directive on the coordination of procedures for the award of public works contracts, supply and services in order to ensure the free movement of goods and services and a directive on the coordination of laws, regulations and administrative provisions relating to review procedures on the award of public supply contracts and public works contracts (review directive), with these two directives being transposed into national law.
The EU general procurement principles include in particular: a requirement for a competitive environment; a requirement for equal treatment or a discrimination; a requirement for transparency.
EU procurement principles include the directive on the coordination of procedures for public procurement includes provisions on construction projects whose total expected value is or exceeds 5 miles. €.
These clauses affect: Content documentation content; type of procurement used; publication of certain information before, during and after the end of the procedure; compliance with the deadline for acceptance of tenders; qualifying requirements that may be required of tenderers; criteria for the selection of the most suitable offer.
The legal protection of applicants follows the review proceedings directive.
In the event of a potential breach of the procurement law, tenderers may have the contracting authority reviewed according to review procedures.
Both countries transposed EU requirements into national legislation.
Prevention of corruption
The importance of prevention of corruption
There is no legal definition in any of both countries what corruption actually means.
In general, corruption is seen as an abuse of a personal (confidential) position in its own favor.
Usually this means that such abuse is incited by persons who gain benefit.
Corruption can be an obstacle to competition and can cause serious economic losses.
According to estimates, the total corruption related damage accounts for 5 % of the world's economic performance.
For the EU area, these costs are estimated at 1 % of the EU's economic performance.
If a contracting authority is involved in the contract, conventions limiting competition or allowing dishonest conduct can weaken confidence in integrity, ability and overall work of public administration.
Therefore, prevention of corruption is an essential task of contracting entities.
Practice and procedures must be controlled especially in areas particularly prone to corruption in order to allow adequate measures to prevent it.
Taking preventive measures and carrying out effective checks can significantly reduce the susceptibility of the decision-making process to corruption.
Procurement of works contracts is usually considered to be particularly prone to corruption.
Corruption prevention measures
In Germany, corruption is prosecutable under criminal and labour law, which concerns active and passive bribery, accepting and offering significant benefits.
The German Federal Government has issued a manual with recommendations on the prevention of corruption in the federal administration and according to which the following principles are applied throughout the procurement process outside the risk analysis: priority of open procurement; principle of multiple control and transparent decision making; division of planning, procurement and accounting phase; accurate and complete documentation of the procurement procedure.
Moreover, other measures with preventive influence against corruption became part of the procurement law.
In 2011, the relevant Federal Ministry of Information Technology established a system for monitoring contract for construction of federal roads.
Using this system, data such as estimated costs, total value of the contract and the involvement of private projections offices can be fully recorded and analyzed to detect possible irregularities.
In the Czech Republic, corruption is prosecuted under criminal law, the level of employment or civil law is also considered.
Legal requirement for transparency, equal treatment and no discrimination throughout the procurement process (preparation and implementation) is the most important part of corruption prevention.
Anti-corruption measures in this area were established by the government in the ′′ Government's strategy to fight corruption for the period 2011 to 2012 ′′ updated for 2013 and 2014.
Part of the said measures were incorporated into the public procurement law and follow-up implementing regulations.
New legislation contains the following basic provisions: lowering limits for small-scale contracts; obligation to prior notice by the contracting authority including justification of the contract; prohibition to limit the number of tenderers in a narrower procedure and cancellation of the general possibility to limit the number of tenderers by drawing; obligation to publish contracts including attachments; obligation to publish actual and lists of subcontractors I'm sorry.
Results of checks related to subsequent stages of the procurement procedure
Procurement documentation
The procurement documentation must contain all the information needed to allow applicants to prepare their tenders in an appropriate form.
In particular, the documentation must allow the offer price to be processed.
In order to do this, applicants must not be exposed to risks they could not expect.
The specification of the contract documentation contains mainly specifications, and the requirements to demonstrate candidate s' qualifications and the criteria for choosing the best bid.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
European law contains in particular requirements regarding technical specifications.
Specifications must limit competition to the least possible extent and all interested parties must have equal access to it.
Specifications must be neutral.
Requirements for specific products are allowed on a very limited scale in the procurement documentation.
The basic principle of prevention of corruption is that the procurement documentation does not contain requirements that could restrict competition.
Documentation should further avoid ambiguity or inaccurate data that create room for speculation and manipulation during the evaluation of offers.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries transposed EU legal provisions into their national legislation.
The basic principle is that the specifications be given in general without reference to a particular product or brand.
Specifications must define the required supplies and services accurately and indicate in detail the number of units of work and supply.
In normal cases prices should be reported according to units of work or supply (e.g. in CZK / m or CZK / item).
Defining the required work in terms of their functionality is only acceptable in exceptional cases.
Basically, the rule is that the specifications need to be prepared completely and unequivocally.
They must contain accurate amounts and must not include work and deliveries, the necessity of which is not quite obvious.
Payment in the form of flat-rate amounts or according to the time worked must be avoided wherever possible.
These parts of the procurement documentation must exclude speculation and manipulation based on ambiguous specifications.
Specifications must allow each candidate to prepare their offer with certainty and without excessive preparatory work.
The invitation to tender must be published only when the procurement documentation is complete.
Different clauses
In the Czech Republic, there is no obligation for contractors to award construction contracts in parts.
The contracting authority may divide the contract into several separate parts, provided that the nature of the subject matter of such a contract.
In Germany, the application of the rule to divide works into parts, either quantitatively (partial supply) or according to special aspects (specialized parts of the contract).
This allows small and medium-sized entities to participate in the competition, increases the number of potential applicants and makes price fixation difficult.
This type of assignment is usually considered the most appropriate in terms of providing value for money.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement documents must contain evaluation criteria for national and European procurement procedures.
This should inform the candidate in a comprehensive and exhaustive manner of the criteria according to which his offer will be evaluated.
In Germany, the requirement for evaluation criteria in the notification applies only to European calls for tender.
In national procurement procedures it is necessary to include evaluation criteria only in the contract record, which is an internal administrative document.
If the contract documentation is prepared by authorized independent experts, German regulations require any information from it to help identify specific interested companies, architects or designers.
The reason is to prevent individual construction companies from acquiring any additional information or other inadmissible competitive advantages without the knowledge of the contracting authority.
This is also why independent experts are not allowed to publish documents regarding tenders and allow their accessibility for verification.
The contracting authority is the only focal point for construction companies.
The Czech Republic currently does not have a similar provision.
In the case of large construction projects, after the original contract is concluded, there will almost always be a need for more work or modification of existing works.
Legislative of both countries allows a multi-work contract to a certain limit to the same supplier without publishing and implementing a new procurement procedure.
The volume of multiple work under European and German legislation must not exceed 50 % of the original value of the contract.
In addition, more work must be necessary and must have the nature of a special component of the main contract.
In the Czech Republic, a stricter limit of 20 % is applied to the assignment of multiple work.
This can bring the risk of more time delay in the execution of the contract and possible integration of a new entity into an already running project.
If a multi-work contract is awarded to the supplier of the original contract, German law contains a provision that prevents suppliers from arbitrary increase in the price of modified works or multiple works.
Calculations must be made taking into account prices negotiated in the original contract.
In addition to multiple works, less work can occur during construction, i.e. jobs that were not needed.
Less work and more work cannot be compensated in the Czech Republic.
Main inspection findings
BHR
Technical specifications and product neutral invitation to bid
In rare cases, the specifications were referring to national technical requirements or standards, but were replaced by EU standards in the meantime.
In some cases the specifications included data demanding a certain brand, e.g. for the system of resilience of public inscriptions, to prevent water breach or for noise tiling, although it was not necessary.
In some cases the specifications were so detailed that only one product met the requirements.
Quantitative specifications divided into items
BRH has not observed a disagreement with the general requirements for the invitation to tender for supply and services according to the quantitative specifications divided into items.
Complete of the specifications
In most cases controlled, tendering documents were prepared without the rest before the invitation to tender was announced.
However, in various cases, documents during the procurement procedure had to be modified when changes in items or timetable had to be taken into account.
In rare cases, the contract documents contained work and deliveries needed insecure.
One procurement documentation for demolition work contained almost exclusively such items.
Dividing the contract and award criteria
In many cases, the desired justification for not to divide the supply into parts has not been demonstrated.
The criteria for evaluating tenders before the contract award, BRH found no shortcomings.
Inclusion of names of authorized independent experts
In many documents, interested authorized experts were presented.
Names were listed on the opening pages of documents or on plans or attached opinions.
In one case, the contracting authority even urged tenderers to contact an explicitly named architect with their procurement questions.
These cases were found mainly in procurement documentation, where self-employed experts were entrusted with the processing of the specifications.
Contracting authorities stated that they did not have sufficient staff capacity to check the procurement documents in detail.
NKÚ
Technical specifications and product neutral invitation to bid
In the case of a public contract to build a house with 12 apartments, there was a link directly to specific manufacturers and brands of products.
The contracting authority has not allowed the use of other similar product types or justified why it calls for the delivery of specific products.
For the construction of the university facility, the procurement documentation contained links to specific business companies and specific product designations.
Overview of the specifications and sub-specifications
For the construction of certain industrial zones, the contracting authority did not clearly define the quantity and type of required works, supplies or services in the statement and established only the built-in space in cubic meters for each building as a unit.
Complete of the specifications
During the procurement procedure for the construction of the road circuit, the procurement documentation for closer proceedings was changed four times from August to September 2009
The reason was the changes in project documentation caused by extension of the scope of the contract and by changing technical conditions.
For the construction of social objects, the procurement documentation had defects, which forced the creation of multiple work (precise focus was missing, sufficient construction research was not done, drawings were missing).
The contract documentation for the construction of a large library stated interior elements only descriptively, without specification of quality product requirements.
Delivery of the interior of the building was provided by subcontractors, who bought some superior and very expensive equipment.
Parts and criteria for awarding the contract
In the Czech Republic there is no obligation to award a contract in parts.
Analysis of three large road buildings during the construction of the road circuit showed that savings of up to 790 miles were possible when they were awarded in open proceedings (separately after selected objects). Kč from the price of public procurement achieved 15 508 miles...
For example, six building objects as a separate part of the public contract could have been a savings of 62,5 miles.
Kč, i.e. 25 % of the contrasted price and 20 bridges as a separate part of the public contract could have been a savings of 287,8 miles. Kč, i.e. also 25 %.
The contracting authority established qualification criteria during the construction of road roads in the procurement documentation, which restricted the participation of small suppliers in the procurement procedure.
In the contract conditions of open procedure for the contractor at one highway construction construction, the contracting authority requested, inter alia. contractor's practice consisting of the implementation of at least three road buildings with a financial volume of more than 700 miles each. Kč, completed or working in the last five years.
There are only nine companies in the Czech Republic that meet the condition of completion of buildings over 700 miles. Kč in the last five years.
The public contract for the supply of another highway construction in an open procedure included six separate buildings, for which the contracting authority requested a minimum annual volume of construction works in the last three years of 12 billion.
Two thirds of financial volume of road construction works (i.e. i.e. 2.5 billion out of of 3.7 billion) in the period of 2008-2009 were realized by 5 suppliers or individually either in form of consortium.
For 46 orders for a total of 13,2 billion. Kč there were only two or even one candidate.
NKÚ pointed out that reducing market potential can lead to a huge increase in costs.
Multiple work area
In two cases, the contracting authority did not enter into a written contract for the delivery of multiple works of construction and did not enter into any of the procedures laid down in the law during the construction of the road circuit.
The value of pre-approved multiple work in one case was 1 591,4 miles. Kč without VAT (increase by 21 %) and in the second case 4 135,8 miles. Kč without VAT (increase of 91 %).
The cause of multiple work was primarily ambiguous definition of the quantity and type of work required.
For the construction of a university facility, the contracting authority did not include some work and supplies in the procurement documentation, which it already knew about the necessity for completion and housewarming of the construction.
For these works and supplies, he made additions to the work contract with the construction contractor with the price increase, in the negotiated procedure without publication, although the volume of multiple works exceeded the national limit of 20 % of the original contract value.
In connection with the construction of the court palace, the contracting authority reserves the right to enter additional works without procurement.
During construction, the contracting authority increased the scope of the contract by 50,5 miles...
Unit prices of additional work established without competition were significantly higher than comparable works performed by the same supplier.
Other findings
NKÚ on a selected sample of buildings found that the average construction cost of building one kilometer of a four-current highway in the Czech Republic is 355,0 miles...
According to long-term data obtained from the German Ministry of Construction, the average cost in Germany per kilometer section of the four-current highway is 260,0 miles...
This comparison suggests that buying a highway in the Czech Republic is more expensive than in Germany.
Summary
The legal provisions regarding the procurement documentation are almost identical in both countries and are in accordance with the requirements of European law.
The goal is to ensure complete and straight competition and prevention of corruption.
Specifications must be accurate enough to allow candidates to calculate costs and prepare their offers.
Moreover, this requirement restricts space for speculation and the contracting authority is protected against the need to assign more work.
In Germany, the basic legal provisions on procurement documentation are complemented by other rules to reduce the possibilities for limiting competition and for manipulation.
Although there are no detailed requirements of this type in the Czech Republic, there is greater transparency achieved by publishing the award criteria.
In both countries, the specification requirements are mostly met.
However, in some cases, weaknesses have been identified that could lead to a reduction in competition.
The current rule in Germany demanding the division of large construction projects into parts seems suitable for strengthening the competitive environment and achieving cost-effective results.
NKÚ found that in the Czech Republic, the award of contracts for large-scale projects without awarding parts or dividing into a large part of the volume of interested parties can limit a small number of large suppliers to small number of large suppliers.
The result of the strict requirement for references of applicants, which is applied in the Czech Republic for the selection of road works applicants, is that public contracts are awarded only to a small circle of tenderers, so small and medium-sized companies do not have a chance to compete.
A limited number of applicants also increases the risk of price fixation and other illegal conventions.
Regulatory approaches are different in both countries with regard to the award of additional contracts for multi-work or modified work.
If the value of additional works under European and German law does not exceed 50 % of the value of the original contract, the multi-work may be awarded without a procurement procedure and its notice.
The stricter limit of 20 % applies in the Czech Republic.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
This limit is often exceeded by the contracting authority.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If the 20 % limit is exceeded, multiple work must be awarded on the basis of a new procurement procedure.
By dividing the work into part, it is possible to avoid limiting competition and subsequent unfortunate consequences.
Determination of the type of procurement procedure with regard to EU limits
By determining the type of procurement procedure, the contracting authority defines a circle of potential suppliers who will be allowed into the competition.
The contracting authority may leave the scope of potential suppliers unlimited, or it may limit the scope according to the specified criteria.
In case of large project works whose value exceeds or exceeds the limits established by the EU, a European procurement procedure must be conducted.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
When choosing a type of procedure, the contracting authority must meet, in particular, the requirements of European law regarding competitive environment and transparency.
If the estimate of the total cost of the contract for the required works exceeds or exceeds the current EU limit of 5,0 miles. € (125 miles. Kč), open or limited procurement procedure at European level is always required.
In exceptional cases, negotiated procedure or competition dialogue is allowed.
If the construction project reaches the EU limit, the contracting authority may, to a limited extent, deviate from the European procurement procedure by issuing national proceedings if the total value of the relevant part is below 1,0 miles. € (25 miles. Kč) and the total value of all parts does not exceed 20 % of the value of the whole contract.
Dividing a construction project or intentionally estimating its costs too low with the intention of avoiding the fundamental obligation to write a European procurement procedure is not acceptable.
Choosing a type of management is very important for the prevention of corruption, because limiting competition significantly increases the risk of manipulation.
Therefore, an important part of the procurement documentation is a detailed justification of the chosen type of procedure, especially in relation to the application of the European procurement law.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries implemented EU legal requirements for procurement procedures and limits to their national legislation.
Different clauses
The Czech Republic has introduced the principle of equal validity of open and narrower procedures and national procurement procedures.
Open and narrower proceedings can always be chosen, while other types of proceedings are allowed only when the conditions laid down are met.
Unlike the Czech amendment, the relevant German regime of budgetary law and the principle of corruption prevention prefers open proceedings or a public call for participation in proceedings.
Other types of proceedings including limited management are only exceptionally permitted if legislation permits.
Such exceptions must be justified and documented.
The principle of preference for open proceedings is intended to guarantee that competition restrictions are prevented to the maximum extent and that the opportunity for manipulation (pre-selected specific candidates) is limited.
In Germany, this principle of procurement is the central point of prevention of corruption.
Proper estimate of the expected price of the contract is an important basis for a decision on the corresponding type of procurement procedure.
When estimating the costs of ground construction projects, contracting entities in Germany can rely on budgetary and cost databases of public administrations and other organizations.
These were built on the basis of analysis of completed construction projects and include, among other things, standard cost values for types of buildings, construction units, parts and partial works.
Based on such standard cost values, it is possible to estimate the value of the planned project or construction works contract.
Only a few construction administrations in Germany already have a similar database for road construction.
However, the database is expected to be expanded at national level.
Contracting entities in the Czech Republic do not use any central database or average prices of comparable objects to determine the expected costs of public land construction contracts.
In many cases, cost determinations are based on estimation of the project-financing entity or based on the value of the resources available to this entity.
Standardization measures are in the early stages.
Based on the anti-corruption program for the period 2011 to 2012, the relevant Ministries are supposed to develop a database of the usual prices of standardized commodities.
The use of the price system for determining the expected price of the contract is determined by a new regulation ordering the subject line to the contract in detail.
The price system should serve as a set of information on construction and installation works, materials and products and other data to calculate the necessary costs and to determine unit prices.
The Ministry of Transport has issued regulatory prices for traffic buildings to check them, which are regularly updated.
The database is designed to determine the price of the project (investment) plan and should play comparative function in the next stages of construction work preparation.
Main inspection findings BRH
Selection of procurement procedure
Controlled contracting entities generally awarded contracts in an open procedure or in the form of a public call for participation, thus complying with the requirements of budgetary and procurement legislation.
In 2011, the share of tenders in the total volume of federal construction projects in the field of ground construction was 59,5 %.
This share was 94,8 % in road construction.
BRH found that in some cases the use of non-public competition was not sufficiently justified.
In the case of an area inspection, BRH found, based on information collected from more than 16 000 proceedings, that limited management has a clear disadvantage compared to public management and public challenge and limited management also increase the risk of manipulation and corruption.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
According to the BRH study, tenders in limited proceedings and negotiated procedures were between 6 % and 10 % higher than in public procedures.
Parallel studies by the Ministry of Construction and the Land Control Court confirmed differences in value for money received in public and limited proceedings.
A study by the Ministry of Construction even found that prices in limited proceedings were twice the prices in public proceedings.
Compliance with EU limits
For projects whose total value of the contract was estimated to be more than 5 miles. € (125 miles. Kč), controlled contracting entities usually prepared procurement plans stating which works will be awarded in the European procurement procedure and which in the national procedure.
According to the procurement plans, the share of work awarded under European rules exceeded 80 % of the total work.
No case of circumvention of the European management requirement in the form of an overrun low cost estimate has been observed.
However, in some cases, the minimum percentage for pan-European management was not achieved due to a calculation error.
During the course of the work some contracting entities have illegally changed the contract award plan.
These changes did not justify and demonstrate that the minimum share of European management was subsequently observed.
The share of European management according to project accounts was generally lower than the share set out in the procurement plan.
If the expected value of construction projects contracts exceeded the European limits, contracting entities did not apply European proceedings to all individual parts worth more than 1 miles. € (25 miles..).
Instead, they awarded the relevant contracts on the basis of national proceedings without giving compelling reasons for the need for a derogation from the requirement.
NKÚ
Selection of the type of procurement procedure
For several large construction projects (e.g. construction of a road section, facilities for a large sporting event and housing construction) the contracting authority divided one project into several parts, although these partial contracts were of the same or similar character.
The division decreased the expected value of the contract and the contract was awarded under a less demanding regime or even outside the law regime.
Methods for calculating the expected price
Price standards applicable to road construction projects have not yet been an effective tool for determining the expected price.
They were based on the prices shown in final proceedings, but were burdened by non-economic and excessive suppliers.
NKÚ found that the actual prices for three parts of the road circuit were about 37 % lower than these price normatives.
The Ministry of Transport is supposed to update normatives in relation not only to past prices, but also compared to other comparable markets and price developments.
For ground buildings, the expected price was based on the project budget performed by architects or an investor estimation.
The actual price was then significantly different from the expected price.
The expected price of the construction of a large library was twice higher compared to the contract price, but increased by 54 miles during the implementation. Kč, i.e. by 27 %.
Similarly, for the construction of the depositary of this library, the contract price was 33 % lower than the expected price.
In other cases, the price of the successful applicant was higher than the expected price and increased even during the implementation.
The construction of a large library was 400 miles. Kč, i.e. by 22 %. For the construction of the judicial palace, the actual price increased disproportionately (by 139 %) compared to the increase in functional areas (only 12 %).
Summary
Both countries implemented European rules on the choice of procurement type and respecting European limits to their national legislation, so the relevant national adjustments of both countries are almost identical.
The principle of public proceedings in Germany is, however, stricter than the European regulation and the current national regulation in the Czech Republic.
Compared to the narrower procurement procedure, the public procedure or the public call for participation of more competitors to participate in the procurement procedure.
These types of procurement procedures generate a large number of tenders that guarantee the best value effect for money.
The prevention of corruption is significantly strengthened, as the circle of candidates is not limited by decisions taken by the contracting authority, which gives room for manipulation and price fixation among tenderers.
The study confirmed the benefits of the German provision on the preference of open proceedings or public calls for participation.
Czech legislation allows contracting entities to award contracts in open or narrower proceedings.
However, the latest regulation of the public procurement law imposes a ban for contracting authorities to restrict the number of tenderers in narrower proceedings.
The narrower procedure has now become very close to the open procedure.
In Germany, the contracting authority is largely fulfilled the requirement of a preference for open proceedings or a public invitation to participate in the competition, while in the Czech Republic some projects were divided against the law, in order to circumvent the requirement to select the type of procurement procedure.
However, in the case of some projects implemented in Germany, the European limits were not respected, which resulted in a minimum share in pan-European proceedings.
A satisfactory system has not yet been introduced in the Czech Republic to facilitate the correct calculation of expected costs of construction works and projects.
In cases where on site, contracting entities should ensure through more extensive checks that the requirements for the selection of the type of procurement procedure and the volume of the contracts awarded in European procedures are met or should create the conditions necessary to allow proper calculation of the expected costs I'm sorry.
Preliminary information and notice of initiation
In cases where contracts are awarded under the European procedure, the contracting authority must publish a procurement report.
Preliminary information and procurement notice are an important base for European competition.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
Through preliminary notifications, the contracting authority must state the basic specifications of the projects envisaged.
Preliminary notifications are required for projects for which the total cost estimation is equal to or greater than the European limit and when the contracting authority wishes to shorten the deadline for submitting tenders in individual procurement procedures.
The contracting authority is required to publish a procurement notice with detailed information on all public procurement required by the European procedure.
The information is binding upon the contracting authority after publication.
Among other things, the notice shall contain specifications, time limits for proceedings and for completion of the contract, specific requirements and selection criteria and their weights.
A common vocabulary for public procurement must be used to describe the subject of the contract.
Preliminary information and contract notice are published in the EU in the Official Journal of the EU and on the contracting authority profile.
Due to prevent discrimination against foreign candidates, no national notices should contain any additional information and should not be published before the text of the EU Publications Office is sent.
Incomplete or inaccurate information in preliminary notice may violate competition or even facilitate manipulation.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries fully implemented EU provisions on preliminary information and procurement notices in their national legislation.
Different clauses
In the Czech Republic preliminary information and notice must be published even in the case of contracts for which a European procedure is not required.
The procurement procedure shall not be opened before one month after the preliminary notice has been sent.
Preliminary disclosure may only be waived in exceptional cases.
In Germany preliminary information is not required in cases where European proceedings are not required.
In the case of national proceedings, the public call must be published on the Federal Government's website and, when appropriate, in print.
In case of limited proceedings without competition from participants, the notice must be published if the estimated contract price is equal to or greater than 000 25 (625 thousand..).
Preliminary notifications must explain all planned parts of the project.
This is an important requirement given the amount of small contracts in Germany.
The division of projects into smaller parts is not so common in the Czech Republic and this measure is considered less important.
Main inspection findings
BRH
Preliminary notice
Contracting entities published a preliminary notice of projects, which included work to be awarded in the European procedure.
In some open proceedings they shortened the deadline, although the number of days between sending a preliminary notice and sending a contract notice was less than 52 days.
In the case of other abbreviated proceedings, the annual deadline for preliminary information expired and should be renewed.
In many cases, the preliminary notice did not indicate the projected division of construction works into multiple parts.
Procurement notice
Some of the notifications included codes from the common vocabulary that deviated from the contents of the preliminary notice or precisely specify the work to be carried out.
In rare cases, national notifications included more information, e.g. regarding the dates of fulfillment, or were published before the notice in the Official Journal of the EU.
Ex-ante transparency
One contracting authority hired an external company to publish a national notice.
This published a notice on its platform whose use has been charged.
However, the contracting authority did not check whether the company had to comply with the requirement to send a notification to a free internet government portal.
The sample found that only a third of the notifications were actually published on the government portal.
NKÚ
Procurement notice
During the construction of a waste water treatment plant, the contracting authority did not determine the criteria for reducing the large number of tenders for evaluation procedures in the notice of the construction contractor.
The method of selection (reduction) of tenders for evaluation was not able to prove the contracting authority.
The reduction of the number of offers was made possible by previous legislation.
During the construction of a road circuit, the contracting authority did not define in the notice of initiation of a narrower procedure or in the qualifying documentation of the value according to which it will assess the level of compliance with the qualifying criteria and the number of applicants who will be invited.
The contracting authority evaluated the completion of the qualification by fulfilling it all six candidates in the context of the narrower procedure, but excluded one of them from fulfilling it only in the last sixth place.
The contracting authority's procedure was not transparent because it did not publish information in advance on what will be evaluated from the qualification data and how.
Publishing calls
The contracting authority did not publish a written invitation to submit tenders in the case of construction adjustments in former military újezdech.
Conclusions and recommendations / summary
The two-stage information process with preliminary information and publication of the notice of initiation is an important tool for meeting the requirements for transparency and strengthening the competitive environment applied in European proceedings.
By extending the obligation to publish preliminary information in the Czech Republic also for national procurement procedures and by strengthening this obligation in Germany in cases of limited procedures, both countries increased the transparency of procurement procedures and improved the competitive environment.
Selection of candidates in limited procurement procedures
Compared to the open procedure, limited procurement procedures do not allow participation to all potential interested applicants.
In limited procedures, the contracting authority will first select potential suppliers who will be asked to submit a tender.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
EU provisions allow to limit the number of applicants in European limited procedures.
However, limited proceedings require at least five tenderers to be invited to submit an offer and in case of a negotiated procedure with publication, at least three potential tenderers must be invited.
In any case, the number of challenged applicants must be wide enough to guarantee real competition.
Selection criteria must be objective and non-discriminatory and must be published in advance.
Selecting potential applicants to be challenged is very susceptible to manipulation, e.g. the preference of some of them.
Reducing competition to several applicants can make their secret agreement easier.
This has a negative impact on the outcome of the driving.
Therefore, the contracting authority needs to take measures to prevent manipulation and make sure it has effective control to ensure that the procedure is transparent and credible.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The provisions for selection of applicants are similar in both countries.
In addition to the requirements of the European directive, contracting entities should change tenderers inviting to submit their tender.
It is also not acceptable to restrict competition from a regional point of view.
Contracting entities must document and justify candidate selection and selection process.
Different clauses
In Germany, it is required to invite at least three applicants in case of limited proceedings and several suitable applicants in the case of a negotiated procedure.
Except for two cases, new Czech regulations do not allow the number of applicants to be reached in case of narrower and negotiated proceedings.
In Germany it is necessary to respect the ′′ principle of four eyes ′′ when selecting applicants.
While one worker proposes their list, another has to substantially modify the proposal, e.g. by crossing out the proposed candidate or adding another candidate.
This is supposed to prevent a situation where an individual can definitively define a circle of applicants to participate in the proceedings.
If such a provision is not introduced, a far-reaching illegal agreement between participants is allowed.
The list of tenderers who will be invited to submit a tender must be confidential and must not be disclosed.
This also gives a commitment to authorized independent experts.
There is no similar measure in the Czech Republic, nor a measure for confidential treatment of the list of applicants.
Under German clauses, they must not define candidates for an external company, but they can make suggestions to the contracting authority.
There is no similar requirement in the Czech Republic.
Main inspection findings
BRH
Number of candidates
In addition to several cases, the requirement to address the minimum number of applicants was met.
An analysis of nearly 7 000 national-limit construction assignments showed that in the case of limited proceedings, contracting entities invited an average of 6,6 potential tenderers and in the case of direct negotiation proceedings, an average of 4,4 tenderers.
Change of suppliers and regional restrictions
Contracting entities especially in the area of building buildings did not change the circle of approached applicants because they had good experience with those with whom they worked so far.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Contracting entities argued that in case of non-public proceedings they should guarantee that they would address the tenderers whose suitability they had already assured beforehand.
Although there was no evidence for illegal regional restrictions, the circuit of applicants in the non-public proceedings included a larger part of regional applicants than in the case of public proceedings.
Contracting authorities explained this the low level of the contract compared to public management and high cost of travel for potential tenderers.
The principle of cross-check and design of self-employed experts
Contracting entities mostly ignored the obligation to change the list of tenderers proposed by self-employed professionals.
They argued especially with lack of staff, time pressure or inappropriate knowledge of a suitable candidate.
In many cases, it was not evident from the records who suggested the candidate who was asked to participate in the proceedings.
Checking some samples showed that the list of potential applicants was created by self-employed professionals and the contracting authority was accepted unchanged.
Thus, contracting entities did not adequately protect themselves from potential manipulation.
Confidentiality of handling lists of potential applicants
One contracting authority had a list of tenderers for invitation to the procurement procedure in the database, which all employees had access at any time.
This allowed manipulation or unauthorized disclosure of the names of expected or accepted applicants, who could then agree on the price.
Documentation
The documentation gave reasons for choosing applicants in only a few cases.
NKÚ
Applicant selection criteria
During the construction of the road circuit, the candidates did not have information about what will be evaluated from the data on their qualifications and how.
The action related to the development and modernization of waterways and ports in the procurement notice for participation in a narrower procedure did not define the criteria for restrictions on the number of tenderers.
All eight tenderers met qualifying conditions, but thus exceeded the number to which the contracting authority limited participation in the procurement procedure.
The Commission then made the selection of applicants using the method of random selection - by drawing, which was legal at the time.
This procedure should have been specified as a criterion already in the procurement notice.
Summary
Due to the high risk of manipulation in selecting a winning candidate in limited procurement procedures, both countries introduced special measures to prevent illegal restrictions on competition.
German rules limit such opportunities for manipulation using the so-called. cross-checks (four-eyes principle), by maintaining the confidential character of the list of applicants and by prohibiting proposing to select applicants for external companies.
Czech rules aim to prevent potential restrictions with the aim of manipulation mainly by an unlimited number of applicants.
However, the inspection found that part of the said rules were not sufficiently applied and that inadmissible restrictions on the candidate s' circle were not prevented in some cases.
Contracting entities are obliged to eliminate all the deficiencies mentioned.
Submission of tenders
The procurement phase in which potential tenderers can draw up tenders based on the tender documentation they received starts with publication of the procurement information and / or the invitation to tenderers.
Until the date of opening the envelopes, applicants may submit their tenders to the contracting authority and thus apply for the award of the contract.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of procurement procedure.
The contracting authority must follow national rules governing this stage of proceedings and prevent potential manipulation.
The abovementioned rules apply in particular to organizing and control.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle applies that tendency documents on the basis of which potential suppliers make their offer must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Projection offices that are involved in proceedings should not fulfil this task.
The contracting authority must ensure that all candidates received the same information during this stage of the procurement procedure.
In case of uncertainty in the procurement documentation or further questions arise, only the contracting authority may provide information to tenderers.
The design offices responsible for drawing up the procurement documentation cannot provide any information.
Any contact between projection office and applicants must be prevented throughout this phase.
Those must remain anonymous throughout the course, because allowing contact with them can adversely affect the competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly must be submitted in a closed envelope.
Electronically submitted offers must be encoded.
Different clauses
In Germany, the contracting authority may entrust insured suppliers of external services to print and send documentation, with their employees being obliged to comply with confidentiality.
In Germany, the tenders received must be marked indicating the date of receipt and transmitted directly and immediately in its original state (sealed) to the official responsible for their custody.
This worker must not be involved in the procurement procedure.
Bids received must be locked up until the envelopes are opened.
In the Czech Republic, the offers received are marked with a serial number.
The contracting authority shall issue a report with competition details including the tender number and information on the draft and receipt of the tender.
There are no special regulations on the safekeeping of offers.
Main inspection findings
BRH
BRH checked the assignment of the administration building.
Sending procurement documentation
Controlled contracting authorities of the construction administration sent out the procurement documentation either directly or entrusted it with printing and distribution to an external company.
Self-employed persons sent no documentation.
Information provided to applicants
For the part of the procurement documentation concerning inquiry and information, the contracting authority did not follow the rules for separate planning from the procurement procedure.
Contrary to the relevant regulations, he often did not mention the names of his contact staff, but rather the workers of the project management department.
Some procurement notices even included names of companies or self-employed persons involved in the preparation of the procurement documentation.
In rare cases, tenderers who asked questions during the procurement did not receive identical information.
Offer tagging
For contracting entities all accepted tenders were marked with a stamp and a receipt certificate.
However, in some cases in the negotiated procedure, offers were accepted by self-employed experts, violating the rule of one corruption prevention construction.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to keep them in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
With one contracting authority, offers were temporarily placed in an open compartment of the mailroom, which was accessed by all employees.
Another contracting authority placed a box in the hallway without constant supervision and part of the offers thrown into the mailbox stayed there overnight.
The box opening was wide and unsecured, so it was accessible not only to employees.
NKÚ
NKÚ has not identified shortcomings in this area.
Summary
In both countries rules are laid down to prevent contacts especially between stakeholders and design offices cooperating in procurement procedures throughout the entire process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all applicants.
Rules to prevent manipulation and corruption are suitable for receipt, storage and confidentiality of offers.
In Germany, the relevant requirements are somewhat more developed than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the accumulated control records have demonstrated violation of the rules in some areas.
These irregularities can easily be corrected.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of envelopes, offers that have been closed, opened, are read and published.
The period for which the tenderer is bound by his tender begins at the time of the deadline for submitting or opening the envelopes and ends with a deadline specified by the contracting authority.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
European legislation does not contain any specific provisions on opening envelopes.
However, national law and regulations contain extensive requirements for the protection of tenders and competition during this sensitive phase of the whole procurement procedure.
The principles of ′′ more eyes ", transparency and credibility of the process of opening envelopes are intended to prevent manipulations and adjustments of offers already submitted.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The opening of envelopes must be performed by several persons appointed by the contracting authority.
Conformity with the principle of ′′ more eyes ′′ is supposed to prevent individuals from manipulating offers.
Applicants may be present when envelopes are opened.
When opening all envelopes must be placed before the chairman of the commission and opened one by one.
Late offers received must not be taken into account.
In order to ensure transparency in opening envelopes, this phase including the conclusions (results) must be recorded in writing. The record must include, among other things, the names of applicants and prices offered.
The registration must be read and signed by the group leader.
The registration may be signed by the applicants present.
Different clauses
A commission is set up in the Czech Republic for opening envelopes.
Participation of independent experts is admitted.
Members of the commission may be responsible for discussing even in subsequent stages of the proceedings, i.e. by evaluating offers.
In Germany, the opening of envelopes takes place in the presence of the leader and the recorder.
The manager must be an employee of the contracting authority.
The manager and in the case of ground construction and the recorder must not be participants in the preparatory phase (production of the procurement documentation), must not decide on the award of the contract and may not be members during subsequent processing (proceedings) of the contract.
German regulations require registration of opening envelopes to contain not only offer prices, but also all information about discounts and special (unusual) signs, e.g. damaged envelopes upon receipt or late delivery.
In the Czech Republic, the registration purchased in addition to the offer prices must include an indication of the tender language and the signature authorization of the candidate.
German regulations require that all parts of open envelopes be marked to avoid subsequent changes.
Tenders, usually marked in the form of perforation, must be held at the end of opening the envelopes as confidential (secret) and can only be made available to persons who continue to process them.
Similar measures do not exist in the Czech Republic.
If a single offer is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope must not be opened and the candidate must be informed immediately.
They do not have this modification in Germany, and if a single offer is accepted, it is open and evaluated.
Main inspection findings
BRH
The principle of cross check
During the opening of envelopes, contracting entities followed the principle of four eyes.
There were always a leader and a recorder who was not intended for another role.
However, in rare cases, in small negotiated procedures, the natural person opened the tenders sent to them without the participation of the contracting authority.
The course of opening envelopes
Envelopes from opening envelopes did not always document the course.
In some cases no late bids were marked and in some cases were missing signatures.
Marketing of offers received
Contracting entities marked offers of perforations with a date, which was in accordance with the requirements.
Some of them have incorrectly flagged offers in the past, but after BRH alerted, they changed practice.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
NKÚ
Time limit for receipt of tenders
