During road repairs, the candidate's offer was handed over to the contracting authority with a monthly delay and he still accepted it.
Summary
In both countries, the essential parts of the envelopes are identical with the principle of ′′ more eyes ′′ and the principle of transparency and therefore allow for significantly reducing the risk of corruption and manipulation.
German rules are more complex compared to the Czech Republic, especially requirements for accurate documentation of the procedure.
Marketing, safe keeping and respecting the confidential nature of offers significantly limit the possibility of subsequent changes in the submitted tenders.
In addition, workers responsible for opening envelopes must not carry out any other contract related activities.
Discovery, despite some discrepancies, confirms that the rules for opening envelopes are mainly applied.
Assessment and evaluation of tenders
The contracting authority must examine and evaluate the tenders received within the specified deadline.
At the same time, they must award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
EU law sets out the process of assessing and evaluating offers in several steps:
The first step examines the suitability of the applicants.
They must have a good economic and financial position and required professional and technical knowledge and abilities.
Candidates who have ever been legally convicted of bribery or defraudation must always be excluded from procurement procedures.
Offers of non-excluded tenderers must be evaluated in terms of number of correctness, technical suitability and value for money based on previously published award criteria.
The contracting authority must identify the most economically favourable offer and especially check all the significantly low price offers.
Review and assessment is especially sensitive and susceptible to manipulation.
For example, applicants may be excluded without a legitimate reason, or offers that do not meet the requirements may be left in the competition.
The result of the evaluation may be wrongly influenced by the preference of a candidate or his disadvantage, thus preventing the most economically advantageous offer.
Therefore, the contracting authority must take special measures when selecting persons involved in the process and must ensure that they meet the requirements for integrity and technical knowledge.
They also need to make sure that the whole process and decisions taken are transparent and credible.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
In accordance with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require review and evaluation of tenders in progressive steps.
During the evaluation, the requirements to demonstrate the suitability of the applicants, the evaluation criteria and their weights specified in the notice or in the procurement documentation shall not be changed.
The criteria laid down for the assessment of the suitability of the applicants cannot be applied further.
A further evaluation can only be carried out on the basis of the evaluation criteria.
Offers submitted must first be examined from a formal point of view whether they are complete or not included suspicious elements that might encourage manipulation.
If tenderers are excluded from further examination and evaluation of the tenders submitted by them, they must be informed immediately.
If the assessment of the tenders of the finding is disproportionately low bid price, the candidate concerned must be given the opportunity to comment on the situation before possible withdrawal of his offer.
The reasons for the decision must be transparently documented.
Different clauses
In Germany, tenderers must remain confidential and only eligible persons can participate in the evaluation of offers.
Only the contracting authority can review the mathematical accuracy of tenders.
Only employees who are not integrated into the decision-making phase of the contractor's selection or the project implementation phase may be entrusted with the evaluation.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are entrusted with examining and evaluating offers, they must realize that offers are confidential and respect that fact honestly.
They can only give the contracting authority suggestions for decisions.
In the Czech Republic, tenders must be reviewed and evaluated by the commissioning authority, which will draw up a report with the proposal for a contract conclusion.
However, in both countries the final decision depends on the contracting authority.
If in Germany the documents and declarations required in connection with the submission of tenders are incomplete, the tenderers concerned must subsequently submit the required documents within six days.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If applicants fail to comply with this obligation, their offers must be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority can decide whether it will give the candidate an opportunity to supplement the missing documents.
If the candidate does not support them, they must be excluded.
In Germany it is necessary to review not only the total price, but also the unit prices.
If the price structure of the offer shows that prices for parts of the overall project were estimated disproportionately high or low, applicants must be asked for clarifications.
If they do not provide an explanation and if the contracting authority can prove that the tender contains compensatory prices, such offers must be excluded.
This should prevent applicants from submitting price calculations based on the assumption that significant quantitative changes will be made for each part of the project, which can lead to a significant increase in project costs.
In the Czech Republic, the total price of the work is evaluated and the prices of individual parts are not examined in detail.
Appreciation compensation is not a reason to exclude an offer.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a candidate who offers disproportionately high or low price.
If one or more offers differ price by 10 % or more compared to the price estimated by the contracting authority or by other tenders, tenderers must prove that their offer was plausible and convincingly calculated.
If they are not able to do so, the contracting authority should exclude them.
In the Czech Republic, procurement procedure may be cancelled after a price review if only offers with disproportionately low prices were received and tenderers did not justify these prices.
If the price of the tender is significantly higher than the contracting authority's estimate, this is not a reason for refusing to award the contractor concerned (unlike the German procurement law).
If there is a suspicion of action in Germany to reduce competition, the contracting authority shall immediately report this fact to the competent supervisory authority.
The candidate must decide on the next procedure and whether it is appropriate to inform the antitrust authority or criminal law enforcement authorities.
They also have to approve (e.g. when the contract exceeds 000 50 and the contract has not been awarded to the tenderer with the lowest bid) whether the contract will be awarded when the contract is negotiated or whether the procurement procedure will be cancelled.
Czech rules do not modify this area.
Main inspection findings
BRH
Appropriate examination and procurement criteria
Most proven procurement procedures were in accordance with relevant requirements.
In case of some recommendations of potential suppliers made by self-employed persons, contracting entities themselves did not check the suitability of the tenderers.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In some cases, procurement procedures were not sufficient documentation as to whether the contracting authority took into account all published evaluation criteria or whether the selection decision was based solely on the price criterion.
Selection of interested persons and confidentiality of offers
Some contracting entities used the services of unauthorized persons, such as self-employed persons or employees of the construction authorities.
These were incorporated into the planning or implementation process of construction projects, performing functions that should have been held solely by the contracting authority.
Contracting entities sought to justify this fact with their lack of human resources in a given sector.
In some cases, they used self-employed professionals to examine offers of services of persons who were not formally bound to maintain the confidentiality of offers and perform with proper care the execution of their contract commitments.
As regards contracting entities, there was usually no evidence of whether offers in the custody of self-employed professionals were only available to designated persons.
Review and mathematical check of offers
Some contracting entities handed over open envelopes for further examination to self-employed professionals without first conducting a prescribed check of tenders and mathematical examination and without documenting the results of these tests.
In case of any intention of manipulation, third parties could make changes in tenders that could not be identified by the contracting authority.
The examination of documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the offers were not adequately identified or where price and product data were missing.
Performance audits
A model inspection of one contracting authority revealed that in 75 % of the procurement cases, the most advantageous tenders deviated by more than 10 % from predetermined costs.
One of twenty procurement procedures were cancelled due to non-adequate tenders.
In many cases there was lack of evidence or sufficient documentation on the examination of offers or deals with applicants for further clarification.
In many cases, detailed information was also missing e.g. on unit prices of the most important invoiced items.
Changes in market prices or increases in material costs were often stated as a reason for the derogation.
Contracting entities defended that identifying and demonstrating compensatory prices was difficult.
In case of one call for tenders, made by an entity outside the ordinary contracting authority, a 66 % lower price was offered compared to the original cost estimation.
No data on closer cost examination or finding reasons for variations were recorded.
In clarifying this question, the contracting authority found no indication of price dumping of the tenderer to whom the contract was potentially awarded.
Therefore, it was not clarified whether the original cost estimate was inflated or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the contracting authority evaluated this candidate as a ′′ low cost company ′′ that was unable to meet either qualitative requirements or deadlines.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to the tenderer whose price was 35 % higher than the original cost estimate.
The contracting authority did not cancel the procurement procedure and stated the unfounded argument that the candidate concerned could be assumed that he did not base his price on excessive costs.
Suspicion of irregularities
One contracting authority found two cases of irregularities and reported to the company responsible for technical supervision.
In one procurement procedure, two tenderers submitted tenders containing an identical price calculation, which prompted the contracting authority to exclude both tenders.
The checks showed no significant deficiencies in the application of other provisions.
NKÚ
Appropriate verification
For many construction events such as university buildings, roads and railways, contracting entities did not exclude tenderers from participation in the procurement procedure, even though they did not meet the requirements of the contracting authority, or did not prove the qualification to the required extent, or on the contrary, one contracting authority failed to demonstrate or explain the reason for eliminating the candidate who met the requirements I'm sorry.
Reviews
Although the individual evaluation criteria of the contracting procedure for the construction of the sewage plant were established for the construction worker, the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For railway infrastructure development action, the evaluation criteria were not established at the start of the procedure, but only at the beginning of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the evaluation of the 'reduction of construction time' criterion was not done correctly.
For applicants in second and third place, the evaluation incorrectly reported a larger reduction in the construction period than stated in their offers.
Documentation of the reasons for choosing the candidate
The contracting authority failed to demonstrate for three housing support actions, based on which criteria it assessed the accepted tenders and how it chose the most suitable of them.
Properity of selection of contractors of small-scale contracts associated with road circuit construction with the expected price up to 500 thousand.
Kč could not be verified, because suppliers were selected only based on telephone consultations on price and date of fulfilment, but documents of these negotiations were not made out.
Summary
In both countries, rules for verifying and evaluating offers correspond to EU requirements.
However, they differ with regard to specific management and choice of individuals in the proceedings included.
Unlike the Czech Republic, in Germany these steps of the procurement process follow stricter and more detailed requirements, especially in terms of the application of the cross principle and the protection of tenders.
The same applies to rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, checks found in some cases that substantial steps of the process in verifying and evaluating tenders were not documented at all and if so, only partially.
Absence of control tools and transparency in taking decisions during reviewing and evaluating tenders allows manipulation.
The checks showed serious defects, such as the submission of tenders to third parties without prior proper examination and documentation of tenders by the contracting authority.
If contracting entities entrust a third party to carry out the functions of examination and evaluation of tenders, adequate measures and increased control of measures against increased manipulation are necessary.
In all cases, controlled German contracting entities did not use the complete set of available tools and did not deal with their own price structure.
In the Czech Republic, shortcomings were found in the assessment of the suitability of offers and the application of the evaluation criteria.
Completion of the procurement procedure
After examination and evaluation of tenders, the procurement process is completed by awarding a contract or cancelling the procedure.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
In the case of European proceedings, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the decision on awarding the contract.
Contractors have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited time limit of 10 or 15 days and request a review if applicable.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The 10 days period applies to electronic submissions and 15 days for other submissions.
The contract must not be concluded before this period or before the decision of the review procedure is taken.
If the review body rejects the complaint and confirms the decision, candidates and tenderers must be given the opportunity to have the correctness of the application of the procurement law examined by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting authority will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by rapid implementation of the procurement decision.
The contracting authority must properly document the procedure.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries implemented on informational management duties.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure lies with the contracting authority.
However, this one cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of the proper examination and evaluation.
The contracting authority is supposed to contract within the specified time.
The reason is because the tenderer is not bound by his offer after this period.
Content of the contract must not deviate from the winning bid.
Unsuccessful applicants should be informed of the outcome in time, stating the reason why their offer was not accepted.
The cancellation of the procurement procedure is only allowed when certain conditions are met, e.g. if the prices in the offers do not meet the specifications.
Different clauses
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory waiting period before the conclusion of the contract of 10 or 15 days applies to European and national proceedings.
In Germany, the equivalent provision applies only to European proceedings.
In all other proceedings in Germany, tenderers cannot be informed of the award of the contract before a decision on its EU provision and review award.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement procedure must be cancelled if a single tender has been received or only one offer complied with the requirements for its consideration and evaluation.
The contract must be awarded in Germany, even though a single tender has been received, provided that this tender meets the conditions laid down in the procurement documentation and is cost effective.
Main inspection findings
BRH
The checks found few discrepancies in completing the controlled procurement processes.
In some cases of European proceedings, the companies empowered letters before the expiry of the notification deadline, which may invalidate the contract.
In several cases of open proceedings, authorizing letters of modification included incompatible with the content of the tenders, e.g. new deadlines.
In some cases contracting entities did not comply with the deadline for awarding the contract.
In one open procedure, the contracting authority chose the second most favorable offer, because the candidate offering a price more than 50 % lower did not wish to meet the contract at the originally offered price.
NKÚ
During the reconstruction and construction of the college, the contracting authority did not enter into a contract with the contractor in accordance with the draft contract contained in the offer of the selected candidate.
Some road repair and maintenance events, highway construction and road circuit construction contracts were concluded later than the law provides.
The contracting authority sent a notice of selection of the most suitable offer to all tenderers after the legal deadline expires, for construction adjustments in former military újezdech.
Summary
Both countries implemented EU regulations on termination of procurement procedures.
Legal protection of failed candidates contributes to the reduction of corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act includes the Institute of Legal Protection also in cases of contracts below the EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that a limited time limit for contract closure was exceeded.
This can cause adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting entities should eliminate such shortcomings when closing the procurement procedure.
Documentation, notifications, information duties
The procurement process with all its individual phases, relevant findings and decisions, including relevant justifications, must be documented in a transparent way.
The completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
The data on procurement procedures are summarized in EU statistics.
Demands of European law and prevention of corruption
The obligation to document the procurement procedure is in accordance with the essential requirement of the principle of transparency applied at EU level.
Only proper and time-relevant documentation on decision making and justification guarantees transparency in the procurement process, and above all guarantees effective legal protection of the interests of each candidate in cases where the value of the contract exceeds European limits.
Proper documentation is also an essential part of anti-corruption measures, since the obligation to substantiate individual decisions and their justification significantly reduces the space for manipulation.
In cases of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must announce their completion of the EU's Office of Official Publications within 48 days of the date of award of the contract.
The Office publishes the notification in the Official Journal of the EU and thus fulfils the requirement of transparency.
The contracting authority must summarize the essential information on its procurement procedures and communicate them to the European Commission through the relevant national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission publishes annual statistics, which allow for an overview of the development of the single market in the field of construction.
German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have completely transposed into their national legislation the provisions of the European documentation and notification laws.
The provisions on documentation and notifications for European statistics are almost identical in both countries.
Different clauses
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to announce the award of a contract does not only apply to European procedures, but also to national procurement procedures.
The deadline for notification is only 15 days after the contract is concluded.
In Germany, the obligation to notify procurement procedures, in addition to those compulsory under European law, applies only to limited procedures exceeding the limit of 25 thousand. € (625 thousand. Kč) and direct procedures exceeding the limit of 15 thousand. € (375 thousand. Kč) VAT incl.
Only parties are informed below this limit.
Main inspection findings
BRH
Documentation
Large amount of assignments have not been fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, e.g. reasons for supply specifications and national rules.
In the case of one procedure, the contracting authority did not explain why it contracted a candidate whose offer did not contain compulsory elements.
In several cases, some required records were also missing.
Disclosure of award of the contract
In the case of some European procedures, the contracting authority made mistakes in the publication of the notice.
In case of several assignments, evidence of publication of the notice was missing.
Notification obligation
Statistically proven files included the required minimum of information and were created and sent on time.
Preliminary transparency
In most cases, the contracting authority published information on the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting authority, contract information was not published due to a communication error.
The contracting authority took six months to notice the error.
Consequently, the outcome of the proceedings was not published during this period.
NKÚ
Documentation
The events related to the organizing of a major sporting event have been identified considerable shortcomings in the procurement documentation such as: incorrect information on offer prices in protocols from the evaluation committee meeting.
Moreover, some documents about opening envelopes were not signed.
Disclosure of award of the contract
In preparation of repairs and maintenance of communications, highway construction and road circuit, public procurement notice was sent after the deadline or not published.
Summary
Documentation and notification and notification and notification obligations include European requirements and are almost identical in both countries.
This generally ensures the transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
Czech reporting duties are somewhat stricter compared to German.
The checks revealed shortcomings significantly lowering the value of documentation as a means of corruption prevention.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Contracting entities should continue to strengthen the transparency of their procurement procedures and fully comply with the notification and notification requirements.
Summary evaluation and recommendations
Parallel checks of NKÚ and BRH were focused on two areas that are essential for the process of procurement both in the Czech Republic and Germany, namely the application of EU procurement law and corruption prevention.
EU Legislative gives opportunity to international competition within the EU to create a single European market.
The aim of measures to prevent corruption is not only to avoid it or at least reduce it, but also to prevent financial damage and possible loss of confidence in the integrity of the government.
The sought inspection findings of both control institutions - NKÚ and BRH - with regard to the application of the procurement right of both countries and the comparison of its relevant provisions give an internal view of common and different elements that can help both countries in the further development and application of this right.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries transposed EU law regarding public procurement into their national legislation.
Thus, there is an important common basis in both countries for public procurement and fulfilling essential requirements in the area of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting entities reinforce these requirements with partially very extensive measures.
The Czech Republic has raised public procurement clauses requiring European management and procedures that are below EU limits and therefore governs national legislation.
However, checks showed that contracting entities do not always fully comply with all relevant EU requirements.
German contracting authorities should continue to improve the quality of their procurement procedures to eliminate the mentioned irregularities taking into account the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, checks identified risks affecting economy and achieving value for money.
In particular, this is an incomplete definition of the subject-matter of a public contract resulting in additional works, which were often awarded against the law, insufficient definition of the expected price and also the required qualifying assumptions narrowing the possible circuit of tenderers and thus reducing competition especially in the field of transport buildings.
Prevention of corruption
Joint checks were not intended to detect corruption cases.
The reason was that both BRH and NKÚ do not have the tools to do so.
However, they can verify whether the competent authorities of both countries are taking measures to reduce corruption and manipulate during public procurement and how these measures are applied.
In terms of corruption prevention, both countries focused on different aspects.
The German provisions mainly give space to wide and unlimited competition, transparency and controls as a central element of corruption prevention.
Czech regulations mainly monitor the strengthening of the transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany there are general principles of corruption prevention that apply to the whole Federal administration.
These principles were also incorporated among the public procurement requirements and were adopted to meet the specific needs of these procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, sometimes very precisely, ways to comply with the requirements for the prevention of corruption during the procurement procedure and the choice of persons included therein.
In the opinion of the BRH, the principle of preference for open procurement procedures and calls for participation is a particularly appropriate instrument for substantial reduction of the risk of corruption in public procurement, while limiting competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Risk analysis and adequate control (especially the principle of cross control), requirements regarding transparency, procurement documentation and various organisational measures are also an effective mechanism to prevent corruption and manipulation.
Therefore, BRH does not feel the need for substantial changes to the current provisions that public institutions must comply with during the award of public procurement.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
Irregularities found in some areas highlighted weaknesses in compliance with certain requirements.
Therefore, contracting entities should provide their employees with further education and thus inform them with anti-corruption requirements and further increase their awareness in this area.
A significant part of the exposed weaknesses applies to activities delegated by the construction administration to private entrepreneurs.
However, the absence of adequate controls in delegation of powers increases the risk of their abuse.
Consequently, manipulation and corruption activities should only be transmitted to third parties if the administration can guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against unauthorized intervention.
NKÚ
In the Czech Republic anti-corruption strategies were adopted at the government level, which also significantly affect the public procurement area.
NKÚ control events took place during the implementation of one of the most important parts of this strategy, a significant change in the public procurement law and the adoption of follow-up implementing regulations.
Strategy adopted and new laws can be effective steps to improve the situation.
According to new regulations, for example, the contracting authority must justify the effectiveness of the contract, the determination of the expected value of the contract, the adequacy of requirements for qualifying assumptions, the determination of basic evaluation criteria and the method of evaluation of tenders and the proper improvement and publication of everything.
Recommendation
Overall, both NKÚ and BRH have a positive opinion on the ways of implementing EU requirements.
Their wide application in practice confirmed that EU requirements for competition, equal treatment and transparency are an appropriate basis for the award of public procurement within the EU.
A multinational model established in the EU can also serve as a base for similar projects aimed at facilitating and supporting international competition.
Taking into account the great potential of material and intangible damage caused as a result of manipulation and corruption in connection with the award of public procurement, both BRH and NKÚ insist that it is the responsibility of contracting entities to continue measures against corruption and manipulation and improve them wherever possible.
Especially organisational structures and procurement processes should be monitored continuously in terms of weaknesses and risks to identify and respond appropriately to the need for repair actions.
Compared to the practice in Germany, it appeared that the share of open procurement procedures should increase in the Czech Republic, which give space to competition and significantly reduce the possibility of corruption.
Procurement in parts can also have a positive impact on the price achieved in cases where it is admissible and suitable for contracting entities. The higher number of applicants puts pressure on the price achieved.
The influence on the procurement procedure is also provided by his organization.
In Germany, it is provided by special state organizations, while in the Czech Republic, except for transport buildings, central authorities organize it themselves or through contractors.
Both NKÚ and BRH wish to further develop knowledge in their work where it is in place and address them with their parliament and government beyond their common project.
Moreover, they believe that the principles of procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will also be of interest at the level of the International Organisation of Highest Supervisory Institutions (INTOSAI), because these principles and findings are of general importance for effective countering corruption and guarantee, that public procurement is awarded in a regime of well functioning and honest competition and that value is achieved for money.

COMMON FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel checks on the management of excise taxes in SR and Czech Republic
Joint final report
May 2017
The highest supervisory office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Supervisory Authority of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The Joint Report submitted informs about the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel checks carried out by the Slovak Republic's Supreme Supervisory Authority and the Czech Republic's Supervisory Authority, with a focus on the management of excise taxes in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the top control institutions of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the NKÚ SR and the NKÚ Czech Republic in the performance of parallel inspections focused on the management of excise taxes, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel checks was selected based on the fact that both EU Member States are based on common European legislation to find out how it is applied at national level, how the excise tax management system is set up and how the systems in SR and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out was exchanging experience, identifying differences and finding good practice.
Last but not least, it was beneficial to find that international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise duty management is very limited without parallel checks being carried out.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrík,
President of the President
Chairman
The highest supervisory office of the Czech Republic
The highest inspection office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel checks of SPD management in SR and Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the SR and their administration is in accordance with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences were found between the adjustment of excise duties in SR and Czech Republic, in the Czech Republic contributes to the effective management of excise duties verification of the economic stability of applicants for the issuance of permits and compulsory marking and coloring of selected mineral oils and some other oils; in SR the distribution of control signs is simpler than in the Czech Republic and less burdened by the tax manager.
In the fight against excise tax evasion, the supervision of raw tobacco movement and or as a good practice in both countries. tobacco raw materials, implementation of the Institute of Fuel Distributor and registration of retailers of alcohol packaging.
Excise tax revenue in SR and Czech Republic grows slower than other tax revenue.
EU goals consisting of reducing labour taxation, introducing ecologically economical measures and reducing tobacco and alcohol addiction have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and SR, among others. also because there is no indexation of excise duty rates in both countries.
This results in reducing the importance of excise taxes on total tax revenue and due to increasing purchasing power, a real reduction in tax burden with excise duties.
The state has long-term support for the implementation of environmental measures, but these measures have a negative impact on excise tax revenue, which will need to be replaced by other revenue or reducing state spending.
Administrative costs incurred on the management of excise taxes in the Czech Republic and the SR have been growing long-term, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency is decreasing.
In SR, this effectiveness is negatively affected by the costs of electronization of excise duty management (IT expenditure) and the costs incurred on the wages of employees carrying out permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol.
Electronization of the management of excise taxes in SR did not significantly improve the number of tax administrators.
NKÚ Czech Republic and NKÚ SR recommend doporučují SR to rethink the justification of the performance of permanent tax oversight in tax warehouses for alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the effectiveness of administrative expenses was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the controlled period, which would lead to a reduction in the staffing of the excise duty management.
The number of comparable administrative actions of tax administrators was similar in SR and the Czech Republic in the various years of the controlled period, but the number of comparable tax entities is about a third lower in SR than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in SR perform administrative actions mainly in the form of physical exercise of tax oversight, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote oversight and risk analysis.
The management of excise taxes in SR is more administratively demanding than in the Czech Republic and due to the ratio of the number of tax operations to the number of entities and more costly.
Electronization of excise duty management in SR and Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In SR, the administration of tax returns for excise duties is fully electronized, documents demonstrating taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are transmitted in the Czech Republic.
Both methods of electronization support effective management of excise taxes and therefore NKÚ Czech Republic and NKÚ SR recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure on the implementation of the EMCS system could not be compared as the FG SR provided spending data only for the system upgrade in the period 2011-2015, but the costs were incurred even before this period.
Expenditure incurred during this period only for the EMCS upgrade was about 20 % higher in the SR than the costs incurred in the Czech Republic both on the introduction of EMCS and on the upgrade of this system in over ten years.
Excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and SR did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when comparable spending was incurred.
The level of supervisory is comparable in both countries, but in the SR, the management of excise taxes is significantly more resource demanding.
The introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise products (EMCS) has been streamlined by the management of excise duties, but in SR to a lower extent, because significantly higher costs were incurred than in the Czech Republic on the introduction of the system and its modernization.
Basic information
The cooperation of both supervisory institutions was carried out under the Cooperation Treaty on the implementation of parallel checks aimed at the management of excise duties on 18. 8. 2015.
NKÚ Czech Republic and NKÚ SR agreed to perform parallel checks, which will primarily focus on the issue of excise duty management and whose results will allow analysis, comparisons and evaluation of the facts found.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel checks were based.
Characteristics of the object and the aim of parallel control:
The aim of parallel checks was to compare the performance of excise tax administrators, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators and identifying weaknesses of the excise tax management process.
The following main audit questions should have been answered in particular:
Did excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and SR achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when incurring comparable expenditures?
Has the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise duty products (Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) been streamlined and the costs incurred effectively for its introduction?
Parallel checks carried out should have identified causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of tax management in the Czech Republic and SR, especially in the field of regulation and organisational structure.

Legislative for excise duties in Czech Republic and SR
Excise tax management legislation is divided into EU legislation (see Annex No. 1) and national law level (see Annex No. 2).
Council Directive 2008/118 / EC on the general adjustment of excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12 / EEC defines excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the management of taxes and the management of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive provides for the imposition of taxes on consumption on other products.
EU legislation regulates in particular the minimum conditions for: the amount of tax rates for the different types of selected products, production, storage, processing and possession of taxable products, taxation, exemption and tax refund, oversight of transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and keeping registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation enables control procedures and institutes to be introduced at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Legislative of excise duties in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legislation of excise duties is concentrated in the excise duty law (law no. 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the management of mineral oil tax, alcohol tax, tobacco tax, beer taxes, wine and intermediate taxes and raw tobacco tax.
This law defines forms of handling products subject to excise duties, tax payer, permitting proceedings, conditions for transport of products, tax return and penalties for infringements.
The law and follow-up decrees further modify some other conditions for handling mineral oils (marking of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirit drinks and tobacco products, monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and storage of crude tobacco for a purpose other than the production of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and some other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in sections 45 to 47 of Law No. 261/2007 Coll., on stabilization of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic there are also a number of provisions related to the management of excise duties contained in special legislation. Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulates the conditions for the sale, distribution of fuel and keeping fuel records for free tax circulation.
In law no. 61/1997 Coll., o alcohol and its implementing rules define the conditions for manufacture, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll., on compulsory alcohol marking and relevant implementing regulations provide for compulsory marking of alcohol in the packaging, conditions for handling control bands and conditions for alcohol handling (i.e. for the manufacture, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, takeover, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Tax procedures not specified in special regulations are governed by law No. 280/2009 Coll., tax order.
The penalties are imposed in accordance with law no. 500/2004 Coll., administrative order.
Conditions for the issue of a trade licence (concession) for the operation of a business ′′ production and processing of fuels and greases and distribution of fuel ′′ and ′′ production, modification and sale of fermented alcohol, alcohol of consumerism and spirit drinks ′′ are governed by law No. 455/1991 Coll., on business (business law).
The Czech Republic has exercised the right to introduce control procedures and institutes to control the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to supervise compliance with the legislation in the handling of selected products without excise duty, as well as the handling of selected products already taxed taken away.
This is a monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and crude tobacco, marking some other mineral oils, marking tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic used the authorization to apply excise duty to other products and introduced an excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject matter of inspection in the Czech Republic
Based on the resolution of the Government of the Czech Republic of 3. October 2012 No. 735, the implementation of the ′′ zero tolerance plan for the black market for spirit drinks ", between 2012-2015 and 2012-2015 in the Czech Republic, fundamental legislative arrangements were introduced in the Czech Republic, which introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on alcohol excise duty.
During the same period there were also major changes in the legislation on mineral oil tax, tobacco product taxes and the criminality of preparation of tax reduction.
Criminal protection of tax revenue
Effective from 1. 7. 2016, the crime preparation of the crime is introduced ′′ tax reduction, fee and similar compulsory payment ". The adjustment made should allow police authorities to take more efficient and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, e.g. deployment of operational resources.
General provisions for the management of excise duties
The issuance of an authorization to handle excise products under the Excise Tax Act is conditional on: reliability; debtlessness; economic stability; right to operate a business allowing the pursuit of an activity related to the authorization; a situation where the appellant not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The aim of the regulation was mainly to address the issue of tax arrears, by reducing operators with the right to handle excise taxable products.
The condition of economic stability newly enables the tax manager to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the framework of the authorization procedure and after the issuance of the authorization.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities not having sufficient financial income to properly fulfil tax liabilities from handling selected products.
Indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, productivity, labor productivity) were established to assess the economic stability of the appellant.
In addition to these indicators, the administrative discretion of the tax manager is also important in view of the individual conditions of the procedure.
The law sets out the periodicity of verification of the fulfilment of the condition of economic stability because of the current data - verification takes place once a year following the deadline for filing income tax returns.
The tax administrator has the opportunity to lay down other conditions needed for tax management.
If the holder of the permit does not fulfil the conditions, the tax manager is entitled to revoke the permit or cancel with delay.
Out of the total of 2 609 entities with the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18,6 % were found economically unstable with high risk of arrears when the tax liability exceeds the amount of tax security (e.g. repeated recipient).
The permit was revoked by ten entities, other applicants increased tax collateral, capitalized their contribution to the company or documented current accounting data according to which they already met all conditions for issuing the authorization.
In addition to the appellant, a natural person who is a statutory body or is a member of the statutory body, or a natural person who is not the statutory body of the appellant or its member, must comply with the conditions of reliability and without debt, but exercises such activity (chain of legal persons in the position of a statutory body or of its member), so called. established entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30 entities were checked.
Registration kept under the Excise Tax Act (§ 37 to § 40 and § 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) contain information on:
type, name, code and quantity of goods manufactured, received, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax management scheme (tax exemption regime, importation, re-entry into the suspension scheme, taxable export, free circulation, own consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the recipient or supplier of selected products, the declarant, the date of the event and registration;
transport of selected products (eg means of transport, carriers, transport numbers);
the registration numbers of related documents;
notification of the introduction of alcohol in a consumer package marked by control tape for free tax circulation and distribution data.
Record of post-transport takeover must be made immediately upon completion.
In case of electronic-kept records, registration must be kept or allowed to output in xls, xlsx, ods.
Alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures to ensure a detailed overview of the activities of the subjects (see Annex No. 2012). 3, Scheme A) from the production of raw alcohol through marking with control tape to its distribution to the final seller or the legitimate user of the exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, customs authorities and production equipment for the production of alcohol that is not in operation is subject to the supervision of customs authorities.
The aim of the new regulation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirit drinks and to identify persons handling alcohol in the packaging, reduce alcohol management to financially stable and reliable persons and ensure constant supervision of the production and marking of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of production, income, stocks and issuance of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to each stages of production and alcohol processing, indicating the documents numbers.
Limitation of the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and restrictions on the number of packages with a broken control tape at the point of final sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or another packaging with a volume of max. one liter, resp. three liters when it comes to a glass container.
Spirit drinks in larger packaging are viewed as unmarked, which are prohibited from handling.
Max can be found at the point of final sale to a natural person for his / her personal consumption. one consumer package with a broken control tape or three if fitted with a one-way valve.
The compulsory registration of a person who presents alcohol in products in a consumer packaging of at least 15 % volume of alcohol for free tax circulation and is: importer of alcohol, producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or operator of a tax warehouse under a tax exemption regime, provided personal and technical conditions.
Personal conditions - reliability, integrity and non-expression of a ban on activity - must be met by the applicant and the person in the position of a statutory authority or a responsible representative.
Depending on the expected amount of inspection bands, the applicant must provide bail 100 000 CZK to 5 000 CZK (i.e. approx. 3 700 € to 185 000).
The technical conditions for registration are suitable place for marking alcohol and the equipment of the place of marking or tax warehouse with a camera tracker with continuous operation and remote access of the tax manager.
The registration designation of the control tape is introduced for the marking of spirits with a volume greater than 0,06 liters.
When carrying control bands, the registration marking of the control bands shall be indicated in the transport documents or customs declaration at the time of export.
The inspection tape until 2013 30. 11. contained a 30.-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration number, the application code for inspection belts and the classification code according to ethanol volume concentration level.
The control tape from 12. 1. 2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the amount of alcohol in the consumer packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20°C, with rounding to the whole millilitres downward.
Registration of control bands for spirit drinks shall contain daily records of individual methods of handling control bands according to registration codes and also documents on the basis of which registration was made.
In the event of the destruction, loss or theft of specific control bands, their holder shall inform the tax manager by electronic means of the registration code of the inspection bands concerned and their number on the following working day following the operative event.
Introducing a new factual nature of offences and adjusting the amount of sanctions imposed for infringement of the legislation in the handling of control bands.
Penalties may be imposed up to the amount of excise duty or exceed times (e.g. when the control belt is destroyed or lost in a number exceeding 0,1 % of the total quantity of the individual inspection belt orders, when the control tape is not returned within the time limit specified).
Restriction on control tapes only to registered holders who are not allowed to transfer them to another person except for their provision to a foreign supplier for the purpose of marking spirit drinks in a packaging manufactured outside the Czech Republic.
The inspection tapes exported must be placed on the consumer packaging and re-imported no later than nine months after taking over from the tax manager.
Compulsory registration of alcohol distributor in a consumer packaging provided similar personal conditions as for a person compulsory to sign alcohol and with a obligation to deposit bail up to CZK 5 000 (i.e. Approx. 185 000).
Definition of persons for selling or buying alcohol in a consumer package.
Authorised persons are obliged to sell alcohol in a consumer package to other registered persons or final sellers, or they may sell it as a final seller.
They can acquire alcohol from other registered persons, insolvency administrator, administrative body, state organisational components or unregistered persons during the execution of tax execution.
Notice of the introduction of alcohol or sale in a consumer package for free tax circulation are obliged to send alcohol holders and distributors immediately the following day after the operative event to the tax administrator via the tax administrator's information system (ORO web client) or with content in xml format.
The notification contains the number of control bands used, volume and type of consumer packaging, volume alcohol, European goods code (EAN), identification of distributor or final seller, as well as product name and batch of production.
Tax entities sent about 10,5 miles between 2014 and 2015 an announcement.
Compulsory concession (a specific form of business permissions) not only for the production and treatment of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in a consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or another legal or business person for his or her own internal use.
Concessed business can only be executed after a decision is made by the business authority, when competence and other conditions are fulfilled.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit of tax administrators is the overview of vendors and their premises and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, about 94 thousand was registered in 2014 for a field involving production, modification of fermented alcohol, alcoholic alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages. and in 2015 about 104 thousand. concessions.
Checks on compliance with the legislation in the field of handling products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic also provide their activities outside the tax manager: business authorities, state agricultural and food inspection, financial authorities of the Czech Republic, Czech commercial inspections.
If they find that there has been a breach of obligation or a breach of the prohibition, the excise tax administrators shall immediately inform the excise duty manager.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has introduced a comprehensive supervisory system (see Annex No. 3, Scheme B), subject to mineral oils charged with excise duty, but also collected mineral oils by excise duty unloaded, which were abused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from production of mineral oil through storage, transport, marking and coloring of selected mineral oils, marking some other mineral oils to delivery to the final consumer or user and in some cases the consumption of mineral oils.
Customs supervision includes the manufacture of marking substances for marking mineral oils and handling these substances.
The marking and coloring of selected mineral oils are subject to mineral oils specified under the Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 25 19 (kerosene others), 2710 29 19 (other not elsewhere specified medium oils) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 49 19 and 45 2710 19 unless they are banned.
The marking of some other mineral oils is subject to e.g. Benzol, toluene, xylol and lubrication oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine drive.
Branding and colouring selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a branding substance is possible only by the tax manager's permission.

The most important new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils, which is the group of mineral oils under the Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubrication oils and oils other than engine drive) whose kinematic viscosity at 40°C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: flash point is lower than 150°C, at least 20 % of volume distillation including losses up to 350°C during distillation test.
These mineral oils were abused as a substitute for finished fuels, especially for diesel, or were directly used or sold for engine drive, because the physical properties are very similar.
Register with the tax administrator must be subjects dealing with monitored mineral oils in bulk or in a package exceeding 220 liters.
