If alcohol is not accepted, issued, produced or processed in the tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to secure the presence of an employee of the customs office, which is required to secure the space by closure of the customs office.
However, in practice, this option is not often used because tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs office employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators use the legal option within the meaning of Law No. 467/2002 Z. z., about the production and marketing of alcohol, and they use production equipment for the production of alcohol in distillery for growing burning and also for the purposes of distillery for distillates, which must be in tax storage.
Performance of permanent tax oversight in alcohol tax warehouses ensures approximately 250 customs officers.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of check signs for alcohol
The basic action for the collection of control signs is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of registration number and issuing a voucher for the collection of control signs for alcohol.
Alcoholic drink, which is alcohol, means goods of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength exceeding 1,2 % volume.
The control mark is intended for the designation of the consumer packaging of alcohol.
A closed consumer packaging of alcohol, filled with alcohol intended for direct human consumption, is considered to be a consumer packaging of alcohol.
Consumer packaging of the Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 can only be put into free tax circulation on tax territory if it is marked with a control mark.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the beneficiary and the importer of the consumer packaging can mark the consumer's packaging with a control mark with a control mark.
The check mark contains, inter alia. an identification number consisting of a 14 digit character. The identification number contains the registration number (1.- 6. instead of the numeric character), alcohol volume (7.- 11. instead of the numeric character) and the volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer package (12.- 14. place of the numeric sign).
Original model of control sign for alcohol:
The registration number shall allocate. to each customer a check mark separately.
Only a check mark whose identification number corresponds to the volume of the consumer packaging, volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer packaging and customer's control mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging.
National legislation at the end of 2014 brought the introduction of a new information system of control signs.
The aim of the new information system of control signs was to simplify and informatize the ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control signs intended for the labelling of consumer packaging alcohol.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the beneficiary, the beneficiary, the importer of the consumer packaging and the recipient (s) of alcohol can mark the consumer packaging.
A customer of the control marks who wants to collect checks under the 'new system' must request the customs office to issue inspection signs electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of control signs is obliged to request their release, report data resulting from national legislation of SR and keep the registration of control signs.
The number of ordered pieces of inspection stamps must not be less than 500 pieces or multiple of them.
The tax administrator also communicates with customer of control signs via the electronic system of control signs, especially when notifying the number of control signs that the customer of the control signs can remove or. when determining the deadline for taking control signs by the customer of the inspection stamps in the printer.
The customer of the inspection stamps shall, before taking over the checks marks, put funds corresponding to the price of the control stamps he can withdraw and the quantity of which the customs office will inform him of.
The price of the check mark takes into account the amount of printer substitutes. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The control mark is entitled to print the state company Mint Kremnice.
FŘ SR exercises tax oversight of handling and disposal of the control marks in the printer.
FG SR is required to ensure the presence of a staff member of the financial directorate in the printer when handling the checks marks.
FŘ SR guarantees the sale of control signs to the customer of the printer's check stamps.
Control signs can be removed only in the printer from the employee of the Financial Directorate.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of control signs for tobacco products
The customer of the check mark must ask CÚ to allocate registration number and issue a voucher for the inspection stamp.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes can only be put into free tax circulation when marked with a check mark.
It is only possible to mark the consumer packaging of cigarettes with a check mark in the cigarette producing business.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, a licensed recipient or tobacco importer who wants to put tobacco products into free tax circulation in the tax territory may be the customer of the checks marks.
Only a check mark whose data correspond to the price of cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the package, the length of cigarettes, the validity of the tax rate and the registration number can be used to indicate the consumer packaging of cigarettes.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes can be sold for final consumption only at the price shown on the check mark.
National legislation at the end of 2014 brought the introduction of a new information system of control signs.
The aim of the new inspection sign information system was to simplify and informatize the system ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control signs intended for the designation of consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A customer of the control marks who wants to collect checks under the 'new system' must request the customs office to issue inspection signs electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of control signs is obliged to request their release, report data resulting from national legislation of SR and keep the registration of control signs.
The control mark is entitled to print the state company Mint Kremnice.
FŘ SR exercises tax oversight of handling and disposal of the control marks in the printer.
FG SR is required to ensure the presence of a staff member of the financial directorate in the printer when handling the checks marks.
FŘ SR guarantees the sale of control signs to the customer of the printer's check stamps.
Control signs can be removed only in the printer from the employee of the Financial Directorate.
A tax warehouse operator or tobacco importer may mark the packaging of tobacco packaging.
Consumer packaging of cigars or cigarillos with a control mark may be marked by the tax warehouse operator, tobacco importer or the beneficiary.
Only a check mark whose data correspond to the character of the validity of the excise duty rate shall be used to indicate the consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos.
It is only possible to mark the consumer pack of cigarettes with a check mark in the business that made them.
The number of ordered pieces of inspection stamps must not be less than 500 pieces or multiple of them.
CÚ shall electronically notify the customer of the control signs of the number of inspection marks he can remove, the price of the check mark and the FR SR account number.
CÚ may reduce the number of orders of inspection signs if circumstances are arising that it is reasonable to assume that tax rules may be infringed.
FŘ SR will determine the date of taking over of the inspection marks by the customer of the inspection marks, but within 10 days at the latest.
The date of taking over of the control marks of the FG SR shall be notified to the customer of the inspection marks via the electronic system of the inspection marks.
The control marks are issued by the financial directorate exclusively in the printing works, but only after the receipt of the funds corresponding to their price to the relevant account specified in the customs office's electronic notification.
The customer of the control marks is obliged separately for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco to keep the registration of the check signs in the electronic control system.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 The ELO department and SPD systems of the excise duty department of the FD SR is responsible for securing the exchange of information on request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent financial management authorities.
These are especially applications for inspection of operators in the context of the management of excise duties, requests for information regarding the management of excise duties and also requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications is made in electronic form within the EMCS system.
The following actions are included in the administrative cooperation between EU Member States: applications for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on the management of excise duties, application for confirmation of registration in SEED); response to the request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Permission and registration
In SR, permanent tax oversight is applied to alcohol warehouses, in the Czech Republic, this supervision is replaced by the tax manager's continuous supervision via a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic small independent breweries are in tax storage, in SR they are only registered by the tax manager.
The Institute of Registered Consignor is introduced in SR, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In SR, it is possible to burn 43 l at a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in case of growing burning.
In contrast, in the Czech Republic, the reduced rate of alcohol tax can be applied only to 30 l and.
Growing moonshine in SR must have permission not only from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development, but also from the tax manager.
Only the Ministry of Agriculture permits in the Czech Republic.
In SR, imports of the consumer packaging of alcohol are made in addition to the tax warehouse operator, by the importer of the packaging of alcohol.
The authorization of the importer shall be subject to registration of the applicant with the excise duty manager.
No special permission of the tax administrator is required in the Czech Republic to import alcohol packaging.
In SR, the sale of the consumer packaging of alcohol is conditional on issuing the authorization of the tax administrator for the seller.
The seller of the consumer packaging of alcohol has a lawful obligation to keep the registration, including. about buying and selling.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any authorization for final sellers of the alcohol packaging, issuing a concession for the sale of alcohol by the business office is sufficient; the final seller does not keep any special registration.
In the SR of the fuel seller must have permission from the tax administrator to sell them.
National legislation in the SR does not modify any special regulation of the gas station, all activities regarding gas stations are regulated only in the excise duty law on mineral oils.
In the Czech Republic, the gas station regulates a special fuel law, but the tax manager does not issue any permission to sell fuel.
Gas stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In SR it is not technically possible to obtain a list of filling stations from the financial management system.
Since 2012 there has been a significant increase in the number of selected authorisations or tax registrations.
This increase was due to legislative change in the specified period.
In the Czech Republic, on the contrary, the number of permits selected in 2013 decreased significantly due to the introduction of bail for fuel distributors.
Administrative actions
In the SR, substantive legislation provides for tax control duty on selected tax entities.
This issue is specified by the internal control act issued by the FR SR due to the application of the uniform procedure of tax administrators in the territory of SR.
In the Czech Republic, material legislation does not modify tax control requirements, procedural law provides only the possibility of carrying out a check no later than the deadline for taxation.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax checks carried out and local investigations in SR and Czech Republic is that the internal management act of the FŘ SR determines in which cases and time limits the tax administrator must carry out a tax check, while in the Czech Republic the amount of excise duty is correct or its return is verified especially by local inquiries.
Since 2012, the number of comparable administrative operations in the Czech Republic has increased due to an increase in the number of transports in EMCS and at the same time due to an increase in the number of tax returns filed.
In SR, the number of administrative operations between 2012 and 2015 had a slightly increasing trend, which was influenced by the increasing number of EMCS transports and at the same time a decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
Different legislative arrangements have been shown on the large differences between the number of comparable permits and the registration of tax entities.
The number of comparable administrative actions of tax administrators was similar in the SR and Czech Republic in the various years of the controlled period.
In SR, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds compared to the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for about the same amount of administrative operations.
From the above, it can be stated that the SR is more focused on the execution of administrative tasks by tax administrators, e.g. the exercise of physical tax oversight.
In the Czech Republic, the emphasis is placed on distant supervision, e.g. tracking device, immediate data transmission via web interface and risk analysis.
Electronization of administrative operations
Electronization of administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax return can be filed via a data box.
Customs administration of the Czech Republic introduced the so-called. interactive tax returns forms, which cannot be processed any longer.
The data must be further rewritten to the tax entity's personal tax account.
The benefit is to reduce the error rate of tax returns (DAP), which will save the tax administrator's actions related to the corrections of the wrong DAP filed.
DGC is working on a new application for DAP electronic processing.
Smart forms can further: tax applications or registration for activity and notification of changes in data, claim tax refund claims, fulfil notification requirements when handling special mineral oils, handling raw tobacco and fulfilling biofuels duties.
The handling of control bands is recorded by tax entities in the ORO WebClient information system, which is available for registered entities to register by the tax administrator of specified data.
Transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under a tax exemption regime must be carried out in the Czech Republic based on an electronic accompanying document implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality into the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transport of selected products in free tax circulation around the Czech Republic can always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, proof of excise duty, decision of the customs office to release the selected products under the customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision to measure excise duty.
The required content of the data is laid down by legislation.
The Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for the issuing of alternative documents to facilitate the performance of these duties (§ 5 and § 6 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the documentary form of documents to replace or supplement electronically issued documents, which are sent to a data warehouse via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, where each such document is assigned a unique twelve-digit identification code (JIK).
JIK serves for the purpose of inspection by customs authorities on the road and prevents repeated transportation on the same document.
For the largest operator of the tax warehouse of fuel in the Czech Republic, which places about half of the volume of PHM into free tax circulation, the CS Czech Republic has online access to the electronic registration system, where the body automatically deposits tax documents.
CS Czech Republic is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. electronic system for registration and monitoring of transport of selected products in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70 % of the current functional EMCS specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for declarant and customs officers.
It will also be connected to the system of global guarantees, tax registry or risk analysis system.
The system should provide an overview of transport in free circulation between Member States, which is still working on the basis of written documents without registration and the sharing of negotiating numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure for registration of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in the abuse of a simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronization of administrative operations in SR
In the management of excise duties, the SR financial administration uses electronic communication to monitor the movement of goods in EMCS under the conditions of tax exemption, control signs, filing tax returns and also when tax entities register and registering.
One-way electronic communication of tax entities with tax administrator was also introduced in 2014, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016
Within electronic communications, the tax agency has accessible a personal internet zone, called after entering access data. an electronic personal box designed for communication with financial management.
Within this zone, the tax agency has access to the e-mailroom through which it submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents related to the management of excise duties.
However, electronic communication through a personal internet zone does not concern all tax entities.
National legislation defines tax entities who are obliged to communicate with the tax administrator electronically.
This is mainly a payer of value added tax, a tax advisor representing the tax body and attorneys representing the tax body.
NKÚ SR also addressed the issue of the extent of the electronization of excise duty management during the inspection.
These were only fully electronic operations, tax returns and electronic communication within ELO.
If the EMCS traffic is taken away, there has been an increase in electronization of selected comparable administrative operations, which is also a requirement for modern tax management.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Fully electronized processing of tax returns is already in place in SR, from its filing to registration of tax liability.
In the Czech Republic, electronic processing of tax returns is not set.
In the Czech Republic, the possibility for tax entities to insert compulsory documents for individual transport in free tax circulation on the website.
In the future, the announcement of free tax circulation transport in the form and based on EMCS system is prepared.
Evaluation
The system of reporting transport in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax oversight, thus eliminating the transport of selected products, where excise duty has not been paid in violation of legislation.
These can be recommended as a good practice.

Analysis of changes in organisational structure and personnel security in excise duty
The organisational arrangement of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the SR has undergone major changes.
Organizational arrangement of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
Customs administration of the Czech Republic from 1. 1. 2013 is composed of the Directorate-General of Customs and Customs offices, which are administrative offices and organizational agencies of the state.
DGC is an entity for the entire customs administration.
Customs administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out comprehensive management of excise duties since 2004 as one of the many competences it ensures.
CS Czech Republic continues to perform:
(a) check:
śaśa road transport (weighing of trucks, paying fees for the use of road roads, fulfilling conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and international passenger transport matters),
śaśa waste management and packaging material,
śaśa the safety of imported food,
śaśa in the field of consumer protection and protection of intellectual property rights,
śaśa employment of foreigners,
b) customs management - this is a comprehensive application of customs regulations, commercial policy measures and formalities for import and export of goods,
(c) the selection and enforcement of cash transactions imposed by other public authorities within the divisional administration;
(d) the activities of the police authority (designated customs authorities) in criminal proceedings committed by violations of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Czech Customs Administration is the tax administrator.
Although the scope of competences (set of control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there is a cost savings of the extent, because the public administration does not have to incur costs on the position of the control group for each subject of the inspection independently.
At the same time, the administrative burden of controlled persons is reduced by repeated inspection.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic continues to exercise its competence from 1. 12. 2016 to verify the performance of the duties in the registration of sales (§ 2 paragraph 2). Article 2 of Law No. 112/2016 Coll., on sales registration) and from 1. 1. 2017 supervision of compliance with the law and conditions of the operation of gambling, including penalties (Section 116 of Law No. 186/2016 Coll., about gambling).
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has changed the three-step structure to two-stage structure with effect from 1. 1. 2013, with the cancellation of the middle article of the procedure (customs directorates).
DGC spent about 51 miles on the project. Kč (i.e. approx. 2 031 000 €).
The CS Czech Republic from 1. 1. 2013 is DGC and regional customs offices, which are administrative and organizational components of the state.
Customs offices and their competence are laid down by law, the management of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through separation and territorial workplaces.
Territorial workplaces are internal organizing units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled to set up and disturb the territorial workplace and determine their factual competence.
Legislation does not provide for any competence for the territorial workplace; the territorial workplace exercises the duties of the customs office on its behalf.
Organizational structure until 12. 31. 2012
Organization structure from 1. 1. 2013
DGC, eight CŘ and 2012 58 separation (including branches) were executed until 31. August 12. total of 67 unions and departments.
As of 1. June 1., DGC and 51 departments in CÚ and their territorial workplaces, eight workplaces of the DGC legal department and a units providing mobile oversight, i.e. Approx. 60 places.
The costs of CS Czech Republic significantly affect wage costs.
Due to the reorganization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there was no saving of personnel resources.
The execution of main processes is ensured by customs officers in service under the Law on the service of security corps members.
The possibility of reducing the number of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, because according to the provisions of Section 42 (42). Article 1 of Law No. 361/2003 Coll., on the service of security corps members, can be released from the service only in cases of taxatively defined.
Reduction of service posts due to organisational changes in the security corps is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure the allocation of adequate services within the corps and, where appropriate, to secure jobs with another security corps (e.g. Police of the Czech Republic, Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise they will put them in a deposit for the temporary non-inclusion, where members of security corps belong to 80 % of the average service income according to the law.

Organizational arrangement of excise duty management in SR
The Government of the Slovak Republic has established itself as one of the priorities of completion of tax administration reform through the UNITAS programme, which will secure additional budgetary resources by combining tax collection, customs and levies and suppression of tax evasion.
In this context, tax reform was implemented at central level, which brought the merger of the SR Tax Directorate and the SR Customs Directorate into the SR Financial Directorate and the creation of financial management.
FŘ SR was set up on 2012 1. 1. by law no. 333/2011 Z. z., about government agencies in the field of taxes, fees and customs, as last amended, as a budgetary organization based in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
FŘ SR, CÚ and the Criminal Office of Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No. 199/2004 Z. z., Customs law and amendment of certain laws, as last amended, are customs authorities if they carry out tasks under customs regulations.
In the sense of law no. 333/2011 Z. z., about the state administration bodies in the field of taxes, fees and customs, as last amended, together with the tax authorities form financial management.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration on 1. January 2012 is the Finance Directorate of the SR, the Criminal Financial Administration, the Competence Center of Financial Operations, the tax authorities, the tax office for selected tax entities, branches of tax offices, the tax offices, the customs offices, branches of customs offices (branch CÚ tax, branch CÚ combined, branch CÚ customs) and customs office station.
The main mission of the FD SR is the effective collection and management of taxes and customs, i.e. also excise duties, fulfil the income part of the state budget and protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the FG SR is the president of the financial administration, nominated and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The President of the Financial Administration is responsible for the operation of the whole financial administration and therefore also for the activities of the FG SR, which he directs and represents in its entirety.
Organizing structure FŘ SR from 1. 1. 2012 in short form
Within all customs offices in the territory of the SR, excise duty management activities and processes provide, apart from branches of customs offices (38 branches) and customs offices (18 stations), excise duty separation (9 departments) and legal separation (9st department).

In SR, the number of tax entities is about a third of the number of employees in the field of excise duty management compared to the state in the Czech Republic; the impact of higher employees on the efficiency of excise duty management is not apparent.
EMCS system
According to the preamble of Decision No of the European Parliament and of the Council Article 1152/2003 (1152/2003) EC of 16. June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty, aimed at establishing an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information to be acquired on transport and to carry out the prescribed checks, simplify intra-Community movement of goods under suspension arrangements.
During the implementation of the system, Member States should allow operators, especially SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements with the lowest possible costs.
Article 3 of the said EP and Council Decision admits to include national specifications, national database forming part of the system and technical or software that the Member State deems necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in Czech Republic
Development and functionality of EMCS system
In the Czech Republic, the EMCS system was preceded by the system of registration of selected products (EVVV), which was operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
The EMCS is fully functional in the Czech Republic from 1. 4. 2010 and is continuously supplemented by European and national functionality (see Annex No. 5).
The so-called was introduced in the Czech Republic. Customs module and declarant module.
Customs module contains a number of national functions.
Transports under the EMCS system are monitored beyond the Community system in the EMCS system, started and ended in the Czech Republic.
The system ensures, after approval of a notice of receipt of a consignment intended for a beneficiary for one-time acceptance of the automatic transmission of information to the tax agency registry with subsequent invalidation of the permit.
The administration of accepted and sent applications for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO is fully ensured through the system, including sending replies with an attachment in any format and providing translations.
A report on manual termination of ECS exports is also allowed (only the transfer of an auto-created message is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS system does not allow e-AD approval or acceptance notice without the competent customs authority's reaction to a risk profile (risk profile cannot be ignored).
The Declarant module is available for tax entities for free, it has the form of a web application, where the user logs into using the username and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with the CS Czech Republic.
Each act against the EMCS customs module shall be accompanied by a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declarant module.
The Declarant Module enables tax entities to direct registration of data on initiated and terminated transport under the tax exemption regime, so tax entities do not have to spend funds on the acquisition of the system.
The national functionality of the declarant module allows you to load and store data off-line (saves time for frequently used data), fill in recipient data based on SEED ID check and require compulsory completion of data that are optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for every consignment consigned from the Czech Republic to block the security of excise duty in the corresponding amount of taxable transactions until the end of transport.
The amount of security is calculated automatically by EMCS.
Without sufficient amount of collateral it is not possible to send e-AD design for approval to CÚ shipment from the EMCS declarant module.
Each warranty has a unique number and contains ARC transport (including the amount of blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The tax operator can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it sees the current amount of blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantees.
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS system
The EMCS development was implemented on the basis of eight execution contracts from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46 791 (i.e. 1 412,56 761.) without VAT.
In accordance with the contracts concluded, the contractor issued invoices from 2006 to the end of 2015 for a total amount of CZK 43 577 (i.e. 1 401,10 640.) without VAT.
During the controlled period, the EMCS upgrade was incurred with výdaje 14 incl. VAT (i.e. 547 438,99).
The amount spent on the EMCS upgrade during the controlled period and converted into one EMCS transport is on average 16,49 CZK (i.e. 0,62 €), without national transport, these costs in conversion into one transport between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States are CZK 24,40 (i.e. 0,92 €).
The EMCS technical support was implemented under four contracts with execution from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015 the total amount of technical support of CZK 7 499 (i.e. 281 389,77) including value added tax.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on one transport inserted into the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6,18 (i.e. 0,23 €).
Development and technical support invoices covered national solutions and developed the EVV application, which DGC had already operated before EMCS itself.
The invoices were paid under programming funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of service supply and other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS system is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under suspension regime.
Replaced the accompanying administrative document - the SAD used before the effectiveness of this system, thus ensuring better control and traffic control.
The SR has been introduced since 1. 4. 2010 and is continuously supplemented by requirements resulting from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, called.
ARC code under which you can monitor this transport online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS system
The EMCS system ensures the receiving and dispatch of excise goods by tax entities entitled to use the EMCS system, thus reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest development of functionalities occurred in 2011, when EMCS was fully introduced into operation (see Annex No. 6).
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS system
The introduction of EMCS was implemented as another module of application equipment SysNeD and therefore it is not possible to accurately determine the amount of costs of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of EMCS was to replace a system based on administration of transport in a documentary form.
The benefit of EMCS system is a comprehensive overview of transport between Member States within the EU from the notification of transport to its termination - reducing administrative costs for tax administrators and tax operators for processing, transfer and document archiving is important.
In the Czech Republic and SR, national functionality has been introduced into EMCS system, allowing traffic monitoring in a conditional system between two places in the Czech Republic or. in SR.
In addition, automatic functionality of online monitoring and ensuring a guarantee for excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
A national functionality is also introduced to monitor the risk of the tax entity or. Transportation, with subsequent compulsory response by the tax manager.
The SR and the Czech Republic register a comparable number of transport within the EU in the EMCS system.
However, the costs incurred in SR to upgrade this system were byly 744 higher between 2012 and 2015 than in the Czech Republic.
NKÚ SR received data from the FR SR on upgrade of EMCS system only for the period from 2011, although this system has been established and operated before.
Yet the costs incurred on upgrading EMCS system in SR were byly 188 higher than the costs of introducing and upgrading the EMCS system in about ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
For a controlled period, the volume of expenditure related to the EMCS upgrade in SR in conversion to one transport exceeds costs of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the Czech Republic and the NKU SR met the goals.
Both control institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the excise tax management system in the Czech Republic and SR.
Despite the common basic legal framework, it has been found that there are significant differences in both tax systems that affect the efficiency of the management of excise taxes.
During parallel checks, examples of good practice were found, which could contribute to reducing tax fraud, their importance with rising tax rates will increase.
Procedures have also been identified to reduce the cost of excise duty management.
Cross-cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect tax management efficiency and limit international comparison unless mutually coordinated deep checks are carried out with tax administrator.
In this the role of the highest control institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of parallel control of value added tax management carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The Lim Declaration of 1977 emphasizes that the Supreme Supervisory Institutions (SAI) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenue to be controlled to the extent possible.
The European Organization of the Highest Supervisory Institutions (EUROSAI) considers it one of the most important components of public tax revenue.
VI. EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of SAI public revenue.
An important step towards optimizing SAI control activity is the development of a special strategy for public revenue auditing.
This applies especially to taxes as the most complex source of public income, which is most prone to great losses.
Since the economies of individual states are increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may, to some extent, be unable to carry out a control activity without cooperating with the SAI of another state.
An example is an audit of internationally organized fraud, which causes significant losses in the revenue of many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs that carry out the inspection in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation between themselves.
Just on VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn was created by the idea of checking the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as ′′ VAT ′′) and VIES system in the cooperation of the Supreme Supervisory Authority and the Federal Court of Auditors, Bundesrechnungshof.
Careful preparation followed, when both parties first had to acquaint themselves with the legal environment and procedures for VAT management in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics included in the control programme was made.
Achieving effective and efficient VAT management is a long-term problem and individual states (especially Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of this tax available.
We believe that the results of our control can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrators, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the international information exchange system.
Report on the results of parallel checks on value added tax management performed in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2-2005-1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax administration after the Czech accession to the European Union
(D) Verification of administrative cooperation in value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) No Commission Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 1925/2004
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the control action in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the management of value added tax following the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter the EU) associated with the free movement of goods and services and to check the use of the VIES system, especially when checking the application of the value added tax exemption for intracommunitary delivery.
(D) The aim of the inspection was to examine the system of control of intracommunitary value added tax with a special focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the abovementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
The system of exchange of value added tax information The Surveillance Authority, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ ′′) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter ′′ BRH ′′) in mutual cooperation under a contract concluded between the two inspection institutions on 8. June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the verification of selected commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Germany ′′), the use of information obtained by means of international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of VAT management systems of both countries.
Joint final report on the results of the inspection actions has been processed within the meaning of the European Directive No. 31 to implement INTOSAI audit standards.
The period controlled was from 1. August 2004 to 31. August 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Parallel VAT management inspection in Czech Republic and Germany was performed under agreement between the two SAIs.
Outside the main point - exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No Commission Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 1925/2004-the inspection covered other topics, such as payer registration, VAT tax returns and summary reports closely linked to the main point.
In addition, part of the inspection included the legal situation in the international bus transport of passengers and comparing some statistics.
The comparison of the VAT management systems of both countries identified differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany business owners are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic, the first criterion (among others) is for registration exceeding the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, only one tax identification number is assigned to payers, which they also use in intracommunitary transactions.
In Germany, VAT payers are assigned a tax number, used only for business transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracommunitary transactions, he must request an assignment of a special identification number called. VAT ID.
Since different methods of registration cause problems, conditions should be offset throughout the EU (see. 4.1).
2) International bus transport of persons.
In the Czech Republic, international bus transport of persons is exempted from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, part of the shipment taking place on German territory is subject to VAT.
At EU level efforts should be made to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of VAT (see. 4.2)
3) VAT tax return.
While in the Czech Republic, payers filed tax returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany, payers are entitled to submit so-called. preliminary tax returns for VAT (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they must submit an annual VAT return.
Unlike the Czech Republic of payers, payers in Germany are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to submit VAT tax returns in the Czech Republic electronically would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see. 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While the payers report summary reports to the financial authorities in the Czech Republic, the payers report summary reports to the CLO in Germany.
Therefore, data from summary reports are available immediately after submission of the financial authorities in Czech Republic.
German financial authorities have information from summary reports only after processing it into CLO.
Fighting VAT fraud requires updated intra-communitarian transaction information to be available as soon as possible.
Monthly summary reporting would shorten the time shift between the date of transaction and VIES data update.
This would subsequently allow early examination of taxation in the Member State of the customer (see. 4.4).
Which would, however, require all Member States to accept the same deadline for submitting a summary report.
5) International exchange of VAT information.
Czech CLO monitors the three-month deadline for information received.
German CLO does not follow the past time.
Consequently, the German tax administration dealt with significantly lower percentage of the applications received within the specified deadline.
Due to these problems, BRH recommended the German CLO to carry out permanent warnings (see. 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States develop their own risk management system (hereinafter referred to as ′′ RMS ′′) that has its strengths and weaknesses.
NKÚ and BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of RMS must be exchanged and introduced in each EU Member State, otherwise the scammers will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, both SAIs tested selected cases of intracommunitary transactions between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Thirty-one cases of commercial transactions were examined together with the application of the CLO legislation, where there were doubts about their effectiveness or suspicion of tax evasion on VAT.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained through international cooperation and measured VAT tax liability for the payers.
In these cases, payers either unduly claimed the right to exemption from VAT or did not admit the acquisition of goods in VAT tax return.
In some cases the financial authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases the information could not be used due to various legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to the request for information.
Cases were found where payers misplaced commercial transactions in summary reports.
As a result, VIES data were incorrect and tax administration had to check these cases (see. 6.).

The control was part of the 2006 control plan and was therefore notified to the Federal MF in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
