4. Value Added Tax Administration in Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
The tax subject is according to law No. 337/1992 Coll., on the management of taxes and fees (hereinafter referred to as ' Law No. 337/1992 Coll.") means taxpayer, tax payer and legal successor to a natural or legal person who is defined as a tax entity by law.
On June 31., 2004, 421 tax entities were registered in the Czech Republic.
There was an increase in the number of tax entities registered for VAT to 457 590.
A taxable person who has a registered office, place of business or an establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover will exceed 000 1 CZK (EUR 33 575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months, becomes a payer from the 1. th day of the third month following the month in which it exceeded the registration limit (§ 94 paragraph 94). Article 1 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax; hereinafter referred to as ′′ Act No. 235/2004 Coll.").
The application for registration is required within 15 days after the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow the taxable person to register the so-called taxable person. retrospectively where the reason for registration is to exceed the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or an establishment in the Czech Republic, who makes taxable transactions or transactions exempted from VAT with a right to deduct, can become a tax payer, even if he does not exceed the turnover of 1 000 CZK (33 EUR 575) if they meet any of the other conditions laid down in Law No. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not fulfil any of the conditions laid down by law can apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The delivery of the application to register to the local tax administrator is initiated by law No. 337/1992 Coll.
Voluntary VAT payer on the VAT registration application will also indicate the date on which he asks for registration as VAT payer.
Tax administrator data communicated by the tax agency i.e. filed application for registration with all attachments, will be checked.
If he has doubts about the data, he will invite the tax agency to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After verifying that the tax agency fulfils the conditions for registration, the tax agency issues a decision in the form of a certificate that the tax body is registered and has been given a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as 'the tax ID').
The certificate shall indicate the tax administrator's date of effectiveness of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the tax period.
The delivery period is a calendar quarter, unless the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year has reached CZK 10 000 (EUR 335 750).
If the turnover of the payer for the previous calendar year reached CZK 10 000 (EUR 335 750), the tax period is the calendar month.
The payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 2 000 (EUR 67 150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and will notify the tax manager of the taxation.
This segmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the VAT in the registration certificate is always of a constitutional character and the tax body is obliged to state in all cases communications (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law (e.g. law no. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The ID number contains the code ′′ CZ ′′ and the tribal part consisting of the general identifier.
The general identifier is the birth number for a natural person or. another general identifier, if such a special law, and for a legal person an identification number (clause § 33 (33). Article 12 of Law No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax body has failed to fulfil its registration obligation or at the call of the tax manager, the local tax manager shall register it without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issue of the Ex officio Registration Certificate, which is served on the tax body.
In the Czech Republic, the tax agency that has been entitled to business activities is allocated a tax ID at the moment of its first registration for any tax.
The tax entity uses the same tax ID even if registered as VAT payer.
According to the wording of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., which has been effective from 1. 1. 2005, the tax administrator may, in case of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, pay a taxable person up to 10 % of the total income or income for taxable transactions carried out illegally without tax, for the period from the date on which he was supposed to be a registered payer by law until the date on which the tax manager decided to become a registered payer (Article 98 (98) of the basic Regulation). Article 1 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined is considered to be a tax deduction (§ 98 paragraph 98). Article 3 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it's not about sanctions.
Revocation of VAT payer registration when legally established conditions are met is possible for two reasons:
1)
Revocation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover that does not exceed the registration limit (§ 106 paragraph 106). Article 1 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to apply for cancellation of registration at the earliest after 1 year after the expiry date of effectiveness given on the registration certificate.
2) Revocation of the ′′ official power ′′ registration (§ 106 (106) Article 7 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll.), if: (a) the payer has not made the tax administrator without notification for 12 consecutive months of fulfilment, (b) the payer does not fulfil his obligations under Law No. 235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who have no registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic Tax registered in another Member State who has no registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who takes place with the place of delivery in the country and is a person liable to admit and pay tax on such transactions under Section 108 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. (so-called. ′′ non-established payer ′′), becomes payer on the day of this delivery.
This person is obliged to apply for registration to the IRS for Prague 1 no later than the date of implementation.
In the registration application, it is required to state all the VAT paid to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If the ′′ unused ′′ payer submits an application for registration later than on the date of the first taxable operation in the Czech Republic, the Financial Office for Prague 1 will register it retroactively because according to law No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax body became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable operation in the Czech Republic.
During retroactive registration, the Finance Office for Prague 1 requires tax entities proof that the performance has been performed (invoices or. explanatory letters).
If a ′′ non-established ′′ tax entity applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable operation takes place, the Finance Office for Prague 1 asks for the presentation of contracts that the execution takes place.
473 ′′ non-established ′′ payers were registered at the Czech Republic for Prague 1, of which 124 payers from Germany and registered as of 31. 12. 2005 951 ′′ non-established ′′ payers, of which 233 payers from Germany.
According to the provisions of Section 106 (106) Article 9 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the registration of the ′′ non-established ′′ payer on 31. January of the following calendar year, unless the payer has been incurred during the current calendar year.
The NKÚ check found that if the ′′ non-established ′′ payer filed a tax return abroad for postal transport on January 25., i.e. in accordance with the law in the deadline for filing tax returns, the tax office does not often have it available on January 31.
In cases where the facts are relevant for the possibility of cancelling registration to the tax office later than on 31. January, it is no longer possible to cancel the ′′ non-established ′′ payer's VAT registration in the Czech Republic.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§§ 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as ′′ AO ′′), anyone who is engaged in business is obliged to inform the municipal / municipal office or the relevant financial authority.
The deadline for submission of information is one month after the business starts.
This information is processed by the municipal / municipal office for the tax office.
If the IRS detects an undertaking that started the operation but did not register, the competent tax authority may register this payer with official power - even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-residents in Germany are legally obliged to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Section 2 of the German VAT Act (UStG).
This obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover they execute.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
For business owners permanently residing abroad there are special financial authorities.
For example, for those who are located in the Czech Republic, Chemnitz-Süd is the competent tax office.
On April 30., 2004, 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office; on March 1., 2006, a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
BRH found that these special financial authorities often refused registration called. semi-dependent independent workers based in the new Eastern EU Member States.
Since employee s' work permits from ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers tried to avoid these restrictions by starting their business.
These companies do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in § 2 UStG because they are usually dependent on a single employer to determine their working hours and the way they perform their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire of the competent financial authority, where he must provide information about the company and the activities he / she performs.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding on all financial authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the financial authorities or by universal services responsible for the assessment of taxpayers.
Through this form, a risk assessment of individual taxpayers is performed before the tax office gives out the tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions follows certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the competent financial authority, the following three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the financial office, another five (or four) are to distinguish payers, with the last one always the check numbers.
If an entrepreneur intends to participate in an intracommunitary trade, he needs a VAT identification number to receive tax exempt intracommunitary delivery.
CLO allocates VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and has a VAT tax number.
CLO allocates VAT ID to entrepreneurs automatically when the payer automatically gives intra-communitarian delivery in their VAT return.
VAT ID structure is a country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Entrepreneur registration can be cancelled: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business), after all administrative work (assessment for all marketing years) and 2. if the tax administration realizes that he is no longer developing business activity.
The validity of the VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of the VAT number.
In these cases, the tax authorities are required to inform the CLO of the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can expire the VAT identification number.
According to German VAT Act (§ 19 (1) UStG) tax residents in Germany are not liable to pay VAT in case of 1. that turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. the following year is likely to not exceed EUR 50 000
So-called small business owners (′′ Kleinunternehmer ′′) are not entitled to invoice other entrepreneurs VAT and are not entitled to deduct entry tax.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small business owners must be registered at the IRS and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small businessman can claim that there will be no provision § 19 (19) of the basic Regulation. 1 UStG apply.
This confession is binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct tax on entry.
For tax non-residents there is an option to appoint tax representatives (§ 22 and UStG).
It is an essential prerequisite that they carry out exclusively tax exempt commercial operations and not be entitled to deduct the entry tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfil the tax liability of a foreign businessman, who does not have to register for VAT.
The invoices must include information about representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany business owners are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic, the first criterion (among others) is for registration exceeding the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
If the tax body in the Czech Republic does not exceed the limit, it has the option to apply voluntarily for VAT registration.
Registration procedure is standardized in Germany, but different organizational models in the federal states may cause different.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is assigned a tax ID at the moment of his first registration.
In case the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same ID for intracommunitary transactions.
In Germany, the payer is given a tax number for registration for VAT, only for business transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracommunitary transactions, he must request an assignment of a special identification number called. VAT ID.
As NKÚ and BRH have identified, the German two-stage registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as in the Czech Republic, which allocates a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intracommunitary transactions.
On the other hand, the two-stage system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform municipalities or the competent financial authority about their business.
This retroactive registration allows correct VAT measurement for previous taxation period, especially accurate estimation of VAT tax liability.
Since different ways of registration cause problems, conditions should be offset throughout the EU.
The German parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as the ID).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate the VAT at birth of a natural person.
This VAT will be valid throughout the life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the competent tax authority will ask for an economic ID, which will be used as a VAT ID.
There should be no delay in the future between national payer registration and VAT ID allocation.
The work on the introduction of an IT device to manage the VAT has not yet been completed.
International bus transport of persons
Legislation in the Czech Republic
According to the provisions of Section 70 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. the transport of persons between Member States and between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempted from VAT with the right to deduct the tax.
This transport is exempted from VAT, even if it is performed by tax-registered entrepreneurs in other Member States or by a taxable foreign person.
Return transport is considered to be separate transportation.
If ′′ non-established ′′ tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out other economic activity besides international bus transport of persons, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International transport of persons in the Czech Republic was exempted from VAT based on the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V kap. Article 5 (5) of the Treaty 1 (1) (b) where it is stated:
' For the purposes of Article Article 28 (28) of the Treaty 3 (3) (b) Directive 77/388 / EEC may the Czech Republic continue to exempt the value added tax on international passenger transport under point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 17 (17) is met. Article 28 (28) of the Treaty Article 4 (4) of the directive or while the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier."
Description of the legislation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC of 28. November 2006, implemented by § 3 b (3). 1 German VAT Act is the place of delivery of passengers (i.e. transport services) route (i.e. place) where the transport takes place.
The German tax system therefore does not distinguish between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only the part of the route that takes place in Germany represents a taxable provision of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If a tax non-resident transports passengers through Germany, the part of the route that takes place in Germany is also a taxable provision of transport.
A tax non-resident must notify his intention to provide passenger transport to the competent financial authority before he performs his services in Germany.
The IRS will register this non-resident tax (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach specified in the taxpayer's notice.
The taxpayer is obliged to admit his taxable transportation provided in German tax return to VAT.
On March 1., 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Finance Authority registered 741 Czech payers, who engaged in passenger transport.
If passenger transport is provided to a tax resident who is a VAT taxable person, the tax non-resident does not have to pay VAT to the tax office itself.
Instead, the tax resident who is the body who is liable to pay VAT to the tax authority and the net bill to the tax nonresident is the tax resident who is the recipient of the services; this process is known as the ′′ reverse charge ′′ and is in accordance with Article 196 Council Directive 2006/112 / EC.
In addition to the tax non-resident notification and his tax return on VAT, the German tax administration has several means to assess the correctness of the taxable provision of passenger transportation.
Customs office mobile inspection groups audit buses licensed (licensed) licenses for foreign transport used to transport passengers via Germany.
After each audit, mobile control groups shall send a control message to the competent financial authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to demand VAT payment from the bus driver before continuing further transport.
A non-resident tax deduction of the VAT paid thus calculated in his VAT tax return.
If the IRS has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may announce the intention to carry out an audit that must be held in the office of the IRS or may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if the tax non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT measured in accordance with its legal rate, the tax authority may apply for administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308 / EEC.
If a review of VAT tax return or the discharge of tax non-resident tax duties is to be carried out, BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too demanding in terms of workforce compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable provision of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the tax non-resident accounts raises disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
Tax administration must audit foreign accounting, which does not only mean the need for foreign language knowledge, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger transports taking place in Germany.
On the other hand, the tax non-resident may not only accept the right to carry out the checks due to his national tax administration, but also the right to audit by other Member States in which he transports passengers.
In addition, in every Member State in which only one provision of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all the tax liabilities applicable to him in these Member States, in all languages and on all tax forms of these Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transportation therefore incurs disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the Czech Republic there is transport of persons between individual EU Member States or. between Member States and third countries, under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic exempted from VAT with the right to deduct tax.
In Germany, the part of the transport taking place on German territory is taxable.
If this transport is provided by a non-established payer in Germany for the first time, it is required to inform the competent financial authority of the delivery of the transport.
The tax office of this payer registers and the payer is obliged to admit taxable supply of part of the transport in the tax return in the Germany.
Implementing the law is very time consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Finance Office are in passenger transport.
Compared to a given effort, the tax return, when implemented, is rather low.
Member States collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC of 28. November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time consuming duties without a financially sensitive outcome.
In order to avoid excessive costs to measure VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in one Member State only.
This could be the state where the transport starts or where the provider is located.
Such taxation would require modification of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC.
VAT tax returns
Submission and processing of tax returns for VAT in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to submit a VAT tax return on the form prescribed by MF within 25 days after the end of the tax period, even if the law does not provide otherwise.
Own tax liability is due within the deadline for filing VAT tax return, except for the tax charged with the importation of goods under Section 20 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., for which the maturity of the tax is laid down by customs regulations.
If a refundable overpayment is caused due to the measurement of excessive deduction, the payer will return without request within 30 days of the measurement of excessive deduction.
The deadline is not applied when the tax manager initiates tax proceedings regarding the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73 (73). Article 11 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. the right to deduct the tax deduction may be applied in the proper VAT tax return no later than the last tax period of the calendar year in which the tax deduction could be applied.
Upon expiry of this period, the right to deduct the tax deduction may be further applied within 3 years of the end of the tax period in which the right to deduct the tax may have been applied first.
However, this is only possible by submitting additional tax return to VAT.
Amendment to law no. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1. 1. 2005 allows additional tax return to VAT only for the period when the right to deduct the tax deduction could be applied for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit additional VAT tax return if (a) the aggregate of the corrections increases the tax liability, (b) makes a repair where the last known tax liability does not change, but only data by the tax entity previously tempered, (c) makes the rate corrected and the amount of the tax according to Section 49 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit additional tax return to VAT if it reduces the tax liability by a summary of corrections.
Additional VAT tax return to the payer is required to submit by the end of the month following the finding of these facts.
Submission of tax return to VAT in electronic form can be carried out via the Internet network or on a technical data medium.
Submission after the Internet can be performed as a data report with a guaranteed electronic signature or as a submission with a data message without a guaranteed electronic signature.
In case of filing with a data report not guaranteed electronic signature, submission in writing is still required, i.e. delivery of the computer assembly to the tax administrator (e-form).
VAT tax return contains separate rows regarding intracommunitary supply / acquisition values.
Values of the acquisition of services are reported on special rows of VAT tax return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of initial automated inspection within ADIS.
Values of supply of goods to other Member States to taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with the information given in the summary reports submitted by Czech payers.
The values of acquisition of goods from other Member States from tax persons in other Member States shall be compared with the values obtained through VIES system from the summary report of payers from other EU Member States.
The IRS is undergoing a test of credibility of VAT tax returns under the ADIS system.
This test is performed automatically, because without the test, tax returns to VAT cannot be measured.
The credibility test involves calculating the credibility criteria and evaluating risk types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of Section 37 (37) Article 1 of Law No. 337/1992 Coll. the tax authority may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2 000 (67 150) on a non-cash basis on a given period of time, or by a decision under this law. EUR).
Automated tax information system used by FÚ to support tax management.
The NKÚ check found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the opportunity to impose a fine on payers for not filing their VAT tax return.
Submission and processing of tax returns for VAT in Germany
In Germany we distinguish between preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT returns and annual VAT returns.
Those taxpayers who are obliged to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small business owners who are not liable to pay VAT annual tax returns.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10. th day of the month following the quarter in which VAT is incurred (§ 18 paragraph 18). 2 UStG).
However, if VAT tax liability exceeds EUR 136 in the previous calendar year 6 or in the case of a newly established business, the relevant businessman is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10. th day of the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to submit a monthly VAT return if last year a tax refund exceeded EUR 6 136 (§ 18 paragraph 18). 2 and UStG).
VAT admission may not be made unless the amount of the annual VAT exceeds EUR 512
The relevant amount of VAT tax liability must be paid by the 10. th day of the month following the tax year in which VAT was incurred.
Tax refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by FÚ
There are no time limits (according to the law) for processing tax returns and refund of excess VAT.
For the purpose of early tax refund it is possible to offer collateral of the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process tax returns to VAT and return tax quickly.
German VAT law provides for an extension of this period (Section 18 (18) of the basic Regulation. 6 UStG).
Such extension must be applied separately.
It allows you to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT tax liability a month later, provided that a special advance is paid for monthly returns.
This advance payment will be offset compared to December's VAT tax liability.
Whenever an error is found, the entrepreneur must submit a VAT tax return.
There is no additional VAT admission.
Once the annual VAT tax return, which must be filed by May 31. of the following calendar year, is registered with the IRS, the business owner cannot fix the wrong preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
Repair of the annual VAT tax return for the benefit or failure of the payer is possible within the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT tax return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT tax return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns to VAT electronically.
The financial authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid disproportionate hardness.
Submission of annual VAT refund is possible in paper or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If done without certification, the payer must submit a confession once again on a paper with personal signatures.
In case the payer does not file VAT returns, the tax administration is entitled to make a gross estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late submission, the payer may be penalised (maximum of 10 % of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
BH found during previous inspection that the financial authorities often do not measure this standard fine.
In other cases where the financial authorities imposed a fine, the amount was inconsistent and arbitrary.
Therefore, the standard fine does not fulfil its aim to shorten the average delay, especially when filing annual VAT tax return.
VAT tax return contains separate lines related to intracommunitary supply / acquisition values.
Values of the acquisition of services are reported on special rows of VAT tax return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on separate tax return / VAT line.
In the case of VAT return submitted in paper form, copy must be made either via a scanner or employees specifically designated for it.
Electronically VAT return data shall be immediately available to the tax authority.
Once all data are entered into the system, RMS staff will pass it and select cases that meet certain criteria.
The selected VAT returns must be rechecked by the financial authority on the basis of a control report drawn up by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration must grossly estimate the amount of VAT paid by the taxpayer, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers submit their tax return to VAT within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
The taxation period depends on the amount of the payer's turnover, either the calendar quarter or the calendar month.
In Germany, payers submit preliminary tax returns to VAT, depending on the previous year's tax liability, either within 10 days after the end of the calendar quarter or month.
By 31. May of the following year, payers are required to submit an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit annual VAT tax returns has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly preliminary) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
- if the payer corrects the admitted intracommunitary transactions, the repair cannot be related to the period for which the summary report is submitted;
- Federal states do not usually compare VIES data on intracommunitary acquisitions of German payers before processing annual VAT returns.
In accordance with registration (see. 4.1.3) German payers are obliged to submit annual VAT tax return regardless of their turnover.
This obligation enables the German financial authority to check the maximum turnover limit for small business owners.
Moreover, the responsible financial authority is able to compare annual VAT returns with direct tax returns and with closing accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only on income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany have an obligation to submit VAT tax returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns in the Czech Republic electronically would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as ′′ SH ′′) is submitted according to Section 102 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. a payer who has delivered goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always reported in Czech currency broken down by tax entities, indicating their VAT ID under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services provided are not included in SH.
SH shall serve payers with monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days after its end to the local competent financial authority.
Fixing the wrong data is done in the subsequent SH within 15 days of the date of error finding.
The erroneous data given in SH are always replaced by the data given in the subsequent SH.
Just like tax returns, payers and SH can submit in electronic form.
In case the payer does not submit SH or subsequent SH and had them under law no. 235/2004 Coll. submit, the tax administrator will invite him to submit him and at the same time instruct him about the consequences in case of failure to submit SH or subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax manager is under Section 37 of Law No. 337/1992 Coll. entitled to repeatedly impose a fine up to CZK 2 000 (EUR 67 150) for failure to fulfil obligations of a non-cash nature.
The NKÚ check found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the opportunity to impose a fine on the payers for failing to comply with their legal obligations.
Especially in the case of SH filing, tax entities are not sufficiently motivated to perform their duties, because SH failure to submit does not affect VAT tax liability.
The tax administrator is obliged according to § 102 (102) 5 law no. 235/2004 Coll. data in SH, or subsequent SH, check, delete any inconclusiveness and use data for taxation.
In case of non-compliance with SH data and data in the relevant (payer with monthly taxation period) or the relevant (payer with quarterly taxation period) VAT tax return, the tax manager should verify the correctness of the tax liability given in the VAT tax return.
The wrong data in SH will be removed by filing a subsequent SH himself or may be called upon to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the data on the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
- the payer will not demonstrate the data given in SH (or subsequent SH), correcting them by submitting subsequent SH,
- the tax administrator has demonstrated that the data given by the payer in SH or subsequent SH are not true.
The tax administrator does not replace the filing of the tax body by the payer by entering a repair without submission of the subsequent SH payer, only adjusts the data in the VIES database so that they are up to date, complete and accurate.
Data from SH shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
Only a national financial authority can send and receive them, designed to cooperate with other Member States in the VAT area; this is CLO (in the Czech Republic, the International Cooperation Department of VAT Management (CLO).
O _ MCTL is an automatic message received by CLO from other Member States.
Includes all erroneous VAT IDs listed in SH rows sent.
If the wrong VAT ID is used in one of the common SH or subsequent SH rows, the record is made into the wrong VAT ID table.
The table contains so-called. ′′ Notice of doubt to VAT ID ".
The tax administrator will check and record the result of the verification in the system.
When goods are acquired from another Member State, the payer is obliged to award VAT and indicate the values of acquisition on separate lines of VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of goods purchased declared by the Czech payer in his VAT tax return and in the value of the goods supplied, as reported by payers from other Member States in their SH, are sent from the CLO to the IRS for examination.
Tax administrators have a duty to investigate the irregularities.
There may be three situations:
(a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the respective lines of VAT tax returns is lower than the value of delivery declared by EU payers.
In this case the tax administrator will check the accuracy of the data.
b) The difference is 0.
This situation can either happen by changing EU data (foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the tax return to VAT (the Czech tax entity himself lodges additional tax return to VAT).
In this case, it is up to the tax manager's discretion whether despite this fact he will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT tax return.
c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States, which the Czech tax payer has shown in the relevant VAT lines, is higher than the value of the goods supplied declared by the EU payer.
Even here it is at the discretion of the administrator whether it will verify the accuracy of the data.
After checking the difference and clarifying the causes of its creation, the tax administrator will introduce the result of the verification into ADIS.
The results of the verification are transmitted back to CLO.
The number of cases sent from CLO to the financial authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005 shows graph no. 1 (Note: source: MF).
The above graph no. 1 demonstrates that the number of cases transmitted from CLO to the financial authorities in each quarter of 2005 decreased.
A significant decrease in number occurred in the 4. th quarter of 2005. CLO increased the minimum financial limit, including. with regard to the possibility of sending information requests to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT tax returns and EU data may not always be caused by a fault on the side of the domestic payer.
It can also be a mistake on the EU payer side or a mistake arising from the fact that in individual EU Member States some types of transactions can be introduced into SH in a different way.
The most common reasons for irregularities in the values of the reported transactions found at the inspected financial authorities are given table 1.
Submission and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs who carry out intracommunitary delivery from Germany to other EU Member States or participate in trilateral transactions shall be required to serve SH once every quarter of a year, which indicate intracommunitary delivery according to beneficiaries (§ 18 a (odst 18 a). 1 UStG).
SH must be submitted by the 10. th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If extension of this deadline is allowed in case of preliminary VAT returns, this applies to SH as well.
SH must be delivered to CLO.
From 1. January 2007 they must be administered electronically.
Exceptions may be allowed by the competent financial authorities to certain taxpayers to avoid excessive hardness.
In cases where taxpayers realize that SH has false data, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In case taxpayers do not submit SH, CLO will initiate proceedings in order to make this report possible.
Part of this procedure is: - the first reminder - the second reminder associated with the threat of a fine / penalty payment and - penalty payment.
Although the German tax code allows a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (§ 329 AO), the CLO measures fines in three steps, amounts 125, 250 and 500 EUR.
Besides, § 26 a (26) 1 no. UStG 5 stipulates payers act illegally unless they deliberately or negligently administrate SH, serve them incomplete, do not submit them on time or if they do not repair or repair the late SH.
This offense can be punished with a fine of up to EUR 5 000
Intracommunitary supply data cannot be entered by the VIES by the IRS because SH processing is the sole task of the CLO.
SH data are stored only in the CLO system.
Data from SH are therefore visually available only after processing to CLO.
Deadlines for SH processing are set in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
SH data must be stored within three months after the relevant calendar quarter.
In case of incorrect VAT ID in SH German payers, CLO receives O _ MCTL codes from another Member State.
The CLO contacts a particular businessman and asks for correct information.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case shall be transmitted to the competent financial authorities.
It is then up to these financial authorities to request the correct data.
During the inspection, BRH found that most VAT ID entrepreneurs have repaired at CLO request.
However, the challenge, threat and measuring three additional fines works in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud, too much time.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the competent financial authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The IRS rejected the exemption of reported intracommunitary delivery in 73 % of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the IRS asked him to submit a repaired SH to CLO, since the tax authorities cannot repair data in VIES themselves.
BRH found that neither the financial authorities nor the CLO checked the filing of the repaired SH, so the payers often failed to comply with the request.
Due to the fact that the CLO has no access to VAT return data, a comparison of the delivery data of goods admitted in the VAT return and SH will not take place before submitting this data to the CLO of other Member States.
Only the financial authorities can carry out this inspection and is usually applied in the preparation of the VAT check.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed into CLO.
Wrong VAT ID are selected and then submitted to the Member States concerned.
This data is used for the purpose of inspection of acquisition by the financial authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, CLO will recheck them based on comparison with previous calendar quarter data.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), inspection information is created and sent to the competent financial authorities.
This procedure is applied permanently, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created later and submitted to the financial authorities.
The RMS installed for the assessment procedure will subsequently check these data with intracommunitary acquisitions data.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who are not fully entitled to VAT deduction.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who delivered goods to another Member State serve a taxable person in another Member State within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the local tax authority.
The tax authorities process SH and transmit the data to CLO.
Values of supply of goods to another Member State, listed by the payer in SH, are compared at the financial authorities with the value of the supply of goods to another Member State, given by these payers in VAT tax returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the measurement procedure.
In Germany, payers who made intracommunitary delivery are obliged to serve SH quarterly until day 10. of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers serve on CLO, from 1. 1. 2007 in electronic form.
Tax authorities have SH information available only after it is processed into CLO.
Payers from Czech Republic and Germany mention only the delivery of goods in SH, the provision of services is not listed in SH.
Unlike Czech financial authorities, German financial authorities are unable to correct the wrong lines submitted by SH.
Due to this limited access to German VIES data, the wrong VAT ID was not corrected, although the payer provided the correct VAT ID.
German tax administration does not compare data on intracommunitary supplies, which are given in the tax return to the German payer and its SH.
The differences between the data of these two statements are not usually identified before the German CLO provides VIES data to other Member States.
Given the findings of BRH, it is clear that comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
The data on the supply of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their tax returns for VAT.
The comparison is performed by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most important cases of irregularities are handed over to the financial authorities as a reminder of possible errors in payer s' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intracommunitary acquisitions.
Such a general inspection is only processed for payers who are not fully entitled to VAT deduction.
Moreover, the German tax administration checks the taxation of intracommunitary acquisitions of other payers only if RMS produces a control alert or if the payer is intended for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the financial authorities from the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, VAT fraud detection depends on the quality of RMS.
Carousel scams fighting requires continuously updated information on intracommunitary acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specially VIES, provides financial authorities with information that could be up to six months old.
This delay can be shortened by up to four months if the payers serve SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, because most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to submit VAT returns monthly - and SH does not require any further information compared to tax returns.
In order to prevent bureaucratic costs, the submission of SH may be associated with filing a VAT return.
However, the obligation to serve SH monthly would cause more time disagreements between intracommunitary delivery and intracommunitary acquisition and could increase data flow between individual CLOs.
The German Federal Government in 2006 considered general provision of monthly SH.
Its implementation failed due to federal state s' doubts.
These were worried that monthly submission of VIES data to the CLO of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the duty of monthly SH and monthly data transmission were to be effective, monthly update of VIES would require a European standard of monthly SH.

International level 3 information exchange
Implementation of international information exchange in Czech Republic
International exchange of information allows tax administrators to acquire information from other Member States regarding intracommunitary business transactions and payers who made these transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No On administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 1798/2003 218/92, distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information on request and exchange of information without prior request.
International exchange of information on request is made in the form of the so-called. requests for information (hereinafter referred to as ′′ ŽOI ′′), using standardized SCAC forms.
Tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI or. replies to the ŽOI delivered via the CLO Financial Directorates, ensuring the translation of information contained in standardised SCAC forms into foreign language and sending it to other Member States.
The CLO also ensures the income of ŽOI from other Member States and replies to the ŽOI sent, translation into Czech and distribution to local tax administrators.
In Article 8 Council Regulation (EC) No 8 1798/2003 the maximum deadline for the operation of the ŽOI is set for 3 months after the application is accepted.
NKÚ checks were subjected to all ŽOI transmitted during the controlled period between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Out of the total of 94 ŽOI, accepted in the Czech Republic from Germany, there were 70 cases (i.e. 74,5 %) finished within a specified three-month deadline, 23 more cases (i.e. 24,5 %) was finished after this deadline and the remaining 1 case was not sent to Germany until the NKÚ check.
More detailed information about the deadlines in which replies to the ŽOI received from the Czech Republic were sent from the Czech Republic, contains graph no. 2.
Out of the total of 335 ŽOI sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, there were 136 cases (i.e. 40,6 %) response received within the specified three months deadline, another 179 (i.e. 53,4 %) the request was answered after this period and 19 cases (i.e. 5,7 %) no response from Germany was delivered until the NKÚ check (in the remaining 1 cases it was not possible to determine when the reply from the FRN was received).
More detailed information about the deadlines in which answers to the Czech Republic were delivered to the Czech Republic to the Czech Republic, graph no contains 3.
The percentage of the values of intracommunitary transactions, given in ŽOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany, contains graph No. 4.
As seen from the above graph, the value of business transactions, tested via ŽOI, was most frequently in the zone above EUR 60 000
The international exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or in the form. structured automatic exchange of information or in the form of spontaneous information exchange.
Tax administrators from other Member States are often transmitted without prior request information which may be relevant to them in the management of VAT.
In the Czech Republic all information is collected at CLO.
Information is transmitted electronically between Member States.
'Automatic exchange' shall apply according to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and at pre-specified regular intervals.
'Structured automatic exchange' means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information about the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to tax administrators from the form Report on delivery of a new means of transport under Section 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the tax document issued.
The tax administrator shall complete the necessary data to a specially created template when processing the aforementioned form and transmit it to the contact worker at the financial director where the data are collected and within the specified deadline, i.e. notified to the CLO for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States within two months of the end of the quarter in which this information was available.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information about the dispatch sale, which is exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information about intra-EU operations that appear unauthorized and information about potential ′′ missing traders ".
This information is sent to other Member States by means of spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of international information exchange in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and spontaneous information are initiated by the competent tax authority.
The financial authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form via e-mail directly to the German CLO transmitting SCAC forms to foreign CLO.
The financial authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of Germany's requests for information controlled by BRH were sent to ensure taxation of intracommunitary acquisition in another Member State or to demonstrate exemption of intracommunitary delivery from Germany to another Member State from tax.
If a German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it will check the value of the supply of goods or services specified in the application for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000
If there is no reasonable reason for this application, the German CLO will reject any application containing an amount lower than this specified limit.
In addition, German CLO translates free texts of the SCAC form [(B1- 17) or (E)], unless these texts are in German or English.
To respond to the request for information, CLO sends the application to the competent financial authority with a reference to the three-month deadline.
There are no other deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of tax administration.
Although German CLO has technical conditions for monitoring the past time limits, it lacks sufficient personnel capacity to draw the attention of the financial authorities to the response of unsuccessful requests for information.
The financial authorities will obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by auditing.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit, which concerns any taxable process over a few months or so-called VAT inspection, which can relate to only one business operation that has recently been carried out.
This short and flexible type of audit requires no notification to the taxpayer and proved its beneficial effect in the investigation of individual taxable commercial operations.
Under automatic exchange without prior request, Germany provides information to other Member States - VAT ID allocated to payers resident in other Member States - on the refund of entry tax to payers resident in other Member States.
Moreover, Germany has committed itself to providing other Member States with the following information through a structured automatic exchange:
and. Delivery of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without using their VAT ID, b. sending or catalog sales in other Member States not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intracommunitary acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intracommunitary delivery of goods not shown by the German payer in SH because he treated the delivery as domestic transactions, e. potential ′′ missing trader ′′ that carried out intracommunitary transactions independently of their VAT ID, f. business owners who delivered goods to potential ′′ missing traders ′′ or to those beneficiaries who abused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The sending of ŽOI or spontaneous information is initiated by the competent financial authorities in both Czech Republic and Germany, which send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech - English) and translates the sent information into English or English. German language, German financial authorities follow the instructions according to which they should write ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German on a single language form.
German CLO does not secure the translation of German texts.
By checking the ŽOI transmitted between 1. August 5. and 31. August 12. between the Czech Republic and Germany found out that the Czech tax administration has handled 74,5 % of the applications received within a specified three-month period, while ŽOI dispatched to Germany were executed by the German tax administration within the specified time limit only 40,6 % of cases.
Although German CLO alerts the financial authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not follow the past time limits.
The result of missing notifications is a large number of late replies to ŽOI.
Due to these issues, BRH recommended regular alerts to CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, German CLO now alerts the financial authorities to answer the unfinished answers to ŽOI.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at various tax administration organisational levels deal with risk management.
The following departments address the issue of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
Department of Methodology and Performance of VAT Risk Management Report, which, inter alia, governs the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates trends of these risks at both domestic and community levels.
Nationwide coordinates the functioning of the role of Trustworthiness of VAT tax returns and the use of VIES data in terms of tax evasion risks in intra-communitarian transactions.
Based on data from the Czech trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risk commodities, processes conceptual risk management in the field of VAT and cooperates in this area with relevant EU institutions and other Member States.
Department of International Cooperation in the Management of VAT, which, among other things, is the same. ensures exchange of VAT information, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public awareness and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT ID or VAT IDs, contained in the O _ MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the controlled period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data shows substantial differences.
Different bases for determining the number of O _ MCTL reports may cause these differences.
While Czech CLO covers their numbers for the calendar quarter for which SH was submitted, the German CLO covers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O _ MCTL report was received.
Department of Methodology Tax Control and Search, which inter alia conducts a risk analysis in the methodological management of tax checks and in accordance with risk analysis, sets priorities for the focus of tax checks in the plans of the financial directorate, processes risk analysis in the framework of tax evasion restrictions, including the collection of knowledge gained during tax management and other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Financial directors have set up search departments, which are performing, among others. searches of tax entities and areas that are at risk in terms of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searching for unregistered tax entities in terms of tax evasion risks (e.g. from internet services, work brokerage, radio and printing services etc.), analysis of chain fraud bonds and transmission of information to territorial financial authorities.
Specialized inspection department is set up at selected 12 financial authorities.
They have regional competence, tax checks outside the territorial scope of the financial authorities under mandate.
The need to set up a separation of specialised tax checks came from the growing findings of new and more perfect forms of tax evasion, which mainly occur with entities connected to chains.
These departments focus on controlling fiscal entities according to the requirements of the search department, tax entities with specific activity and multinational companies and tax entities of a large scale of activity in terms of turnover size.
The following mechanisms were integrated into the ADIS system to reduce risks in the field of VAT: - the task of credibility of VAT tax returns, used to evaluate the risk of tax returns filed, - the role of the selection of tax entities for inspection, allowing the selections based on selected criteria of the payer for inspection, - the role of the task VIES through which tax administrators have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES enables, inter alia, to verify the validity of VAT ID of payers from other Member States, - to obtain from other Member States the values of goods supplied to a Czech payer declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, - to generate a set of payers who did not submit SH, - carry out a formal check of data reported by the Czech payers in SH before sending such data to other Member States, - generate a set of payers where the data on the supply of goods to other Member States listed in VAT tax returns do not match the data in SH, - generate a set of payers where the value of acquisition of goods from other Member States listed in VAT tax returns does not match the data declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
As part of the tax evasion risk reduction activity, tax administrators have access to registries of state authorities such as: business register, real estate cadastre, motor vehicle registry, business registry etc.
More detailed information is given in Chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the Federal (Federal) structure of Germany, the Federal Tax Administration (especially CLO) and the tax administration of 16 Federal States are involved in the development and operation of RMS.
Although there are common working groups for developments, neither CLO nor tax administrations of federal states share a completely consistent database.
At CLO level, the ST I 2 (hereinafter referred to as ′′ KUSS ′′ - the coordination unit for special VAT audits and tax investigations) collects the findings of the tax fraud control in a special database called the OPUS.
KUSS introduced a new database called ZAUBER designed for the transfer of tax fraud company names ′′ missing traders ′′ in cooperation with the financial authorities.
KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
KUSS experience is projected into RMS development in working groups.
In addition, specialists of several other CLO and MF services are entrusted with RMS duties and powers.
At CLO level, a formal inspection of the composition of VAT ID of other Member States in SH submitted by German payers is introduced.
This formal inspection is carried out before shipping data from SH to other Member States to improve clarity and use of VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Verification of validity of VAT ID specified in SH is performed on the basis of O _ MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the repair of invalid VAT ID, see. also 4.4.2).
In addition, the CLO RMS is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and produces several types of control messages based on several characteristics, which are usually called. carousel business operations to identify potential ′′ missing traders ".
The Federal State s' financial authorities are instructed to process these inspection reports and report in some cases on the results of their CLO findings.
The BRH audit findings confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all the available characteristics if the existence of a tax fraud case is likely to be expected (instead of sole focus on company turnover).
Therefore, BRH suggested the MF to take into account various characteristics when processing reports.
RMS should also affect other facts, such as taxpayer's (morale) payment behaviour, field (economic activity) or shareholder structure.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the Federal States and focused on the processing of VAT tax returns.
For example, RMS generates a list of those payers who showed intracommunitary delivery in tax returns.
This list is sent to CLO to monitor full SH administration.
In addition, this type of RMS compares the intracommunitary acquisition reported in the payer's annual VAT tax return with VIES data.
Tax Administration of the Federal States seeks to avoid comparing quarterly data, because this comparison would reveal too much disagreement data attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
- a different period of implementation of the intracommunitary transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
- different accounts on sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting in tax returns.
In addition to comparing VAT tax returns data and VIES data, many Federal States have introduced RMS elements based on VAT tax returns data and some other facts (such as company name structure, shareholder age, employee number and payment behavior / morale of taxpayer).
Bavaria has introduced RMS based on rules that allow a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to program their own rules for earning potential tax fraud offenders.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly tax return for VAT.
Therefore, the competent tax authority receives recommendations made by RMS before the VAT determination.
Since this RMS is not able to project current findings into its activity, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules based on the feedback of the financial authorities.
The Mecklenburg-West Pomerania administration programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data of tax files in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
Based on this data, RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
RMS produces once a month a list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The competent financial authorities use this list as a basis for the audit decision of proposed taxpayers.
Following the audit, auditors must report their findings in order to be projected into RMS.
North Rhine-Westphalia Administrative Region uses adaptive artificial neural network that is combined with a system of fuzzy based on rules.
Based on the large number of data assessed VAT tax returns and some other facts, this neural fuzzy system or potentially useful information collection system (called. data-mining system) calculates the probability that a taxpayer committed a tax fraud.
He then compiles a monthly list of potential scam offenders.
Local financial authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the taxpayers concerned for inspection and announce the findings of the data processing center.
The introduction of one of these three RMS in the other spolkových is further underway.
Since none of these three RMS are based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful to solve tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although this report cannot discuss specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany, NKÚ and BRH found that each Member State has developed its own RMS.
As well as different approaches in three Federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of EU Member States are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud - turns out not to be a national but rather a European problem.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State but in multiple states.
Effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and introduced in every EU Member State, otherwise the scammers will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
VAT loss caused by fraud in the EU does not have to intervene by the Member State of the fraud initiator.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and discussion about RMS.
Selected inspection findings when verifying commercial transactions
In the framework of cooperation on the implementation of parallel control events, NKÚ and BRH tested the quality and use of information about selected commercial transactions, which were the subject of international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
The two supervisory institutions also jointly examined the implementation of several commercial transactions, where there were doubts about their implementation, or. irregularities in the way payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their tax returns to VAT or SH.
NKÚ checked a total of 8 cases involving commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities at the request of BRH.
In 43 cases, NKÚ checked the value of intracommunitary transactions with Germany, which Czech payers reported in their tax returns and SH due to the BRH alert.
AT the request of the NKÚ, BRH checked a total of 23 cases involving commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information has been exchanged under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 via official communication with CLO.
The examination of selected cases was among others. a different method of registration in EU Member States found to lead to problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer should have been bought in III. quarter 2004 from the German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500
Since the Czech payer showed the acquisition of goods only worth EUR 29 869, the Czech tax manager sent a request to the Czech tax manager to the Czech Republic for a verification of the value of the goods supplied.
In reply to the ŽOI delivered from Germany, the German party stated that in II. quarter of 2004, German payer supplied the Czech payer with goods worth EUR 27 381, in III. quarter worth EUR 31 997 and IV. quarter 2004 worth EUR 10 276
The reply further revealed that the German payer's VAT ID was valid only from 28. August 9., but German CLO in 2006 following additional application by the German payer for validity certificate VAT ID retroactively issued a valid VAT ID certificate from 1. 5. 2004.
The German payer did a repair of SH.
The Czech payer was based on this information about the acquisition of goods.
NKÚ found by a local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the Czech payer submitted additional VAT tax returns for each tax period 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States while exercising the right to deduction VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional tax returns to VAT, the Czech tax manager could not clearly determine whether they included the value of the supply from the above German supplier.
Based on NKÚ request, BRH found that a German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not apply for VAT ID on registration, he was only assigned an ID for transactions within the FRN.
Although it is not usually possible to allocate VAT ID retroactively in Germany, in this case the German tax official assigned VAT ID retroactively to the above German payer in 1.5.2004.
German CLO allocates VAT ID retroactively unless the German entrepreneur caused the delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay caused the CLO after the payer's VAT ID application.
In this case, CLO allocates VAT ID retroactively because the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intracommunitary delivery under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the contrary, the German recipient does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier to report intracommunitary acquisition.
Due to these various procedures between Member States, German CLO allocated VAT ID retroactively in this special case.
2.
The Czech tax administrator asked for VAT registration of the German tax payer as part of the international exchange of information.
VIES stated the date of registration on 5. June 3., with the date 1. 2004. on the certificate of registration of the German payer issued locally by the competent German financial authority.
In a response received from Germany, the German party stated that the German tax entity was registered from 1. 10. 2004, but VAT ID was provided to him in Germany for organizational reasons up to 16. 2. 2005.
NKÚ by question at the local tax manager, found that the Czech tax manager carried out a VAT check with the Czech tax payer for the tax period III. quarter 2004 to II. quarter 2005.
Through this inspection, the IRS found that the Czech payer included a VAT service of CZK 9 (EUR 314) in the tax return, provided to the German payer at the time prior to his VAT registration (i.e. before 1. th June 10.).
For tax period III. quarter of 2004, the tax authority measured VAT of 1 880 CZK (EUR 60) to the tax agency.
The BRH found out, based on NKÚ's request, the German payer was allocated up to 16. 2. 2005 when he informed the IRS about his business he launched in 2004.
In addition, the IRS registered it for VAT retrospectively on October 1., 200415 to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer showed an intracommunitary acquisition from the Czech Republic worth EUR 160 (approx. 5000 CZK).
3. The Czech payer reported VAT tax return for September 2004 and SH for III. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth CZK 114 (EUR 3 642) to the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator found out when verifying the registration of the German payer in VIES system that his registration was valid from 11. 11. 2004, i.e. only after delivery of goods by Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer submitted additional DAP to VAT, showing the tax base for transactions in the country worth 114 615 CZK (EUR 3 642) and VAT of CZK 21 (692 EUR) paid for.
NKÚ found by a question at the local competent tax office in the Czech Republic that the Czech payer subsequently submitted an application for a revision of the proceedings regarding the additional tax return to VAT and presented a confirmation of the German tax administration that the German payer was taxed from 1. 1. 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of registration of the German payer in international information exchange.
The response received from Germany showed that VAT ID was allocated to the German payer up to 11. 11. 2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the application for renewal.
BRH found out that in the present case it was not an intracommunitary acquisition of goods because the German payer obtained VAT ID up to 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient reported the acquisition as an intracommunitary acquisition and declared VAT on this acquisition when demanding the input tax refund of the same amount.
However, because there would not be changes in the value of VAT that the German payer had to pay, the tax manager in Germany did not correct the data in his VAT return.
BRH further found that the name of the German payer, listed in ŽOI, was changed during the processing of the response in Germany, resulting in two German tax entities confusing.
This change in the name of the German payer confused the Czech tax manager.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax manager verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech payer in I. quarter 2005 worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
NKU found out by a local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that this administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer verifying that the delivery of goods was carried out and the Czech payer charged and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not confess the acquisition of goods in VAT tax return, because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for national transactions in Germany.
In VIES application, the Czech tax manager found out that the German payer was registered to VAT for intracommunitary transactions only from 21. 4. 2005, i.e. only after delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax manager asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the certificate of registration of the German payer so that he could take steps to pay tax if necessary.
The Czech Financial Authority assessed the commercial transaction as acquisition of goods from the non-payer from Germany and therefore the Czech payer on the said commercial transaction was not taxed.
BRH found that according to German legislation, a VAT ID does not have to have a VAT ID allocated to intracommunitary supply of goods exempted from VAT.
The supplier must only have VAT ID available to the customer from another Member State and be able to demonstrate the transport of the goods to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, it was an intracommunitary transaction and VAT should be measured in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax manager noticed this transaction, because the delivery of the machine at the value was not the basic subject of the German supplier's business.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to respond to ŽOI regarding intracommunitary transactions with a value of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to data from VIES in III, the Czech payer had a Czech payer. quarter of 2004 to buy goods from a German payer worth EUR 12 561
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax check on the tax agency for this tax period.
In international administrative cooperation, he asked the German tax administration via the SCAC form to verify the delivery of the goods.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of goods, claimed that he had never traded with the German company and in his accounts the acquisition of these goods was not accounted for.
The German tax administration rejected the request for evidence - contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents, justifying that the turnover was not more than EUR 15 000 and no further explanatory reasons were given.
Since the Czech tax manager did not obtain evidence for the measurement of the tax on the goods purchased, he ended the tax check without finding and the tax obligation remained in the original amount.
The BRH found that the German payer performed as the so-called based on the NKÚ request. ′′ fiscal representative ′′ (§ 22 a - e UStG).
The German payer showed the said supply in its annual VAT tax return and SH.
The claim to exemption of delivery has been recognized.
Based on the BRH alert, the German financial authority will send documents needed to the Czech Republic for measuring the tax on acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
