7. The Czech tax administrator requested in 2005 via the SCAC form to verify the delivery of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German payer, performed in III. and IV. quarter 2004 showing signs of carousel fraud.
NKÚ found out that ZOI had not been delivered from Germany until the time of inspection.

The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax agency filed the subsequent SH.

Following the BRH alert, a German customer was inspected in Germany, which found that all cars were properly taxed and that the relevant cars were sold to another payer in Germany.

12.
During the international exchange of information, the German tax manager requested via the SCAC form to verify the supply of goods and services made in III. quarter 2005.
According to this ŽOI, the Czech payer was supposed to supply the German payer with a total value of EUR 396 126 and provide services worth EUR 11 885
NKÚ found out that the Czech tax manager carried out a local investigation to verify this delivery with the Czech payer.
In response to ŽOI, the Czech tax manager stated that the Czech payer supplied a production line including assembly to the German payer.
The Czech payer delivered individual parts of the production line before the Czech Republic joined the EU and after 2004 1. 5. the line was assembled based on order.
German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed it had defects.
In III. The Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took over the issued invoices, but he did not acknowledge them and pay them.
The NKÚ further inquiries from the local tax manager in the Czech Republic found that all invoices are properly registered in the Czech payer's accounts.
In tax returns for III. 2004. quarter 2005 only amounts supported by the Czech payer related to invoicing after 1. 5. 2004.
BRH found that based on a response from the Czech tax administration, the local tax authority in Germany concluded that in the case of the transaction it was the delivery of goods from a Czech payer to a German payer including services for assembly.
In this special case, the place is called. work is done where the production line was installed.
According to German VAT law, the German recipient is liable to pay VAT.
At the same time, the beneficiary can claim VAT deduction from the same amount.
As there would be no changes in the value of VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the repairs in VAT tax return were neglected by the German tax authority.
13. Czech payer A according to data from VIES in February 2005, he should have bought a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify this delivery.
In response to ŽOI, the German party stated that the German payer C added the German payer C to the Czech payer B, which was supposed to return the machine to the German payer C in October 2004
According to German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but transported to the organizational component of the German payer C in Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the answer to the request for information revealed that German payer C sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the German payer C in Czech Republic.
Since the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intracommunitary delivery of goods.
NKÚ by a question from the tax manager of the local payer B found that according to VIES data, German payer C added in III. quarter 2004 to the Czech payer B goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027
The payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the local tax manager from the Czech Republic sent ŽOI to Germany.
According to the response to this request, the machine was delivered.
Another investigation with payer B, the Czech tax manager found out that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in the bookkeeping of payer B and that it could be a machine of the same type as the organisational component of the German payer C to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
NKÚ further found out that the Czech tax administrator local payer A conducted a local investigation with this payer.
The tax administrator had an invoice of German payer C dated 7. 2. 2005, on which the payer A was listed as a machine customer.
The Czech tax administrator found out that the payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounting.
The payer A had a leasing contract with another Czech company, where the subject of the leasing was a machine of the same type.
Handover of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9. 2. 2005, the transport of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax authority to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found out that German payer C machine worth EUR 88 027 was not delivered to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
So it was not an intracommunitary delivery of goods, but a taxable operation in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax manager did not acknowledge the German tax payer C tax exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D added the machine to Czech payer B.
According to German legislation, this delivery was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Next, BRH found out that German payer C stated in his SH for I. quarter 2005 delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to the Czech payer A.
This delivery was not verified during the tax inspection carried out by the German tax authority.

The Czech tax administrator thus incorrectly concluded the local investigation.

20. According to data in VIES, German payer bought goods from the Czech Republic in 4 2005 251 after acquiring EUR 43 274 worth of goods in the previous year.

Moreover, he did not show adequate deliveries either.
Due to these differences, the German IRS sent ŽOI for the 4. rd quarter of 2005 and 1. th quarter of 2006.
The Czech supplier showed intracommunitary delivery of goods to the German payer totaling 167 246 CZK (EUR 5 615 299) in SH.
On June 6., 2006, ŽOI was delivered, in which the German party asked to check whether the Czech payer of reported intracommunitary delivery was held.
In reply to this ŽOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the German party's request was not possible because the Czech payer had no manager.
As it follows from materials provided by NKÚ by the competent tax manager, on 30. June 3., a protocol was written with the director of the Czech payer on the start of the VAT check for IV. quarter 2004 and January to December 2005.
The payer was also invited by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above periods, but he did not submit any documents.
The Czech payer's only director disappeared according to the Trade Register of functions on 16. 5. 2006, the new director was not named.
Since April 2006, the Czech payer stopped filing tax returns for VAT.
During the NKU inspection in cooperation with BRH, among other things, he checked several cases of intracommunitary delivery between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not subject to previous exchange of information between tax administrations of both countries.
The two top control institutions were transmitting information on the proven cases via the CLO of both countries.
21. Czech company (eCR) which is not resident in Germany informed the competent financial authority (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out taxable transactions in Germany.
Due to this information the company was registered since June 2005 but did not receive German VAT ID.
(ECR) accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind power plants and for the delivery of these wind power plants on behalf of, at risk and at the expense of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to lack of capacity, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), based in Germany.
The following scheme shows the contractual relations and the method of transporting wind power plants:
According to the German legal situation, the place of carrying out these transactions must be determined according to the following:
- Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent wind power plants to assemble under his name, at his risk and his account to Austria.
Since the installation of this delivery took place in Austria, the delivery of wind power plants is taxable in Austria.
- Because the carrier was instructed by the Danish businessman (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and at his own expense, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started - in Germany.
Although wind power plants were sent to another Member State and the recipient is a registered payer from another Member State, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption because another Member State of destination differs from another Member State of the registered office of the Czech company.
Therefore, this delivery is rightly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted tax on entry in its tax returns.
The place of delivery of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of the transport.
Transport of some wind power plants started in Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- Delivery of those wind power plants that are made in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- Delivery of other wind power plants manufactured in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intracommunitary delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intracommunitary delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found out that the Czech company (eCR) did not report any intracommunitary acquisition or submit SH to the German CLO in its tax return.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intracommunitary delivery uniformly as an intracommunitary delivery from the Czech Republic.
NKÚ found that (eCR) showed no intracommunitary delivery to Austria, but intracommunitary delivery to Denmark.
Verification of taxation of intracommunitary acquisition in Austria would require cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though this case shows no sign of tax fraud or evasion.
Furthermore, the NKÚ and BRH examined transactions to highlight the differences between VIES reporting and VIES data caused by different VAT legislation in 2004.
Checked cases also demonstrate that changes in legislation need time to apply new legislation into practice by payers and financial authorities:
22. V SH for II. up to IV. quarter of 2004, the Czech payer showed intracommunitary delivery to the German payer totaling 792 977 CZK (EUR 25 197 885).
For the same period another Czech payer in SH showed intracommunitary delivery to another German payer totaling CZK 18 157 (EUR 576 970).
According to information provided by NKÚ from BRH, both cases were the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers stated the abovementioned delivery in SH in accordance with the text of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., valid in 2004.
By further examination of the abovementioned transactions, the group checking NKÚ found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and the Germany in the regulation of delivery and delivery. acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers showed electricity supply in accordance with the valid version of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intracommunitary supply of goods, in terms of German law in force in 2004, it was not an intra-communitarian acquisition, but a taxable operation with the place of operation in the territory of Germany.
The difference in legal adjustments was removed in the Czech Republic by the adoption of law no. 635/2004 Coll., amending certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Administrative Charges Act, effective from 1. 1. 2005.
23. During the examination of selected intracommunitary transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was also found that the Czech payer showed intracommunitary delivery to the German payer in the 1. th to 4. th quarter of 2005 163 Kč (EUR 8 071 823) and another Czech payer showed intracommunitary delivery to the German payer totaling 263 470 776 CZK (8 8 846 050 EUR).
According to the information provided by NKÚ by BRH, both cases were the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1. 1. 2005, in case of electricity supply, the place where the customer has its registered office, place of business or where the establishment for which the goods are delivered.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have introduced electricity supply to SH in 2005
The two above-mentioned payers showed intracommunitary supply of electricity in SH, the VIES data was distorted by a total of 503 881 CZK (EUR 16 917 873).
Conclusion
Cooperation met the goals of BRH and NKÚ.
Both SAIs gained a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
Cooperation revealed differences in both systems and showed that VAT rules differ.
Suspicious cases of intracommunitary transactions were detected during parallel checks.
Some of them make sense to check afterwards.
Based on the inspection findings, both SAI made recommendations regarding VAT management.
Monitoring these recommendations should also be part of a follow-up check.
New experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of both control institutions is the basis for successful VAT management checks.
Communicating
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the President of Bundesrechnungshof, the Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in checks on excise duty management between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The joint report submitted informs about the progress and outcome of international cooperation during parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's High Supervisory Authority, focused on the management of excise duties during the period after the entry of both countries into the European Union.
Cooperation was implemented under a control activity cooperation agreement concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel checks has been selected with a view to the fundamental change in the system of excise duty collection, which has occurred in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union since 1. May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of non-taxable goods until the date of delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, new legislation, adopted in both countries, allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under tax exemption regime.
The system places great claims on tax administrators and envisages a mutual close synergies of the competent administrative authorities of the Member States in combating tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in checks on excise duty management from 1. May 2004 to 31. December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of control: (Czech Republic) Excise Tax Administration (SR) Procedure of colonial authorities in the management of consumption taxes
The Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the ′′ NKÚ-Czech Republic ′′) and the Slovak Republic's Supervisory Authority (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ SR ′′) concluded on 8. February 2006 a cooperation agreement in control activities.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel checks ′′ Excise Tax Administration ", included in the plan of the NKÚ-Czech Republic control activity for 2005 under no. 05/34, and ′′ Control of the procedure of colnesian authorities in the management of consumption taxes ", included in the NKÚ SR control plan for 2006 under no. 48/11.
Parallel checks were the character of coordinated checks.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information that the Contracting Parties could not obtain during the inspection of the management of excise duties in the territory of their state and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks in the sense of the European implementing directives for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards - Directive No. 31.
In the territory of the Czech Republic, groups inspected from the state budget department and from the territorial unions of Central Bohemia, South Bohemia, West Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Northeast Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia between 7. February to June 2., 2006.
27 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The controlled persons were the Directorate-General of Customs (hereinafter referred to as ′′ DGC ′′) and 11 financial authorities.
12 selected customs offices were checked within the DGC out of 54. total.
The section of the financial and tax NKÚ SR in cooperation with exposures NKÚ SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 5 customs offices out of 9 between 13. February and 2. from 2. February to 2. 2006. June 2006.
8 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of parallel checks was to examine the procedure of customs authorities in the management of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation focused on the procedure of tax administrators in the exercise of supervision of transport of excise goods, especially on the registration of initiated and terminated transport under the conditioned tax exemption regime, and on the exchange of information under mutual administrative assistance between the managers of excise duties of the Czech Republic and the SR.
2. Excise duty management
The management of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by financial authorities until 31. December 2003
Since 1. January 2004, the customs authorities, which have only levied excise duty on imports, took over this agenda.
Excise tax is subject to mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products in Czech Republic.
The revenue of the state budget from excise taxes in the Czech Republic was totaled 82,8 billion in 2004 Kč and on the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees of 424,7 billion. Kč excise duties participated in 19,5 %.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties amounted to 103,6 billion. Kč and share of the state budget revenue from taxes and fees of 460.4 460.4 billion. Kč was 22,5 %.
In 2004, the revenue from the excise duty on mineral oils to the state budget was 80 % of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 was 90,9 %.
Difference to 100 % of 13 billion. Kč in 2004 and 6,9 billion. Kč in 2005 was the income of the State Transport Fund.
Customs authorities have been executed by all excise duties in SR since 1. May 2004, except for excise duty on mineral oil, which they have been administered since 1 1. edna 2002.
Until then, tax authorities were exercising the management of excise duties.
Excise duty in SR is subject to mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The revenue of the state budget from excise taxes in SR was 43.4 billion in 2004 Sk and on total tax revenue of 209,5 billion. Sk excise duties participated in 20,7 %.
In 2005 the revenue of the state budget from excise duties was 50 billion. Sk and on total tax revenue of 222,6 billion. Sk excise duties participated in 22,5 %.
Chart No. 1-Comparison of the revenue of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and taxes and tax revenue of the state budget of the SR with excise tax revenue
Legislation in both countries is based on European Union rules governing this field, in particular on: - Council Directive 92/12 / EEC on general arrangements, holdings, movement and monitoring of excise products (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Directive 92/12 / EEC ′′), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Regulation No 2073/2004 2073/2004 ′′), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2073/2004 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the transport of excise duty products under the excise duty suspension scheme (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Regulation No 2719/92 2719/92 ′′), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 Article 3649/92 (3649/92) of the simplified accompanying document for movement of excise products which have been released for domestic consumption in the Member State of dispatch (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Regulation No 3649/92 3649/92 ′′).
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Law No. 353/2003 Coll., on excise duties, as last amended, (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No., 353/2003 Coll.") effective from 1. January 2004.
In the management of excise duties in the SR, the customs authorities are among others. bound by the following generally binding legislation: - Law No. 98/2004 Z. z. on the consumption tax on mineral oil in the detection of non-inclusive prescriptions (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No. 98/2004 98/2004 Z. z."), - law no. 104/2004 Z. z. on the wine tax in the non-skilled regulations (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No 104/2004 Z. z."), - law no. 105/2004 Z. z. on the lieh tax in the non-skilled regulations (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No 105/2004 Z. z."), - law no. 106/2004 Z. z. on excise tax on Tabak products in the non-skoral prescriptions (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No 106/2004 Z. z."), - law no. 107/2004 Z. z. on beer tax consumption in non-skilled regulations (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Law No 107/2004 Z. from.").
2.1 Movement of excise goods under the suspension arrangements between Member States of the European Union
Conditions for movement of excise goods under the suspension procedure are laid down in Title III - Movement of goods Article 92/12 (92/12). 15 to 20.
Under these provisions, the transport of such goods can be carried out only by a legitimate warehousekeeper, which is a natural or legal person entitled to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
A beneficiary in another Member State may be an authorized storekeeper or operator without the status of a legitimate warehousekeeper, but they must not store or dispatch these products under the suspensive arrangements.
The authorized warehousekeeper is the operator of a tax warehouse in the Czech Republic and SR, the operator is the beneficiary for repeated or disposable acceptance of excise products.
Transportation of excise products under the suspension regime is possible under Directive 92/12 / EEC only with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be issued by the consignor before the transport starts in four copies, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require further copy.
2.2 Procedure for the start and termination of transport of goods under the suspensive procedure between the Czech Republic and the SR
Transport from Czech Republic
The procedure for starting transport is governed by the provisions of Section 25 (25) of the basic Regulation. Article 3 of Law No. 353/2003 Coll., where is MJ. stated:
′′ The operator of the tax warehouse is obliged to inform the customs office, which is local to the tax warehouse from which transport is to commence;
the transport of selected products can only be started with the approval of this customs office.
The customs office shall approve the transport of selected products without delay after the condition of tax security is met..."
The consignor in the Czech Republic can start transportation of all types of excise products only with the agreement of the local competent customs office.
The customs office will only give consent to the start of transport if the tax security of the amount of the tax on transported products is provided.
The consignor is obliged to draw up the accompanying document in five copies before the transport begins.
On the accompanying document the customs office shall indicate the approval of the start of the transport.
Copy No. 1 will be retained by the consignor, copy no. 2, 3, and 4 the consignor will submit to the carrier and copy no. 5 will be retained by the customs office authorising transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the recipient in SR will retain copy No. 2 accompanying document. Copies No 3 and No 4 confirm receipt of the products and submit both copies to the local customs office.
Copy No. 3 confirmed by the customs office shall send the consignor no later than the 15. th day of the month following the calendar month in which he accepted the products.
Copy No. 4 shall be retained by the customs office of the consignee.
Transport is terminated by the acceptance of the products by the recipient.
The release of the tax security will be decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic, which approved the start of transport, within 5 working days after the presentation of copy no. 3 accompanying document certified by the recipient and the Slovak customs office.
Chart No. 2-Circuit of the accompanying document during transport started in the Czech Republic and ended in SR
Transportation from SR
The procedure for the transport of alcohol and tobacco products from SR to another Member State of the European Union was adapted until 31. December 2005 as follows:
According to the provisions of Section 26 (26) Article 4 of Law No. 105/2004 Z. z.
′′ When transporting lieh from tax warehouse to tax warehouse to tax warehouse or to a beneficiary, or to a tax executive in the inom of the Member State, the issuer '( supplier') is mandatory on the day of the transport, send the code of the first diel of the sprieval document electronically or faxom faxom office of Poprad; this the kópiu is mandatory to send to the colnému office in writing in the piatich working days odo dňa the transport begins."
According to the provisions of Section 22 (22) Article 4 of Law No. 106/2004 Z. z.
′′ When transporting tobacco products from tax warehouse to tax warehouse to a tax warehouse or to a legitimate recipient, or to a tax executive in an inom, you annoy the republican '( supplier') is mandatory on the day of the transport, send the code of the first diel of the sprieval document electronically or fax machine to the Colnému office of Poprad; this kópiu is mandatory to send to the colnému office writing to the piatich working days odo day transport begins."
In the case of the transport of other excise products (mineral oil, wine and beer) from 1. May 2004 to 31. December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as 'the period controlled') the tax authority was not obliged to notify the customs office of Poprad, resp. the competent customs office of commencement of transport under the tax exemption procedure.
The tax administrator was only aware of the transport of these products during local inquiries or tax checks on accompanying documents and from the tax agency's accounting documents.
The consignor in SR is required to draw up the accompanying document in four copies before the transport begins.
Copy No. 1 will be retained by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, copy No. 1 by electronic or fax to the office of Poprad and the competent customs office).
Copy No. 2, 3 and 4 are accompanied by transported goods.
According to Czech legislation, the recipient in the Czech Republic will retain copy no. 2 accompanying document issued by the consignor in SR and on copy no. 3 and 4 product acceptance confirms.
Confirmed copy No. On 3 and 4 at the latest on the first working day after the end of the transport to the local customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall retain copy No. 4 and copy no. 3, where they verify the correctness and validity, returns to the recipient.
The consignee sends a confirmed copy no. 3 no later than the following working day after receiving it by the consignor to SR.
Transportation in SR is considered to have ended on the date of product takeover by the recipient.
The termination of transport is demonstrated by the consignor by submitting copy No. 3 accompanying document confirmed by the recipient and tax manager in the Czech Republic.
Chart No. 3-Circulation of the accompanying document during transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in SR and ended in Czech Republic
In 2006, amendment to all excise duty laws were gradually passed in the SR, according to which the consignor of goods under the suspension regime is required to send a copy of copy of copy No before transport started. 1 accompanying document by electronic or fax to the customs office to the local consignor.
The document demonstrating the termination of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products is copy No. 3 accompanying document certified by the recipient and his competent tax administrator.
The document demonstrating the termination of transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is copy No. 3 confirmed by the recipient.
The confirmation of the tax administrator of another Member State of the receipt of the said goods by the consignee is required if the administrator is required to confirm copy No under the legislation of the Member State concerned. 3 accompanying document.
2.3 Registration of commenced and terminated transport held by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and in the SR
A single electronic system is not introduced to monitor the transport of goods under the tax exemption regime between Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16. June 2003 establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products requires Member States and the European Commission to introduce an electronic system from 1. July 2009 (Excise Movement and Control System), which would allow excise tax administrators in individual Member States to acquire real-time information about the transport of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently used only in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under the tax exemption regime and ensuring more efficient control of the movement of non-taxed products within all Member States.
National transport databases of individual Member States will be part of this system.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport started and ended in the Czech Republic in the Module of Registration of selected products (hereinafter referred to as ′′ EVVV ′′).
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have access to the system online.
In the case of transport carried out only in the Czech Republic, tax administrators can obtain information about the start or termination of transport immediately after registration of the accompanying document by the customs office to EVVV.
The customs office shall release the tax security for transported products provided by the consignor at the time of registration of the termination of transport by the customs office of the local beneficiary.
Customs offices in SR use a database based on SysNed application software that ensures the automation of their activities in the management of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse operator, tax warehouse operator or authorized recipient to SysNed application software, this data will automatically be transferred to the ′′ System for Exchange of Data ′′ database (SEED).
3. Preparation and course of cooperation
The first coordination meeting of representatives of the NKÚ-Czech Republic and representatives of the NKÚ SR, which discussed a specific cooperation procedure in the implementation of parallel checks in the field of excise taxes, took place in January 2006.
Both parties have acquainted with each other's excise duty rules and the organization of excise duty management in both countries.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the SR during the authorization or. when commencing and terminating transport of excise products under conditional exemption regime and exchange of information between excise tax administrators of both countries.
The meeting was agreed that the Czech and Slovak parties: - they will process total data on the quantity of excise duty products transported from the Czech Republic to the SR and on the contrary, whose transport started during the controlled period - they will compare data on transport of mineral oils - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - code of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 in the tax exemption regime started in the Czech Republic and ended in SR and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
During the checks, the verified periods were extended by October and November 2005 and the transport of tobacco products under the tax exemption regime were subjected to checks.
In tables no. 1 and no. 2 The total quantity of excise products transported under the tax exemption regime between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the controlled period is stated.
4. Comparison of the transportation of goods under the tax exemption regime
NKÚ-Czech Republic handed over the Slovak side a database of transport ended in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 5 738 items covered mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
NKÚ SR handed over to the Czech side a database of transport completed in SR, which contained a total of 3 items listed on the accompanying documents, 696 items covered mineral oil, 2 066 items of alcohol and 557 items tobacco products.
NKÚ-Czech Republic compared data on transport provided in the registration of launched transport in the Czech Republic with data on closed transport registered in SR.
The results of the comparison are given in table no. 3.
Transport data in November 2004 and September 2005 compared the NKÚ-Czech Republic with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which the NKÚ SR handed over to him at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data allowing reliably to agree individual transports and therefore only 63 % of the started transport was allocated.
Individual transportation has been assigned according to multiple data, e.g. consignor, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Transport data started in the Czech Republic and ended in SR in October and November 2005 compared the NKÚ-Czech Republic with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, based on which 93 % of the started transport was clearly assigned.
In the Czech Customs Administration database, data on the amount of mineral oils were given in liters or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
In most cases the amount of alcohol was reported in liters, which, however, could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol based on the database of the percentage of alcohol.
Quantity of tobacco products has been reported in pieces, thousands of pieces and kilograms according to the type of tobacco products.
Transports started in the Czech Republic, whose termination of the Slovak database failed to verify reliably or where the information on the transported quantity of products was not in accordance with the information on the transported quantity of products, were checked.
The checks were subjected to accompanying documents for 487 transportation of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products.
The inspection of these documents was carried out at the customs offices where the NKÚ-Czech Republic carried out a check.
For transport permitted by other customs offices, accompanying documents were requested via DGC.
The Czech Republic asked the Slovak party to verify the implementation of 141 transport, which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide confirmed copy no. 3 accompanying document or the quantity of products listed on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products specified in the database.
The Slovak party was also transmitted data on transport registered in the Slovak database, which did not contain the Czech customs administration's transport database.
NKÚ SR traced 95 transport in the Slovak customs administration database.
Verification of the remaining 46 transport was requested by local customs authorities, which showed their completion by copy of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak party forwarded the Czech side a copy of accompanying documents, based on which transport was identified in the Czech database, except for transports carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of initiated transport.
A check of these cases was found:
- 11 alcohol transport transports were registered in the Slovak Transport database totaling 276,7 liters of alcohol implemented by the Czech tax agency in 2004 and 20 transport of alcohol in total of 404,66 liters of alcohol implemented in 2005.
NKÚ-Czech Republic found out that it was transportation of taxed products, which the consignor does not need the approval of the tax administrator.
The consignor informed the tax administrator in writing about the start of transport. Transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under the tax exemption scheme;
- a total of 94 mineral oils transportation were registered in the Slovak transport database, combined nomenclature code 2710 2710 11 21, totaling 173 thousand. liters implemented by the Czech tax agency between September 2004 and December 2005.
NKÚ-Czech Republic found that between May 2004 and June 2005 the tax agency carried out a transport of 102 thousand. liters of tax-free mineral oils without proper approval.
The tax body held a special authorization for the acceptance and use of tax exempt products, on the basis of which he could supply only to the holder of the same authorization.
The opening of transport to the customs office in the Czech Republic did not announce the opening of transportation and did not provide a tax security of CZK 1 680
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax body transported 71 thousand to the territory of SR. liters of taxed mineral oils. In these cases he did not fulfil his legal obligation by notifying the opening of transport to the customs office.
The consignor in the Czech Republic can start transport of products entered into free tax circulation in the Czech Republic without the approval of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office in writing before the start of transport.
A tax body collecting products placed in free tax circulation in another Member State is required to report the quantity before collecting them and securing the tax.
Products can only be transported with a simplified accompanying document, the elements of which are governed by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also admits the use of the accompanying document for transport under the suspension scheme, but clearly indicates that it is a ′′ simplified accompanying document for tax inspection (excise products) ".
The same legislation on transport and acceptance of products entered for free tax circulation in another Member State applies in SR.
In these cases, tax entities transported products entered into free tax circulation with an accompanying document for transport under the tax exemption regime, whose 3. and 4. made by the recipient was submitted to the tax administrator in the SR for verification.
The customs authorities in SR registered these transports into the transport database under the tax exemption regime because the accompanying documents did not indicate that it was a simplified accompanying document.
NKÚ SR compared the Czech Customs Transport Database with the Slovak Customs Administration Database and found out:
- in the databases the quantity of products transported were reported in unity, e.g. mineral oil has been shown in liters, hectolitres or kilograms; alcohol was shown in liters or liters of alcohol, thus making it difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported,
- the quantity of alcohol transported in the invoices did not match the quantity registered in the databases,
- all related invoices were not listed in the databases,
- two transports of alcohol from the Czech Republic to SR were registered in the Slovak Customs Administration database, which was not located in the database of Czech customs administration, which was not located in the Czech customs administration database.
The Slovak party handed over copies of accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the SR
Conditions of cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the management of excise duties were adapted until 30. June 2005 by Council Directive 77/799 / EEC on mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxes, certain excise duties and insurance taxes.
On 1. July 2005, Regulation No 2005 entered into force. 2073/2004 laying down rules and procedures to enable the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange information necessary for the correct excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office that secures contacts with other Member States in the field of excise duty management and is responsible for exchange of information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the report ′′ Excise Liaison Office ′′ (hereinafter referred to as ′′ ELO Czech Republic ′′ was set up on DGC to secure exchanges of information in the field of excise duties between Member States of the European Union.
Security of tasks related to the management of systems for control of movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of mutual administrative assistance information between Member States of the European Union and the SR was carried out with effect from 1. May 2004 by ELO customs of the office of Poprad.
With effect from 1. July 2005, the ELO department (based in Poprad) shall carry out the tasks of the ELO department (hereinafter referred to as ′′ ELO SR ′′).
According to Article 3 (3) Article 3 of Regulation No 3 2073/2004 The central contact authority is responsible, in particular, for - exchange of data kept in the SEED electronic register, - early warning system ′′ Early Warning System Excise ′′ (EWSE) - requests for verification of movement of excise goods sent to other Member States or from ′′ Movement Verification System ′′ (hereinafter referred to as ′′ MVS ′′).
The content, scope and function of SEED, EWSE and MVS systems are adapted in Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 24 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for exchange of information on tax entities trading excise goods.
The system consists of national excise tax payer registers and allows tax administrators in the territory of the European Union to determine whether the person is entitled to do so with excise products.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise duty purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State ensures that persons involved in movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information stored in this database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Law No. 98/2004 Z. z., s s 39 of Act No. 104/2004 Z. z., s s 46 of Act No. 105/2004 Z. z., s s 40 of Act No. 106/2004 Z. z. and s § 39 of law no. 107/2004 Z. Z. ELO SR runs an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, eligible beneficiaries and tax warehouses - SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or a beneficiary to SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, a licensed recipient or a tax warehouse is registered into the SysNed database, the related data will automatically be transmitted to SEED database.
NKÚ SR found that the SEED database exchange between the customs administration of the SR and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the controlled period usually once a month, exceptionally several times a month.
Customs administration of SR accepted 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data to the SEED database in the Czech Republic are transmitted from the national registry, where all persons entitled to dispose of excise duty products and licenses issued for the handling of these products.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the SEED international database.
Applications from customs offices for information from the SEED database of other Member States are obtained only through the ELO Czech Republic.
EWSE - Early Warning System aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods through which the transport of risk consignments is carried out.
The transport of certain excise products in quantity exceeding the limits laid down by the European Commission Regulation and, on the one hand, is considered to be a risk consignment.
The exchange of information is made in two forms:
- information - sent when the limits are exceeded,
- warning message - sent if the transport of goods is evaluated as risk.
ELO SR uses SEED database to send a warning message using the SEED database to check the data contained in the accompanying document when evaluating the risk level.
In case the SEED database does not agree with the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the recipient of the goods or the registered office of the consignee), ELO SR shall produce a warning report sent to the ELO Member State of the recipient of the goods.
ELO is governed by CED 317 and CED 457 commissions for tax and customs areas, which define, among other things, the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measure for the preparation of informative and warning reports.
In the controlled period of ELO SR, ELO sent one warning message to the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, information on started transportation of products in excess of the specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when transport approval is approved.
If the tax manager in the Czech Republic evaluates the consignment as a risk based on his own analysis, he will process the so-called. a warning message sent to the relevant Member State via ELO Czech Republic.
In 2005 ELO Czech Republic sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The MVS - the system of control of the movement of goods - enables the individual transportation of excise products and the control of the specified route of transport between the entities listed in the accompanying document via MVS applications.
The exchange of information takes place on request in which ELO specifies its requirements.
The system is used especially when the consignor takes over the confirmed copy No. 3 accompanying document and required for example refund of excise duty and where the data provided in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the controlled period of ELO SR, ELO Czech Republic sent 33 applications to MVS.
ELO Czech Republic sent ELO SR 25 applications from MVS.
Customs offices in the Czech Republic most often examined the data contained in the accompanying documents, especially the amount received or received. the products dispatched or whether the consignor of the products specified in the accompanying document is entitled to deal with excise products, unless this fact could be verified in the SEED international database.
The applications received by MVS were sent to customs offices located in both countries, competent for the recipients or consignors of excise products.
Customs authorities checked the required data and notified the result of the investigation through ELO to the second Member State.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the NKÚ-Czech Republic and the NKÚ SR enabled the basic legislation on excise duties in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the SR in the opening and termination of transport of products under the tax exemption regime between the two states, registration of these transports and further comparing information exchange between customs authorities in international cooperation.
6.1 Differences were found by comparing the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and SR:
(a) in the procedure of tax entities and tax managers when initiating the transport of products under the tax exemption scheme.
Transport of products under the tax exemption regime can be launched by a tax body in the Czech Republic only with the approval of the tax administrator, who will authorise the start of transportation, provided that transported products were provided with a tax security in the amount of tax on them.
Start of transport of products under tax exemption regime in SR shall not be subject to tax manager's permission.
During the controlled period, the tax agency was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the initiation of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
The transport of mineral oils, beer and wine could have started without informing the tax manager.
In 2006, amendment to all excise duty laws were gradually passed in the SR, according to which the consignor of goods under the suspension regime is required to send a copy of copy of copy No before transport started. 1 the accompanying document by electronic or fax to the customs office, which is locally competent to the consignor;
(b) within the time limits for the dispatch of copy No. 3 accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy no later than the following working day after the end of the transport. 3th and 4th accompanying document tax administrators for verification.
Certified copy No. 3 is required to send the consignor no later than the following working day after receiving it from the tax manager.
The consignee in SR is obliged to send copy No to the consignor of the products. 3 confirmed by the tax administrator and the product receiver no later than the 15. th day of the month following the month in which he accepted the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both SR and Czech Republic keep electronic records of transport of products under the tax exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping this evidence is not regulated by legislation in the Czech Republic or in the SR.
Customs authorities in both countries shall register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which transport is carried out.
There is currently no uniform electronic system for monitoring the transport of goods under the tax exemption regime between Member States of the European Union that allows managers of excise duties in individual Member States to obtain information on the transport of goods in real time.
According to Decision 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16. June 2003, the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of excise products is envisaged from 1. July 2009
Based on the cooperation agreement in the control activity, the Czech party handed over to the Slovak party a database of transport of products under a conditional tax exemption regime started in SR and ended in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 items for transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak party handed over to the Czech party a database of transport of products under a tax exemption regime started in the Czech Republic and ended in SR.
The database contained 3 items for transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech party compared the traffic data contained in the registration of initiated transport in the Czech Republic with the transport registration closed in SR.
The Slovak party compared data on transport of goods under the tax exemption regime started in SR and ended in the Czech Republic.
Comparison of data was made difficult by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not uniformly reported in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to unequivocally attribute data on individual transport in both records, the accompanying documents were checked and the violation of the tax exemption regime and the cases of tax evasion were not found.
Based on the knowledge from parallel checks, it can be stated that Member States can obtain valuable information from transport records to improve the management of excise duties.
Establishment of an electronic system for the transport and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No of the European Parliament and of the Council 1152/2003 / EC will allow the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movement under the tax exemption regime in the European Union territory.
Communicating
This report was made in Czech, English and Slovak languages.
The report was signed by the chairman of the Najšie's Supervisory Authority of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Supervisory Authority, the Czech Republic.
Value added tax management in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Introductory word
Taxes are generally a key source of public income.
It is therefore obvious that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAI) should focus their attention on this area.
An example is value added tax fraud (hereinafter also ′′ VAT ′′).
In their case, EUR 100 billion is estimated in the European Union (hereinafter the ′′ EU ′′) each year.
Already in 2005 participants VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
Within this cooperation, SAI can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very appropriate area for control cooperation, since it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Czech Republic's Supreme Supervisory Authority (hereinafter referred to as ′′ NKÚ ′′) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, also ′′ BRH ′′) performed the first parallel VAT control action in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
Since VAT fraud is not limited to a single country, but is expanded across the EU, close cooperation between SAI is required to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to address this problem.
Therefore both SAIs decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a parallel check.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2-2009-0892
Control subject: (CZ) Value added tax management (D) Bilateral audit with NKÚ (follow-up check)
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the control action was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the management of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for solving selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Germany ′′), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the context of international cooperation.
(D) The inspection action was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement recommendations issued by NKÚ and BRH.
The intention was also to cover other VAT related areas.
The resulting inspection findings were intended to compare with the established best practice (if any).
The period controlled was the years 2006 to 2008, in case of factual context and the period preceding and following, until the end of the inspection.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The subsequent VAT management check in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
Suspicious cases of intracommunitary transactions were detected during previous parallel checks.
Some of them requested further clearance.
Based on inspection findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations regarding VAT management.
The subsequent inspection action performed was used to evaluate measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspicious cases.
The inspection further focused e.g. on selected cases of high-risk intracommunitary transactions, mutual assistance in recovery of claims and VAT checks on large tax entities.
During the inspection of VAT management in selected areas in both countries, inspectors have reached the following inspection findings:
1. Recommendations from previous inspection
• Recommendation 1: Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel checks, comparing VAT registration systems in both countries identified differences.
Since various forms of registration cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonizing conditions for registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation was presented at EU level.
Proposal for amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 1798/2003 218/92 (hereinafter referred to as ′′ Council Regulation (EC) No 218/92 1798/2003 ′′) requested the extension of existing databases within the EU, including VAT tax identification numbers database.
He also adjusted common standards for registration and deregistration of tax payers.
SAI expected EU Member States to agree on adequate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of the document agreed by EU Member States within ECOFIN does not contain the issue anymore.
Both SAIs regret to say that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to consider this project a relevant tool for prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly submission of summary reports
In the context of international cooperation, it was recommended in the previous control action that all EU countries should introduce a monthly deadline for submitting summary reports and thus allow for more timely examination of the values of intracommunitary transactions.
Council Directive Article 2008/117 (2008/117) EC amending Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion related to intra-Community transactions reduces the period for summary reports of intra-EU transactions to one a month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1. January 2010, implemented in Germany since July 1., 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to report summary reports monthly was not introduced within the specified deadline in accordance with the applicable EU regulations, while in the Czech Republic did.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports in Germany in order to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of interconnection of both VAT returns systems and summary reports
The German tax administration accepted BRH recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is ongoing and BRH will monitor further developments in detail.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the EU risk management system Based on the results of previous inspection action, both SAI agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system must be exchanged and introduced in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the offenders of fraudulent activity will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The inspection found that our two Member States use different risk management systems that have their advantages and weaknesses.
In this area, the NKA checked the EUROCANET system, which allows information exchange within the EU, while BRH focused on German participation in the so-called. risk management platform.
2. Subsequent inspection of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions
During the previous inspection action, commercial transactions were jointly examined, where there were doubts about their implementation or irregularity in the reporting of commercial transactions in tax returns or summary reports to the tax payer from both countries.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for subsequent inspection, which included intracommunitary movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Checks carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned were not closed on the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
The subsequent inspection action verified that most tax proceedings in connection with the selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany were closed and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT measurements or avoidance of tax refund at the entrance).
3. Checking selected cases of risk intracommunitary transactions
High-risk cases of intracommunitary transactions performed by EU payers, which were included in the EUROCANET system were selected for inspection.
The EUROCANET system is a tool for detecting risk tax payers within the EU.
Member States participation in this system is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in the EUROCANET system, while Germany has passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant of the system if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
Given the fact that the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in the EUROCANET system, it was not possible to obtain any information about which suppliers with German VAT ID were evaluated as hazardous.
The NKÚ identified both cases of normal commercial transactions and cases with suspicion of carousel shops or VAT fraudulent conduct.
Tax administrators have limited options for controlling risk transactions, especially when it comes to so-called. missing traders, with mere physical vetting of documents can hardly prove any fraudulent behavior to the tax body.
A similar situation for tax administrators occurs when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intracommunitary carousel shops.
In such cases it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation and also monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the end consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, hesitates to actively engage in the EUROCANET system because of the absence of sufficient legal base.
In Germany, other tools are being used to detect risk tax payers, which have been proven to the German tax administration until now.
In this field it is necessary to communicate and exchange experience among EU Member States.
The EU Council has reached political agreement on the proposal for a regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
Experience gained so far using the EUROCANET system should be the basis for creating this new VAT fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance in recovery of claims
In the field of international aid in the recovery of claims, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international aid in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
NKÚ and BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs find it useful to renegotiate at EU level to find a way to avoid persistent inconsistencies.
Without this statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAI agrees that reliable statistics should include more information about VAT.
It would probably be helpful if the Commission, based on more detailed statistics, was to process analysis to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
According to both SAIs, this means assistance for Member States with low enforcement success rate to increase the level of recovery to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
SAI analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control for large tax entities (hereinafter also ′′ VDS ′′) in both countries.
In addition, they collected information from tax administrators on areas that SAI consider essential to the management of the issue.
The answers received clearly indicate that the situation in both countries develops differently.
The Czech Republic has a system based on a large volume of relevant data to direct the selection of cases with a tendency to risk (e.g. information from tax checks carried out, balance sheet data and profit and loss statements etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT checks in general.
The establishment of a specialised VDS finance office is planned in 2012
There is no similar system in Germany yet, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT checks in general.
Germany has so far more focused on the selection of individual cases in question, especially based on VAT tax return data and summary report.
Analysis of this data relies on various components of risk management that will be strengthened.
3. The course of the inspection action
3.1 The course of a control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by Unit II.-by the department of state budget revenue and territorial unions IX. Pilsen, X. České Budějovice, XIII Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The controlled persons were: Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter the ′′ Czech Ministry of Finance ′′) and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter ′′ FÚ ′′): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ in Breclav, FÚ in Domažlicích, FÚ in Hodonin, FÚ in Hradec Králové, FÚ in Cheb, FÚ in Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ in Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Kralupy nad Vltavou, FÚ in Kraslice, FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ Ostrava III, FÚ in Písek, FÚ in Pilsen, FÚ for Prague 1, FÚ for Prague 4, FÚ for Prague 8, 8, in Rakovník, FÚ in Sokolov, FÚ in Tábor, FÚ in Vysokém Myto, FÚ in Zlín and FÚ in Žamberku.
The College of the Supreme Supervisory Authority approved the inspection conclusion of this inspection action on April 27., 2010.
3.2 The course of inspection action in Germany
The inspection was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the inspection unit for indirect taxes and personnel of designated regional inspection authorities in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of case samples, many spolkových were notified of the mission of the control action.
In addition to interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, there were control events in the following spolkových: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hessen, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
Tax files of the following financial authorities were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Financial Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, there was a discussion with the financial authorities of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-south) and the financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münsteru.
The report on inspection findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation of both control institutions
The preparation of parallel control actions took place in September 2008 to discuss and identify control topics.
After December 2008, the top leaders of both SAI signed a cooperation agreement in the implementation of parallel checks.
At the Bonn meeting in June 2009, the control teams informed each other about the initial results achieved during the preparation of the inspection, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed next procedure together.
The second meeting took place in Prague from 2. to 4. December 2009.
The control teams have swapped findings together until then and agreed a timetable for compiling a joint report.
Both SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of recommendations made in previous report zprávě verification of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not resolved during previous parallel inspection, • verification of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, which have been classified as high risk cases, • control of the tax administration's procedure in international assistance for the recovery of VAT claims, • tax checks on large companies.
The report on the results of parallel control events was drawn up during the June 2010. work meeting.
4. VAT management check in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from previous inspection
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
Based on the results of the previous inspection action, NKÚ recommended adjusting the conditions of VAT registration and introducing a new rule for cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
Modified conditions should allow more effectively to reduce the risk of possible tax evasion with VAT collection.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the financial authorities did not use the authorization to revoke VAT registration for payers who did not fulfil their obligations under Law No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax (hereinafter referred to as the 'VAT Act').
The amendment of the provision consisting of the introduction of the duty of tax administrators to abolish VAT registration for payers during the repeated non-filing of VAT tax return has not yet been proposed by the Czech Ministry of Finance.
According to the VAT Act, the tax manager can revoke the registration of the tax payer 'ex offo' in cases where: (a) the payer has failed to carry out the tax administrator without notification of the reason for the tax administrator for consecutive months of transactions, (b) the payer does not fulfil his obligations under this law, c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous inspection action, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the FÚ for Prague 1 to cancel VAT registration on 31. January of the following calendar year called. non-established payers who were not incurred during the current calendar year no obligation to admit and pay tax.
FÚ for Prague 1 often did not cancel VAT registration for these payers, because the relevant provision provided for the cancellation of registration insufficient time limit.
This issue has been remedied by the amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to revoke the registration of a non-established tax payer in case the tax payer has not supplied any taxable goods or services in the previous calendar year or goods or services exempted from taxation with the right to deduct VAT.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
As part of international cooperation, it was recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for summary reporting.
The Council Directive reduces the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2010.
Newly, the obligation to report summary reports in electronic form is also established.
The summary report must be submitted to the payer even if there are services for which the place of delivery is determined in accordance with Section 9 (9). Article 1 (1) of the VAT Act, provided to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State and if he is liable to admit and pay tax to their recipient on such services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8 / EC amending Directive No 2008/8 2006/112 / EC as regards the place of service.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of VAT returns and summary reports to achieve greater reliability of VIES data This recommendation was related to the German tax administration.
The Czech administration conducts a comparison of data on intracommunitary transactions reported in VAT tax returns and summary reports of Czech payers automatically in ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper VAT collection is one of the necessary preconditions for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore one of the areas of priority interest and has been given considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is testified, among others. the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, where the external evaluator tried to determine the difference between the legitimate and actually collected VAT amount in 25 EU Member States (hereinafter referred to as ′′ EU-25 ′′) during the period 2000-2006.
Based on the analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated amount of loss from unpaid VAT for this period is EUR 90 billion, with on average 12 % of the eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25 I'm sorry.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18 %.
In the context of international cooperation, it was stated in the previous control action that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and introduced in every EU Member State.
Regarding the risk management system, NKÚ has carried out a check on the EUROCANET system for information exchange in the EU.
Cases of risk intracommunitary transactions carried out by EU tax payers, included in the EUROCANET system have been selected for inspection (see Chapter 4.3).
The aims of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved by the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of responsible authorities into a form enabling fraud to be detected already in their bud.
This network should later become an important source of information when assessing intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7. October 200812, while setting out the basic principles to follow this network.
The preview of EUROFISC is an already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information EUROCANET developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risk trading transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendation from the first report brought the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration has established a well functioning tax payer registration system based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance alerted the Commission in October 2007.
Improvement of the system is done continuously.
Currently data from the questionnaire are being processed electronically and will then serve as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission has submitted a proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for tax payers registration and deregistration.
Member States requested further clarification and detailed development of the issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to secure the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
On April 8., 2010, a law on transposition of EU directives into national law was passed.
This law contains clauses on monthly submission of summary reports on intracommunitary delivery.
Those provisions took effect on 1. July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of the interconnection of both VAT returns and summary reports
A joint working group consisting of workers from the spolkových and the Federal Ministry of Finance was established.
The group developed a strategy for automatic comparison of VAT tax returns data and summary reports.
This strategy is still being discussed in the spolkových.
The working group also dealt with a tool designed to optimise the control procedure for internal market transactions.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level Exchange of relevant information at EU level.
Germany participates in this exchange within the so-called. risk management platforms.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and based on a written consultation of 18. October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007. action plan.
Members of the platform are further divided into subgroups that deal with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • acting influence, • evaluation, • risk management update.
At the beginning of 2010 reports were published on the results of the activities of these subgroups.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of conditions for VAT registration and cancellation of this registration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
Proposal for amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing EU databases, including VAT identification numbers database.
He also adjusted common minimum standards for tax payers registration and deregistration.
The issue of registration and cancellation of registration has been left to the national legislation of EU Member States for now.
Member States requested further clarification and detailed development of the issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already reached in Germany does not fall.
On 8. June 2010 the ECOFIN Council reached political agreement on the proposed regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
