Member States need to implement national procedures and are only required to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee of these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission failed to convince Member States of the necessity of common standards for registering and deregistration of payers, because both SAI consider this measure an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome the Commission to make further efforts in this direction.
Monthly submission of summary reports
In the context of international cooperation, it was recommended that all EU states introduce a monthly deadline for summary reports, allowing more timely examination of the values of intracommunitary transactions.
Council Directive Article 2008/117 (2008/117) EC amending Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion related to intra-Community transactions reduces the period for summary reports of intra-EU transactions to one a month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2010, Germany took effect on July 1., 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to report summary monthly reports according to the specified calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports in Germany to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and to consider interconnection of both VAT returns systems and summary reports
The German tax administration accepted BRH recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is ongoing so far and BRH will monitor further developments in detail.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of detecting risk-inclined traders.
NKÚ has carried out a check on the EUROCANET system for information exchange in the EU (see drip. 4.3).
BRH focused on German participation in the so-called in this area. risk management platform.
4.2 Subsequent inspection of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions
In the previous inspection action, the implementation of commercial transactions was jointly examined, where there were doubts about their implementation, or. irregularities in the way payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their tax returns to VAT or summary reports.
Both inspection institutions selected nine cases involving the intracommunitary movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany for subsequent inspection by tax administrations of both countries were not completed during the previous joint control action.
1)
The Czech payer bought goods worth EUR 22 686 from a German payer in the 1. th quarter of 2005
This acquisition of goods by the Czech payer in his tax return to VAT, because the German payer did not have VAT ID assigned, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
Based on international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No On 798/2003 July 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that under the German VAT law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to have VAT ID assigned to intracommunitary supply of goods exempted from VAT.
Follow-up inspection of the NKÚ found that, based on a check carried out by the Czech tax manager, the Czech tax payer filed an additional VAT return, admitting the acquisition of goods at the said value and at the same time in this tax return, he claimed the right to deduct VAT of the same amount.
2)
The Czech payer was supposed to buy EUR 12 561 from the German payer.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of these goods and did not mention VAT in his tax return.
The German tax administration refused upon request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 cooperation as the turnover of transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000
Since the Czech tax manager did not obtain evidence, he ended the check without finding and the tax liability remained at the original amount.
Following a follow-up inspection of the NKÚ found that the Czech tax manager received two spontaneous information from Germany under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer bought goods from a Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in a proper VAT return for October 2004.
3)
The Czech payer was supposed to buy a car from a German payer in the 4. th quarter of 2004 CZK.
The Czech tax payer did not admit the acquisition of the goods in question.
This payer has not submitted tax returns to VAT since August 2004, so the tax manager measured VAT of CZK 0 for that quarter.
Based on information received in the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No In March 2007, 1798/2003 from Germany, the tax administrator called on the payer to submit an additional tax return to VAT, which the payer did not submit.
Follow-up inspection found that the tax administrator carried out further tax procedures in 2007, which showed that the car in question sold to the Czech payer to the Czech payer.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment for the tax period December 2004, which he additional paid VAT for the acquisition of goods from another Member State and subsequent sale of CZK 295
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was cancelled with liquidation and a liquidator was established.
In the absence of foreclosures of the tax borrower's property, this outstanding balance appears impregnable.
4)
The Czech payer was supposed to deliver new means of transport (cars) to Germany during the 4. th quarter of 2004 and the 1. th quarter of 2005 totalling EUR 198 167
From reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 it appeared that there is an unfinished tax-criminal proceedings against the German entity in Germany.
Following a follow-up check, BRH received information that after the end of the tax proceeding in Germany, it was demonstrable to find that the German tax payer was incorporated into fraudulent activities.
Intracommunitary acquisition of goods was taxed EUR 182 424 (year 2004) and EUR 369 690 (year 2005).
NKÚ found out by subsequent inspection that the Czech payer was involved in carousel shops with new means of transport.
Based on information from the German tax administration regarding the verification of delivery of goods, VAT was started with the Czech tax agency for the tax period April, May and June 2005.
Based on the inspection findings and information collected in the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additional VAT for the period May 2005, 031 CZK and 703 CZK for the period June 2005
5)
Czech payer A was supposed to buy a machine totaling EUR 58 000 from a German payer in February 2005
This German payer was supposed to supply the Czech payer B with a machine worth EUR 88 027 in the 3. st quarter of 2004, but the payer B denied this acquisition.
Subsequent inspection of the NKÚ found that payer B bought a machine from a German company that had an organisational component established in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not show the acquisition of goods from a German payer in his VAT tax return.
From a German tax manager's response to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 it appeared that the German payer did not carry out an intracommunitary delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000, but the supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
BRH found after the tax inspection that after the tax check was carried out, the intracommunitary supply of the machine was reclassified to supply the machine in the country and the VAT exemption was abolished.
6)
The German tax payer was supposed to supply the Czech payer with EUR 11 600 in the 3. th quarter of 2004
The goods were bought and sold in Germany in 2005
The NKÚ subsequent inspection found that the Czech tax administrator measured the additional tax return for VAT filed, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State was wrongly stated, including the acquisition of goods at the said value.
BRH found that after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No On 1798/2003 July 1798/2003, the German tax administrator corrected the tax return for the German payer's VAT and additional EUR 1 600
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany is subject to tax control.
The summary report of the German payer has not yet been corrected, because repairs of summary reports in Germany can only be made by the payer who submitted the summary report.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request for information from the German tax administration under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 whether the Czech tax payer bought a car from a German payer in February 2005, worth EUR 47 400
The Czech tax administrator, after the tax procedure carried out for the tax period February 2005, measured the Czech tax payer's tax liability of CZK 0 and told the German tax manager that he cannot confirm the acquisition of the car by a Czech payer.
Subsequent inspection of the NKÚ found that registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for failure to comply with duties and the Czech tax manager sent documents to the police of the Czech Republic.
Following the check of BRH, he found that the German payer changed his seat and the new local tax manager cancelled the VAT exemption on the delivery of the vehicle to the Czech payer on the basis of the inspection carried out.
The German tax payer has not yet corrected the data in the summary report and filed an appeal against the tax manager's decision.
8)
According to VIES data, the German taxpayer supplied goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the 1. th quarter of 2005 according to data from the VIES system.
Subsequent inspection of the NKÚ found that the Czech tax manager was trying to identify the causes of differences caused by the Czech tax payer when acquiring goods between the 3. th quarter of 2004 and the 1. th quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax payer repeatedly submitted additional tax return to VAT for the 1. st quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not explain the difference in the value of the goods purchased between CZK 134 and 273 for the period of the 3. th quarter of 2004, because according to the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture the commercial transactions for individual quarter and therefore the tax manager accepted additional tax returns.
9)
The German tax payer supplied the Czech payer with EUR 46 854 in the 3. st quarter of 2004
The Czech payer admitted only EUR 14 856 intracommunitary acquisition of goods in the same period.
Czech tax administrator verified the amount of deliveries made in the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total value of the supply of goods EUR 31 998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT tax return and the data given in VIES I'm sorry.
Follow-up inspection of the NKÚ found that the Czech payer filed additional tax return to VAT for the July 2004 to January 2007. after many urgences.
In this tax return, the tax payer also claimed the right to deduct VAT, thus the tax liability for the said tax period remained unchanged.
The subsequent inspection verified that most tax proceedings were completed in selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany and that tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Germany took adequate measures (i.e. additional VAT or prevented tax refund on entry).
4.3 Checking selected cases of risk intracommunitary transactions
4.3.1 Results of inspection in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET may be an important source of information for the detection of risk entities within the Member State where goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from the EUROCANET system was compared by the local financial authorities with customer data.
Starting in the 1. th quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic sends data on risk transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers into the EUROCANET system.
Nine Czech tax entities included EUROCANET were selected for inspection as part of international cooperation.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as buyers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrators from other Member States were captured in EUROCANET.
Since the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in the EUROCANET system, no information could be obtained to help determine whether suppliers with German VAT ID were evaluated by the German tax administration as risk entities.
The control action revealed cases of normal commercial transactions and cases with suspicion of involvement in carousel shops or VAT fraudulent conduct.
Where relevant, tax administrators benefited from exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax administrators did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risk transactions when verifying signal information.
The financial authorities monitor such tax entities on a continuous basis for their inclusion in the EUROCANET system.
• During the verification of risk transactions, the financial authorities did not demonstrate in the submitted accounting records derogations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT, despite finding irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or reveal trade relations with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• Verification of business transactions was complicated because some tax payers did not cooperate with tax administrators and could not be contacted.
Locally competent financial authorities mostly checked the risk tax entities and risk transactions specified in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax administrators when checking risk transactions, especially in connection with the so-called verification. missing traders, they have limited options and only from physical document control it is difficult to prove fraudulent behavior to the tax body.
Stronger requirements for registration of VAT payers and more flexible cancellation of registration would help reduce missing trader scams.
For tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered for the purpose of reporting fictitious supply of goods within the EU or for the purpose of issuing formal tax documents to payers, who illegally draw VAT deductions on entry due to them.
In cases where tax entities are suspected to involve in carousel shops and other fraud and imports and exports of goods from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation of these institutions would help in identifying goods and irregularities in transport documentation and monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in the EUROCANET system is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in the operation of the EUROCANET system, the European Parliament evaluated at the end of 2008 as a weakness of this system, which should be eliminated by the establishment of a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the inspection in Germany
BRH analysed information available with the Federal Central Financial Authority, which contained data from the EUROCANET system.
These data were the criteria for selecting six German tax payers files for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, refused to actively participate in the EUROCANET system.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means it does not send data to Brussels, but is only a recipient of data from the EUROCANET system.
The justification of this position is contained in the following statement :. in the opinion of the government, it is not legally admissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to the EUROCANET system.
Currently there is no legal base that would allow tax information to be violated.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such data are used by other Member States within EUROCANET." 17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has been analyzing data from the EUROCANET system and advancing it to the finančním's financial authorities in compliance with the agreed procedure.
German financial authorities receive control information on the direct trade relations of payers (registered with specific financial authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in the EUROCANET scheme.
However, German financial authorities do not receive any information about whether such a trader from another Member State has any risk trading relations with traders from other Member States who also maintain trade relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in the EUROCANET system, while Germany has passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse active participation.
As a result of this fact, the control in a given area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal big differences in VAT fraud detection, since the EUROCANET system is not the only systemic risk management tool.
Tax administrations of both countries have many other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to create a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The EU Council has reached a political agreement on the proposal for a regulation, whose main contribution is to the establishment of the EUROFISC network.
Experience gained from the use of data from the EUROCANET system should become part of the expected VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experience at European level.
On the other hand, cases presented to courts at national and European level show that discussion between Member States and the Commission is probably necessary about the conditions of tax exemptions in intracommunitary transactions.
4.4 Mutual assistance in recovery of claims
4.4.1 International assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives are the basic regulation of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive No 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims arising from operations which are part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive No 2001/44 / EC amending Directive No 2001/44 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims arising from operations which form part of the system for financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94 / EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive No 2002/94 / EC 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims resulting from certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic there was Council Directive No. 76/308 / EEC implemented by law no. 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44 / EC it was necessary to implement this directive into the Czech law and at the same time amendment of the said law No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context a new law no has been adopted 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
The new regulation in the system of adaptation of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28. 2008.
The Annex to the Regulation sets out new models of applications, which have been used since 1. 1. 2009, the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the requesting authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guidelines for international cooperation in recovery of claims:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always provided only on request containing the prescribed elements;
3. aid does not apply to financial claims that are in the requested State of criminal penalties;
4. in the provision of international assistance for the recovery of claims shall be followed by the national law of the country which was asked for assistance;
5. foreign claims do not have a priority in enforcement;
6. assistance is provided only for the recovery of undisputed claims;
7. principle of exhaustion (the requesting state without success used all the applicable option to recover the claim given by its legal order).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines three forms of assistance, namely the provision of information, the delivery of documents and self-recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending claims to other EU Member States
Local competent tax authority electronic sends a request for information, a request for delivery or a request for recovery of claims together with relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance via the Financial Directorate.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will arrange a translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it including attachments and sends to the competent tax administration of the designated state via the CCN / CSI network.
Two essential requirements apply to enforcement: the claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse the enforcement.
Procedure for receiving claims from other EU Member States
When receiving an application from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm the receipt of the application as soon as possible, within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the application, it shall inform the applicant authority of the reasons for rejecting the application and shall indicate the specific provisions of the directive it relies upon.
This communication must be sent no later than three months after the date of receipt of the application.
After accepting the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify whether the application has all the elements under the law and should immediately transmit the application to the local financial authority for processing through the financial directorate.
If the application for recovery is accepted, tax administrator among others find out the debtor's property, e.g. acquiring real estate cadastral extracts, checking accounts in banks, verifying vehicle registration at the DMV etc.
The Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the applicant authority of the outcome of the investigation carried out to obtain the information requested.
In the case of non-contact tax entities, when the claim is not possible, the requesting authority should also be informed of this fact.
Any amount recovered by the tax manager shall be transferred to the requesting authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that the Czech tax administrator enforcing foreign claims allow waiting for payment or payment in instalments if the state that asked for enforcement agrees with it.
During the period of enforcement the debtor is prescribed interest or penalty payment under law No. 337/1992 Coll., about tax management and fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the state that applied for the enforcement.
In the case of applications received for enforcement, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not forward local tax administrators applications for processing in a timely manner, especially in 2006 and 2007.
Similar situation was found in international aid in recovery of claims and in case of applications received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The control action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with law No. 191/2004 Coll., because the local competent authority of the Member State did not inform the progress made in enforcement within six months of the date of receipt of the application was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008
Statistical data
Czech Ministry of Finance in accordance with the provisions of Paragraph 13 (13). Article 4 of Law No. 191/2004 Coll. process statistical data for the European Commission by 15. March each year, indicating the number of requests for information, receipt or recovery, sent or received in the previous year, indicating the amount of claims covered by the application.
The European Commission shall process the report on the state of recovery of claims submitted to the EU Council and the European Parliament based on the documents provided by all EU Member States.
The inspection found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated statistics due to an error in the asset item in 2008 by 250 5 thousand. EUR, by indicating the incorrect value of the enforced VAT claim (it was a shift of the decimal point after the conversion of the claim from Czech crowns to the value in euro).
This error was subsequently reflected in European Commission statistics.
Information on mutual assistance including amounts recovered is given in the table below.
4.4.2 International aid in recovery of claims in Germany
Legal authorization for international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from European Community law, Council Directive Commission Regulation of 2008/55 November 2008 (ECR) and Commission Regulation of 28. November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In the interests of more accessible wording and better clarity, the EC directive on the recovery of claims codifies Council Directive No 76/308 / EEC of 15. March 197621, whose provisions have been substantially modified several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia. for VAT recovery, income tax and capital income tax, including accessories.
The EC directive on recovery of claims was transposed into German national law by law (EC) on the collection of state taxes of 3. May 2003.
The enforcement procedure in Germany follows the German fiscal code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities can provide international judicial and administrative assistance based on international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities valid in national jurisdiction and under the EC Administrative Assistance Act.
Part six of the German fiscal code (Articles 249-346) enshrines statutory provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
Administrative operations of the financial authorities follow in particular instructions for execution and enforcement instructions.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with representatives of the nejvyšších's highest tax authorities regarding the principles of administrative assistance in taxation, and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general preconditions for submitting claims for recovery are as follows:
• Legal requirements must be fulfilled (§ 251 and § 254 of the German fiscal code [AO]).
• All available domestic enforcement resources have already been exhausted.
• The claims subject to applications for enforcement assistance must be final.
• From issuing an enforcement order or date when the claim will gain power (i.e. is no longer subject to impeachment), more than 5 years must be allowed to submit applications.
• The total amount of the claim must exceed EUR 1 500
Procedure for sending claims to other EU Member States
German requests for enforcement of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementation departments of the financial authorities to the competent foreign office, for example the Czech CLO, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
A closer procedure follows the Methodical Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Affairs (Recovery of claims) of 19. January 2004.25 The Working Group of the Federal Government and Land Governments is reviewing this methodological order to adapt it to the directive on debt recovery.
The application including attachments shall be submitted by the tax authority to the electronic intermediary office.
This office will check the accuracy of the application on the content and form page.
If the application is not correct, it shall be returned to the competent financial authority.
If it meets all the elements, it is forwarded to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central IRS will then secure the necessary communication with the competent foreign authority and will also ensure the translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving claims from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and will send a certificate of receipt within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check whether the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these applications to the intermediary office, which further advances them to the competent financial authorities and monitors their processing.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the application lasts longer than 6 months, the intermediary office shall invite the intermediate authority to submit a preliminary report to be submitted under Article 16 of Commission Directive No. 2002/94 / DG.
Following inspection of the formal and factual requirements of the application, the implementation departments shall notify the method of enforcement.
All amounts recovered must be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of receipt.
Statistical data

4.4.3 Check of recovery of claims, case studies
As part of international cooperation, 21 applications for international assistance for recovery of claims between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for inspection.
The examination of ten selected cases was among others. found:
1.
On 20. June 10., the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for VAT claim for 2004 and 2005 totaling EUR 3 883, i.e. 109 820 CZK, with a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for enforcement to the tax administrator until 2. 26. 2008.
In order to secure the recovery of the claim, the Czech tax manager established a lien to real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire recovery claim by stopping the real estate, a repayment calendar with installments of mines was agreed with the Czech tax agency. CZK 2 per month.
On June 31., 2009, German tax administration was sent information on the state of recovery, saying that on 25. 8. 2009 the claim was partly recovered in instalments of CZK 49 I'm sorry.
This amount was sent to Germany and another installment of CZK 3 was sent to Germany on 28. August 8.
2.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received an application on 7. June 1. for the recovery of tax arrears of the Czech tax body, which owed EUR 180 869 in Germany, i.e. 4 915 434 CZK, VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent an application to the tax manager until 11. 27. 2008.
The tax administrator found that the debtor does not own any executable property by checking accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movable goods.
Furthermore, local investigation found that the borrower has not been held for nearly a year at the address of his permanent residence.
His place of residence in the Czech Republic is unknown.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received this communication on 6. 4. 2009 and on 16. 4. 2009 the tax administrator's response was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany on 21. July 11. for enforcement regarding tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech tax body amounting to EUR 3 139, i.e. 84 846 CZK.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent an application for the recovery of this claim on 6. 8. 2008 to the tax administrators, even though the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany on 2. 18. 2008 that the Czech tax entity paid the claim in Germany I'm sorry.
The Czech Ministry of Finance announced on June 9., 2008 to the tax administrator that the application for recovery is handled by the payment of the claim by the Czech tax body in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the context of enforcement in the Czech Republic and pointed out to Germany on 27. 10. 2008.
Due to the long time limits in which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the delegated tax administrators, the claim was paid twice - by the company itself in Germany and the recovery of the claim by the Czech tax manager.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount raised from the Czech Republic should have been added to the claim from another application for recovery of EUR 6 649, which was due to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance records only a request for recovery of EUR 3 139 for this company, an application for recovery of EUR 6 649 is not available in the Czech Ministry of Finance with the company concerned.
4.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received an application from Germany for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax body owed in Germany for income tax and VAT tax and accessories amounting to EUR 39 957, i.e. 956 654 CZK.
On June 19., 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax manager.
The recovery procedure started on June 1., 2009, an execution was ordered on the commandment of the claim on banks in the Czech Republic and wage collision (the collision amounted to CZK 7).
When dealing with the tax manager, the debtor stated that he disagrees with the amount of the claim and considers it disputed.
The Czech tax manager found that the tax operator was willing to pay EUR 250 per month in the past, which was not accepted by the German tax manager.
The tax body promised to discuss the application with the German tax manager in order to change its claim.
The recovery of the claim during the NKÚ control action was still ongoing.

August 2008, because it was not possible to identify a local administrator based on the said address of the tax agency taxes.

The German tax administration thus considered the application for enforcement to be done.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the field of international aid in the recovery of claims, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international aid in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
NKÚ and BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In the 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay increased attention to the management of their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of inconsistencies in statistics decreased despite the increase in the number of applications.
Both SAIs consider it important that statistics are renegotiated at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent inconsistencies, otherwise the data reported by individual EU states will not be reliable and comparable in statistics.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics should report an annual number of applications and the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax etc.) also amounts of claims received by individual Member States.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of statistics submitted by Member States, as this may help Member States to assess their own effectiveness in the fight against VAT fraud.
The fact that it is possible to calculate the level of recovery of claims broken down into individual Member States, both SAIs find it useful to intensify their efforts and to improve the level of recovery of claims at least to the EU average level.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
Especially in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit to local tax administrators applications for recovery of claims on time.
Similar situation was found in applications for international assistance received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The control action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with law No. 191/2004 Coll., on international aid in recovery of claims because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State about the progress made in recovery within six months of the date of receipt of the application.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
Procedure for the inspection of VDS is based on law No. 337/1992 Coll., about tax management and fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined the VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or established for business and whose net turnover for the tax period specified in the tax return of natural / legal persons amounted to 2 billion. CZK or higher.
The inclusion of the tax entity among the VDS was submitted after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant taxation period, for the first time in 2003.
The tax entity ceased to be referred to as the VDS if, in three consecutive tax periods since the end of the period when it filed the tax return based on which it was placed among the VDS, its net turnover over the tax period fell below that threshold.
The tax body was not allowed to be excluded from the VDS record without carrying out a tax check of at least one tax for one tax period.
All VDS were checked in at least five-year periodicity by the end of 2009
Since 2010, at least once every 2 years a written assessment of the tax body must be carried out and the subsequent procedure chosen must eliminate tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The Kontrola control focuses on at least one type of tax; the tax manager usually chooses several tax periods at once.
VDS were controlled by specialized inspection departments, which are set up in total for 13 FÚ or by inspection staff of local competent FÚ
The department of specialised inspections shall carry out tax checks within the scope established by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific business fields;
• entities for which tax inspection is professionally and time consuming;
• entities with branched territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of extensive tax evasion;
• entities linked in chains and networks suspected of extensive tax evasion and unauthorized attraction of excessive deductions.
The number of tax checks carried out by departments of specialised specializovaných checks and the results of these checks are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed amendment to law No. 531/1990 Coll., about territorial financial institutions, which consists of establishing a specialised FÚ with national scope for selected tax entities (among others) for business-based legal entities that have reached a turnover of more than 2 billion. CZK).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT checks for large companies follow the same rules as tax checks in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following rules: • German fiscal code (AO), • Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are in effect.
German fiscal code
The statutory rules on control are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German fiscal code in Section IV - On-the-spot Tax check. In particular, these articles enshrine rules of admissibility of on-the-spot tax checks (i.e. in the premises of the undertaking), their scope by the subject line, rules on the distribution of responsibilities, form and content of the inspection notification, the principle of control, the tax body's obligation to cooperate and the preconditions for the implementation of the final examination and the communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax checks are carried out by responsible financial authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Act on fiscal administration According to Article 5.1 (1) in custody of Article 5.1 (1) Article 19 of the law is the participation in on-the-spot tax checks carried out by the financial authorities for the Federal Central Financial Office.
The participating authorities will agree together on the spot the nature and extent of the participation of the Federal Central Tax Office in tax checks.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to demand that the specific businesses it select be controlled at the time it determines.
In such a case he may declare rules on the execution and content of the inspection at the premises of these companies.
The rules on tax checks According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the rules on tax checks (German shortcut BpO 2000) were approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper chamber of the German parliament, where the governments of the spolkových are represented).
These administrative regulations apply to on-the-spot inspections carried out by the financial authorities of the spolkových and the Federal Central Tax Office.
Enterprises are classified according to size at regular intervals in accordance with Article 3 BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to follow-up (Article 4.2 BpO).
According to Article 33.1 BpO 2000, every informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in BpO 2000.
Methodical instructions
In addition to the above, it provides additional methodology for tax administration as follows:
• Uniform manual for special VAT checks in Germany;
• a USLO manual that sets out methodology for the use of data on intracommunitary business relationships led by VIES;
• ZAUBER manual, which sets out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits according to business type.
The Federal Ministry of Finance publishes the data.
They are always evaluated in three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to check - not only big companies - must be set at regular inspection intervals.
In general, checks on large enterprises are carried out on a continuous basis.
Checks are usually announced including VAT checks.
This means that during the inspection the checks will be finalised mainly in income taxes, excise duties and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks can be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisational arrangement of the spolkových.
The number of tax seasons covered by checks usually ranges between three and five years.
BpO 2000 forecast a three-year inspection period.
The subject of the examination is all taxes given to the company.
4.5.3 Management of control of large tax agencies
Both SAIs decided not to check individual cases of VDS checks carried out, but focused on management issues to gain insight into how tax administrations manage VAT checks at VDS.
Through a questionnaire, they collected information from tax administrators on areas they consider essential for managing the issue.
• What statistical records and analyses regarding VAT control with VDS does tax administration have available?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or record rates whereby differentiates between fighting against VAT fraud and generally VAT control?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such distinction with the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and general VAT control.
• Are there any statistics or timeliness of VAT checks (in custody for the time period of controlled transactions)?
Czech Republic: Registration of timeliness of inquiry with relevance for intracommunitary acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers is shown in ADIS system.
In addition, information registered in ADIS is also part of the type of information, how long the questioning took.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors contain only information about the average time of the last inspection (year information).
This data does not provide an overview of selected inspection periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the latest period of tax measurement; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, statistics created at the Federal level for special VAT inspection services do not provide information regarding the classification of tax entities.
• Are there any statistics or records on the nature of additional tax revenue generated, broken down for example according to the following criteria:
i. net tax increase (e.g. in cases where the tax body unduly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only nominal tax increase (eg transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
iii. additional tax revenue collection (payment due additional tax payable).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications performed, the volume of additional tax collected broken down by type of tax, according to the number of tax agencies controlled and according to the number of tax periods checked.
Other tax procedures (local investigation, accusation proceedings) are followed in the same way.
Time stamps and amounts of additional tax paid are registered as a separate task.
Statistics of general debt broken down by type of tax, but not by declared tax or tax found by the tax manager.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not distinguish between the above criteria.
In addition, these differences are not distinguished by most tax administrations visited.
• Are there areas of control that generate high additional revenue?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to collect tax payer for verification based on criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at the Federal level.
This follows that uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach of the Ministers of Finance of the spolkových and the Federal Government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the spolkových must register an increased tax (VAT) requirement if they exceed a certain amount.
In this case they must specify for example the nature of the measured tax increase.
• What findings are the most common?
Czech Republic:
- VDS claim unauthorized right to deduct tax on entry for supplies and services:
• which were not used to carry out any economic activity under Paragraph 72 (72) of the basic Regulation. 1 VAT Act;
• which were used for representation under Section 75 (75). 3 VAT Act;
• based on tax documents that did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73 (73). 1 VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare VAT on output according to Section 21 (21). 1 VAT Act.
Germany: It has been stated that there are no rules at the Federal level.
This follows that uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not provide such data.
VAT findings are not independently registered by the spolkovými if they result from VDS tax checks.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the spolkových must write the increased tax (VAT) requirement, if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Authority is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration analyse the areas of control from which high ′′ yields ′′ and produces consequences for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they start national audits focused on risk commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at the Federal level.
Uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection departments do not provide data on the audit areas from which high ′′ revenue ".
There are various opinions on the analysis process, as well as on case management in terms of importance.
Some regional financial authorities provide special information, but its use is on the own account of the financial authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
Differences in the replies of both Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a lot of data from tax checks carried out and data from accounts - balance sheet and profit and loss accounts.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to direct the selection of cases with risk inclined.
The same applies to VAT analysis and management in general.
In 2012, the Czech Republic is planned to set up a specialised VDS management financial authority.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
This shows that it is more difficult to perform these tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places greater emphasis on choosing individual cases based on data from submitted tax returns.
Risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
Based on adequate reference comments, expert auditors must be able to calculate the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to provide adequate financial management and adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce VAT income outages.
The result will increase VAT revenue and the risk detection rate for unreliable entrepreneurs will improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of both SAIs on parallel VAT management checks met the goals set by NKÚ and BRH.
Both SAIs have better recognized each other's valid systems in the following areas: • intracommunitary transactions, • VAT risk management, especially regarding the selection of risk-inclined transactions, • VAT recovery assistance and a VAT control for large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud cases and differences in the above mentioned VAT management areas in the Czech Republic and Germany were revealed.
Check findings were compared and best practices were identified based on them.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will become an impetus for stakeholders to start discussions on approaches and strategies within Member States, among them and at European Commission level.
Extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of both SAIs can serve as an encouragement to carry out future VAT control actions.
6. Komuniké
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Supervisory Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Edition deadline: June 2010.
